load balancing like an <strong>airport</strong> ‚úàÔ∏è:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-8730-e203eb1953b2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>ClusterIP</strong> = Gate assignment (distributes passengers across planes).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-9193-e0c5cdb47c5e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>NodePort/LoadBalancer</strong> = Airport entrances (ways for outsiders to enter).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-9e4e-c636e68ce082" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Ingress</strong> = Immigration/customs desk (decides where each passenger should go based on rules).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8012-8395-f5a34f03842f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8014-bebf-c325485ff20a" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-b5ae-fd8715be4aa2" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles load balancing by using Services (ClusterIP for internal traffic, NodePort/LoadBalancer for external traffic) and Ingress Controllers for HTTP/HTTPS routing, with kube-proxy managing traffic distribution across Pods.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-9793-cc754d45528e" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 14:</strong> What is the purpose of the kubelet in a Kubernetes cluster?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8018-9a14-c863a5d961ae" class=""><strong>Purpose of the kubelet in a Kubernetes Cluster</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-acf3-e87b42c1cb1d" class="">The <strong>kubelet</strong> is an <strong>agent</strong> that runs on every Kubernetes <strong>Node</strong>.</p><p id="272378cb-b17f-803b-be56-dd6be2ec9036" class="">Its job is to make sure that <strong>containers are running as expected in Pods</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-807c-b66f-f8ea950432e1"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-9095-c836b6c94521" class=""><strong>Key Responsibilities of the Kubelet</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803a-8656-e66da3a4a4f8" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Pod Lifecycle Management</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8051-992c-cb563f1698cc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Watches the API server for <strong>PodSpecs</strong> (Pod definitions).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-9d71-f0e4785978a5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures that the containers described in those Pods are running and healthy.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-a1be-ee5f20a333e6" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Interaction with Container Runtime</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-b85c-e8a63aa859f8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Talks to the container runtime (Docker, containerd, CRI-O, etc.) via the <strong>Container Runtime Interface (CRI)</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-af53-d1924b955dc3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pulls images, creates containers, and manages their execution.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-802f-975b-f5a28c857f55" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Health Monitoring</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8069-bd07-c5dd43780f88" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Runs <strong>liveness probes</strong> and <strong>readiness probes</strong> defined in Pod specs.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-8445-e341e1dea103" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Restarts containers if needed.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-800a-bd92-d4159e28625c" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Node Registration</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-993b-dbadb131c393" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Registers the Node with the Kubernetes API server.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8002-841b-fb7c0bc8abfe" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Reports Node status (CPU, memory, disk, etc.) and Pod status back to the control plane.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-a78f-eddfd8f33a5d" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>Sync Loop</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807a-bf83-c78aac9a8c0f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Constantly compares the actual state of running containers with the desired state from the API server.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8070-abc8-fce87e8c974a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Takes corrective actions if there‚Äôs a mismatch.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-9223-c0a48d18be61" class="numbered-list" start="6"><li><strong>Volume Management</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-943e-d0b93be74b79" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Mounts and manages <strong>volumes</strong> (Persistent Volumes, ConfigMaps, Secrets, etc.) required by Pods.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8076-bb3c-ed34fed0b269"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8001-8e04-d04ac1b2cf92" class=""><strong>What kubelet does </strong><em><strong>not</strong></em><strong> do</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80be-ab0a-eb2c28cad7df" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It does <strong>not schedule Pods</strong> (that‚Äôs the Scheduler‚Äôs job).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ab-8911-dc6c0aa7b96e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It does <strong>not manage networking directly</strong> (handled by CNI plugins).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-9dbd-f6373749b1c9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8055-8e9a-dbab5008eac3" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-a307-ca1ebb3910f8" class="">Think of kubelet as the <strong>caretaker of each Node</strong> üßë‚Äçüîß:</p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-99dc-e3cbe9239643" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>API server</strong> tells it what Pods should be running.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806f-a4b7-e0cd9fbfa92c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The kubelet makes sure those Pods are actually alive, restarts them if needed, and reports back.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805f-aa14-ecece7113107"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8058-b9a3-e533e751016c" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-805e-807e-e952f6bcc6d0" class=""><em>The kubelet is an agent that runs on every Kubernetes Node. It ensures that containers in Pods are running as defined in PodSpecs by interacting with the container runtime, monitoring health, managing volumes, and reporting status back to the control plane.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8060-9a21-d5713b5e5268" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 15:</strong> Explain the concept of a Kubernetes ReplicaSet.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-9169-f41e7b5c3da2" class=""><strong>What is a ReplicaSet in Kubernetes?</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-804a-ab7e-f6a901d69cd8" class="">A <strong>ReplicaSet (RS)</strong> is a Kubernetes resource that ensures a specified number of <strong>replica Pods</strong> are always running.</p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8032-a92d-f9cef227146f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a Pod crashes or a Node fails, the ReplicaSet creates a new Pod to maintain the desired state.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-b01e-c32ccd8e5be9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If there are too many Pods, it will terminate the extra ones.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802e-a5a2-ee626c5b8054"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-8b04-e95733f1665d" class=""><strong>Key Features of ReplicaSet</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801a-b1d6-ed2a14beab48" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Maintains Desired Pod Count</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-be48-f4e1820ec2ca" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Defined in the <code>.spec.replicas</code> field.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800a-8659-dc2d66928ba3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: If <code>replicas=3</code>, it ensures <strong>exactly 3 Pods</strong> are running at all times.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8045-a8e7-c1c7633eff24" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Pod Matching via Labels &amp; Selectors</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-8f69-d71fdf5c43b4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Uses <strong>label selectors</strong> to know which Pods it manages.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8064-be8e-f678e5127417" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If Pods have matching labels, they are included in the ReplicaSet‚Äôs scope.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8076-93aa-d1c93c9e8a06" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Self-healing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8011-8e70-d2f965275f73" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Automatically replaces failed or deleted Pods.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8017-afd3-daf8ca40c559" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Scaling</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-be13-f67efe1e8c3f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can <strong>scale up or down</strong> by changing the <code>replicas</code> value.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806c-bfc5-e016328de862"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-a17c-c8da808ffe7b" class=""><strong>ReplicaSet vs. Deployment</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8057-a333-cf65ea70c32c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ReplicaSet</strong> manages Pods directly.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805b-83e0-e6d9bec32487" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Deployment</strong> is a higher-level abstraction that <strong>manages ReplicaSets</strong> (used for rolling updates, rollbacks, version control).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80da-ac11-ff18443a312b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Best practice: <strong>Use Deployments instead of ReplicaSets directly</strong>, unless you need fine-grained control.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-9e3d-c91510252e32"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8048-ab6f-e2896a572c67" class=""><strong>Example: ReplicaSet YAML</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-802e-9522-db729f32db75" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: frontend-rs
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: frontend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: frontend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: nginx
        image: nginx:latest

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-bf2e-cda40a388b7c" class="">üëâ This ensures <strong>3 NGINX Pods</strong> are always running.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804a-9515-fef7527a745c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-9ad4-ff3f445dd58b" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8088-b944-efeafca7cb93" class="">Think of a ReplicaSet as a <strong>bodyguard team</strong> üõ°Ô∏è:</p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8033-aa49-dbc395cd08aa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If you want 3 guards at all times, a ReplicaSet ensures exactly 3 are present.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807d-8b87-c7c321257d11" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If one leaves, another is assigned immediately.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8056-a627-e43450c6a9b4"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-802c-8b6e-de1a51776a09" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-9e4b-d8165a3a32aa" class=""><em>A Kubernetes ReplicaSet ensures that a specified number of identical Pods are running at all times by monitoring and automatically creating or deleting Pods as needed, using label selectors to identify which Pods it manages.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8004-bfdb-dc1534439857" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 16:</strong> What is the difference between a PersistentVolume (PV) and a PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80af-92eb-ff73292861bf" class=""><strong>PersistentVolume (PV)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8051-885f-e9e03d56debb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>cluster-wide storage resource</strong> provisioned by an administrator.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-a4e8-e48fd16c408c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Represents <strong>actual physical storage</strong> (local disk, NFS, AWS EBS, GCP Persistent Disk, Azure Disk, etc.).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805a-a8ac-f258d99d8d0c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Has its own <strong>lifecycle independent of Pods</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80dc-b677-fc5f9b75e247" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Defined by the <strong>StorageClass, capacity, access modes, reclaim policy</strong>, etc.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-90f3-eb3bcfe4cecd" class="">üìå Think of a PV as the <strong>actual storage space</strong> in the cluster.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80de-b24c-d54655d9f2e0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8039-a8f4-c0db1b03ef1e" class=""><strong>PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-ad47-dccc42da9d4a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>request for storage</strong> made by a user/Pod.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805d-89f8-c20b2078ef97" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Defines the <strong>size, access mode, and storage class</strong> requirements.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8046-b219-df15cac3816f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes matches the PVC to an available PV that satisfies the claim.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8029-b521-c990dbe678f9" class="">üìå Think of a PVC as a <strong>ticket or request</strong> to use some part of the storage.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-8f0e-d38db023e7ae"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8014-b8e9-d087d1e97c0a" class=""><strong>Key Differences Between PV and PVC</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-801a-adf9-dfe93286c6fc" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-a3e5-f9762107b17a"><th id="OQ\J" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="kH;I" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>PersistentVolume (PV)</strong></th><th id="&lt;;Ur" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-803a-bff2-fc3b5ef93ef1"><td id="OQ\J" class="">Definition</td><td id="kH;I" class="">Actual storage resource in the cluster</td><td id="&lt;;Ur" class="">Request for storage by a user/Pod</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-801b-a0aa-c5b330e2d34a"><td id="OQ\J" class="">Created by</td><td id="kH;I" class="">Cluster Admin (or dynamic provisioner)</td><td id="&lt;;Ur" class="">Developers/Users</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806f-bcca-d6717aa23fbe"><td id="OQ\J" class="">Scope</td><td id="kH;I" class="">Supply side of storage</td><td id="&lt;;Ur" class="">Demand side of storage</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806b-b4b7-d4f333e75f10"><td id="OQ\J" class="">Lifecycle</td><td id="kH;I" class="">Independent of Pod lifecycle</td><td id="&lt;;Ur" class="">Bound to Pod usage</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-8414-fda41ccd3446"><td id="OQ\J" class="">Example</td><td id="kH;I" class="">AWS EBS volume, NFS share, local disk</td><td id="&lt;;Ur" class="">Request: &quot;I need 5Gi, ReadWriteOnce&quot;</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8047-a33d-fd4e6045f68d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-873c-e5d575b083f9" class=""><strong>How They Work Together</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8072-a0d5-efeedbc55a8e" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Admin provisions a <strong>PV</strong> (or StorageClass allows dynamic provisioning).</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-95c5-ec71eaae7c4a" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>User creates a <strong>PVC</strong> specifying requirements.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8001-8ab6-fcfe711ff275" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Kubernetes <strong>binds</strong> the PVC to a matching PV.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8026-880f-c7ed0cbcb556" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li>Pod mounts the PVC ‚Üí uses the underlying storage.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8013-832d-c5abc3a63ea7"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8081-9a65-eb78382924e1" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8058-888c-fe814465e07c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>PV</strong> = Apartment üè† (actual storage space available).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-9cdf-c6e10f1d3d43" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>PVC</strong> = Tenant‚Äôs rental request üìù (&quot;I need a 2BHK with a balcony&quot;).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802c-a4d6-e7e9e445b4c8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes matches the request (PVC) to the available apartment (PV).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808f-8c2d-c5677db0d1f1"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8084-a06e-ee07308d89d5" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8060-b724-dacb8e823841" class=""><em>A PersistentVolume (PV) is a piece of storage in a Kubernetes cluster, provisioned by an admin, while a PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC) is a user‚Äôs request for storage. PVCs are bound to PVs to give Pods durable storage independent of Pod lifecycles.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807e-a1d6-f44150e1c2e3" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 17:</strong> What are Kubernetes Namespaces, and why are they useful?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804d-bc08-fd4c26e78e83" class=""><strong>What are Kubernetes Namespaces?</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-8989-d63a5cbc3b48" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Namespace</strong> in Kubernetes is a <strong>virtual cluster within a cluster</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8037-a8d9-d7e509799c19" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It logically separates cluster resources into <strong>isolated environments</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801d-9813-e1d356382b80" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for organizing and managing workloads in large clusters with many users, teams, or projects.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806a-8aef-e7dd6b5c58d2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8008-b2d8-f684ddb46aa6" class=""><strong>Why Namespaces are Useful</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8065-81dc-cfcdf06211b8" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Resource Isolation</strong> üõ°Ô∏è<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8037-8fd9-e92c154cbd24" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Separate teams, environments (dev/test/prod), or applications.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-b1d4-c4b558448e15" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prevent naming conflicts (two teams can each have a <code>frontend</code> Service in different namespaces).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80de-80d7-ebb4baae4182" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Access Control (RBAC)</strong> üîë<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-88c7-ecb803e8d423" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Permissions (Roles/RoleBindings) can be scoped to a namespace.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8067-be45-e79e698e33f5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Devs can only modify resources in <code>dev</code> namespace.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8030-89ed-e164b4310ee7" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Resource Quotas &amp; Limits</strong> üìä<ul id="272378cb-b17f-805b-bbcd-c8a7fb809896" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Limit CPU, memory, and storage per namespace to prevent one team/app from consuming everything.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8022-8523-cbb3ca94a73f" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Organization &amp; Clarity</strong> üìÇ<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-be2c-d8ce4fc2a168" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Makes it easier to manage large clusters with many microservices.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805e-af23-d1ddfd50bd9b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: <code>kube-system</code> namespace holds system components (kube-dns, kube-proxy, etc.).</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-9d75-e34b0a9a24dd"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800f-8dd2-fad059c49eae" class=""><strong>Default Namespaces</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8007-a11b-d3c468e6abe8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>default</code> ‚Üí Where resources go if no namespace is specified.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8063-9639-e43931d40983" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kube-system</code> ‚Üí For system components.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8041-9157-e19f380e37af" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kube-public</code> ‚Üí Readable by all users, often used for cluster-wide info.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-a457-c3d9ff11509d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kube-node-lease</code> ‚Üí Stores node heartbeat leases (for faster node failure detection).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806c-8ec5-e6e790bad3a7"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808a-b11b-f5700b8952c5" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-809e-9bf9-f333dfab9d4a" class="">Think of Namespaces like <strong>folders on your computer</strong> üóÇÔ∏è:</p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-a11d-cfe84dfcc162" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">They help organize files (resources) into groups.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-a9b7-d5b2d5e6cbd9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can set permissions and limits per folder.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-9ed9-ec5b6b024ec4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Different folders can contain files with the same name.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801d-bbef-fbd15ba47c67"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800a-9bc3-ceb97e0a9ec1" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8090-9743-fb3368522f74" class=""><em>Kubernetes Namespaces are virtual clusters within a Kubernetes cluster that provide resource isolation, access control, and better organization of workloads, making them especially useful in multi-team or multi-environment setups.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806d-be93-d596e38c21b7" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 18:</strong> What is the difference between a Kubernetes Job and a CronJob?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8038-8bc3-cb71d8b795ae" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Job</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-8388-dd4c703c5f52" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Job</strong> is a controller that runs <strong>one or more Pods</strong> until a task completes successfully.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-b821-e3bdccd44219" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures that a specified number of Pods finish execution.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-a8ac-c3608ca088fa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a Pod fails, the Job starts a new one until the task succeeds.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f0-a14b-e2cf34cbadb4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Used for <strong>one-time tasks</strong> such as:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-8deb-de89adb7de08" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Data migration</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-8be9-d9c9c5af9da4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Batch processing</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c7-8373-f946cb6a4dc2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Backup tasks</li></ul></li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-be21-de81f3c23108" class="">üìå Think of a Job as <strong>‚Äúrun once, until successful‚Äù</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804e-82b0-fdc38ccf3fdf"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8040-a8b7-e7d439c8f13d" class=""><strong>Kubernetes CronJob</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802e-9d49-dd7f2044c992" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>CronJob</strong> creates <strong>Jobs on a time-based schedule</strong> (similar to Linux <code>cron</code>).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803f-8341-cec35a9f7a97" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Uses <code>spec.schedule</code> with <strong>cron syntax</strong> (e.g., <code>&quot;0 * * * *&quot;</code> to run every hour).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-8d43-e47e674fd640" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Each scheduled run creates a <strong>Job</strong>, which in turn runs Pods until completion.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8068-a8a0-efa7170d941a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Used for <strong>recurring tasks</strong>, such as:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-bfbd-e6009e6278a2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Nightly backups</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-99d1-e63d35f9af07" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Sending daily reports</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8091-93b0-e3b2b72208bc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Regular cleanup jobs</li></ul></li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8072-ae94-e3cea30d8f98" class="">üìå Think of a CronJob as <strong>‚Äúa Job with a schedule‚Äù</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8030-9635-c017848d8c75"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802a-b5a7-c36136d60207" class=""><strong>Key Differences</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8054-8856-d39811713087" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-807d-90d0-e8b9af38969c"><th id="zF?C" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="Nz_g" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Job</strong></th><th id="~SVT" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>CronJob</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8003-ad26-fcdc6d6093d9"><td id="zF?C" class="">Purpose</td><td id="Nz_g" class="">Run a task to completion once</td><td id="~SVT" class="">Run tasks periodically on a schedule</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-807c-9072-e5e3391cd3b2"><td id="zF?C" class="">Trigger</td><td id="Nz_g" class="">Manual (when created)</td><td id="~SVT" class="">Automatic, based on cron schedule</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8044-a08d-cf9cb43c6584"><td id="zF?C" class="">Lifecycle</td><td id="Nz_g" class="">Finishes after task is done</td><td id="~SVT" class="">Keeps creating Jobs at specified intervals</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8063-92e9-ece92810172c"><td id="zF?C" class="">Example Use Case</td><td id="Nz_g" class="">Database migration, file processing</td><td id="~SVT" class="">Nightly backups, scheduled reporting</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805d-ad16-c6294eff6d46"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-966a-cd7ed8974cd5" class=""><strong>Example YAMLs</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-9c42-e52a2dd88301" class=""><strong>Job Example</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-bb5b-e22a2e3be4b0" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: data-migration-job
spec:
  template:
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: migrate
        image: busybox
        command: [&quot;echo&quot;, &quot;Migrating data...&quot;]
      restartPolicy: OnFailure

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-804a-bc95-fbed7ad44d00" class=""><strong>CronJob Example</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8062-81de-d5f1050d1975" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: CronJob
metadata:
  name: backup-cronjob
spec:
  schedule: &quot;0 0 * * *&quot;   # every day at midnight
  jobTemplate:
    spec:
      template:
        spec:
          containers:
          - name: backup
            image: busybox
            command: [&quot;echo&quot;, &quot;Running backup...&quot;]
          restartPolicy: OnFailure

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-b89a-cd88a46c4490"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8056-aa34-ef6118592640" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-aff5-fc1de979e2f8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Job</strong> = Running a washing machine once üëï</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8094-b98d-eb8a1e5ba207" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>CronJob</strong> = Setting the washing machine to auto-run <strong>every night at 9 PM</strong> ‚è∞</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802d-ab22-d5b3b2bad68d"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800a-a373-dcbf056acce8" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8047-b5ca-e404beaba3fc" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Job runs Pods to completion once, while a CronJob creates Jobs on a time-based schedule for recurring tasks.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800d-afc5-f79164e2f9bf" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 19:</strong> Explain what a DaemonSet is and when you would use it.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-955d-f3820e8b9775" class=""><strong>What is a DaemonSet in Kubernetes?</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8092-9558-e2c17d657383" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>DaemonSet</strong> is a controller that ensures <strong>a copy of a Pod runs on all (or some) Nodes</strong> in a cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805f-97a9-e49d618f337d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">As new Nodes are added, Pods are automatically scheduled on them.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804a-be22-ed9b8229884d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If Nodes are removed, DaemonSet Pods on those Nodes are automatically cleaned up.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8084-9892-e9fb0cc7cc55" class="">üìå Basically: <em>‚ÄúOne Pod per Node (or per selected Nodes).‚Äù</em></p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-aaa0-dd3f8ee17385"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8099-a5bd-d44cf4249744" class=""><strong>When to Use a DaemonSet</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8010-b767-c0a2dcd4416e" class="">DaemonSets are typically used for <strong>cluster-wide background services</strong>, such as:</p><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8056-8999-e10c8f8bf3fe" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Monitoring agents</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801a-a9c1-fedd49c4b0a4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Prometheus Node Exporter, Datadog Agent.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-8e0b-e453cb98ec69" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Logging agents</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-ac9b-c4378a09306d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Fluentd, Logstash, Filebeat to collect logs from all Nodes.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-a1e1-eb246b435075" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Networking components</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-8713-ef4a1fa489c9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: kube-proxy, CNI plugins (Calico, Flannel, Weave Net).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-806c-abdf-ffd6a0868d3f" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Security agents</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-a0ed-c6d949cf25ac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Intrusion detection, node-level firewalls.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-b797-ef28026bbece" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>Storage daemons</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-85bd-e1ca78ecf784" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Ceph or GlusterFS storage agents that must run on every Node.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8036-91de-ed3160b03cc6"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-807a-9c61-c1b6be6c256a" class=""><strong>Key Characteristics</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-b874-f938b6a0f2d4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures <strong>uniform deployment</strong> across all Nodes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8072-857f-d5a6f066f69c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Uses a <strong>NodeSelector, taints, or tolerations</strong> to restrict to specific Nodes if needed.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803e-afd1-df91b1ac9d79" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Unlike Deployments, which scale horizontally across Nodes, DaemonSets ensure <strong>one Pod per Node</strong> (not arbitrary scaling).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801a-a913-c980e9836aed"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-95df-f6d07f50a5c8" class=""><strong>Example DaemonSet YAML</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-803d-9f26-fb2c10b44628" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: node-logger
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: node-logger
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: node-logger
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: logger
        image: fluentd:latest

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-9a6e-dd595afd033f" class="">üëâ This ensures a <strong>Fluentd Pod</strong> runs on every Node to collect logs.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8042-9d8b-f49db67d55f5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-8b98-f60e382f7b03" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8022-8855-fc719696a177" class="">Think of a DaemonSet like a <strong>security guard assigned to every building in a city üè¢</strong>:</p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80da-8915-fb33d8c9a59a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">No matter how many new buildings are constructed, each one automatically gets a guard.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8014-94b0-efba62c5f96d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a building is demolished, the guard leaves.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8030-bef8-d874ac950f6f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-801a-ad19-ef5089a286a4" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8054-a033-f37c4d7b84ba" class=""><em>A DaemonSet ensures that a copy of a Pod runs on all (or selected) Nodes in the cluster, making it ideal for cluster-wide services like logging, monitoring, or networking agents.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8008-a7c2-e4aa0f3e1b1f" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 20:</strong> What is the purpose of Kubernetes etcd?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8013-a9eb-d0acc048e8eb" class=""><strong>Purpose of Kubernetes etcd</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8026-aca2-c2990a9c98e5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>etcd</strong> is a <strong>distributed key-value store</strong> used by Kubernetes to store <strong>all cluster data</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-8b0e-df8d40d4d165" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It is the <strong>single source of truth</strong> for the cluster, holding information about:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8065-806b-c92cc46c9de5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Nodes</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8033-9eb7-db4aea15b183" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Pods</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-9805-fd1983c10735" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">ConfigMaps and Secrets</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-bde4-df57dedcf104" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Deployments, ReplicaSets</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8075-ba6a-c0105061a451" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Services and Endpoints</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80db-8925-dcd756356978" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes components (API server, scheduler, controllers) read/write to etcd to maintain the <strong>desired state</strong> of the cluster.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8089-b6a9-d32c24162e12"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8097-8980-d604ffc5fc97" class=""><strong>Key Features</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8030-bd80-ce1e3c4db36c" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Consistency &amp; Reliability</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80af-928b-fa60e8cd8c5e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">etcd uses the <strong>Raft consensus algorithm</strong> to ensure all nodes have the same data.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-820b-dc12d6bf4307" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures cluster state remains <strong>consistent even if some control plane nodes fail</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803c-a17a-d49e86ecf71a" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>High Availability</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808e-b084-dcd155d0a52c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">etcd can run as a <strong>cluster of nodes</strong>, tolerating failures while still serving data.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-8faa-f13acbfaa0dd" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Fast Key-Value Access</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8018-8830-e297dba03ad7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Optimized for storing <strong>small config data</strong>, status info, and metadata, not for large blobs.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8081-9c95-f0ddd0f495a5" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Backup &amp; Restore</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8000-8e8b-fc7912fb5ab1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">etcd data can be <strong>backed up</strong> and restored to recover the cluster state.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8054-8041-fc15b6055f8a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801d-a15c-d2d3422f6335" class=""><strong>Role in Kubernetes</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802c-87a7-df20e7323a24" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>API Server</strong> ‚Üí interacts directly with etcd (reads desired state, writes updates).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8022-8062-e60de6d9f442" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Scheduler &amp; Controllers</strong> ‚Üí query etcd indirectly via API server.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8025-bf5e-d16b47c8c503" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Kubelet</strong> ‚Üí gets PodSpecs via API server (which reads etcd).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-94f4-f4cc69c0001f"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-a0e2-db6f3fb26b4a" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-88cb-f34f563f956f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Think of <strong>etcd as the brain of Kubernetes üß†</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8001-a537-f71cbabef1d8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">It remembers everything about the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8035-8b59-de5c9ce74c07" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Other components consult it to know what‚Äôs running and what needs to run.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805d-8cb9-d0ced1db81d1"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8011-91d5-df442153af99" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80df-b4bc-e93eff2d4cd4" class=""><em>etcd is a distributed key-value store in Kubernetes that serves as the cluster‚Äôs single source of truth, storing all configuration data, state, and metadata to ensure consistency and high availability.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800d-bcac-c5da1c6f590a" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 21:</strong> How does Kubernetes handle self-healing of pods?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808a-bfba-f17776aa913b" class=""><strong>How Kubernetes Handles Self-Healing of Pods</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8010-8dc5-db9184c72840" class="">Kubernetes ensures that the <strong>desired state of the cluster is maintained</strong>. If a Pod fails, crashes, or is deleted, Kubernetes automatically <strong>replaces or restarts it</strong>. This is called <strong>self-healing</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-bdaa-eb042ba6e3d0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-acce-ed8441a325b2" class=""><strong>Mechanism of Self-Healing</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-b1a0-ef84f4a3ca98" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Desired State Declaration</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8027-9376-e60ca3958d55" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">When you create a <strong>Deployment, ReplicaSet, or StatefulSet</strong>, you specify the <strong>number of desired replicas</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-a450-d62df3ea697f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: <code>replicas: 3</code> ‚Üí Kubernetes should always have 3 Pods running.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8049-b0ee-f6e2d0e1ecef" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Monitoring &amp; Detection</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809a-a1a8-c9fa347d8324" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>kubelet</strong> on each Node monitors the health of Pods using <strong>liveness and readiness probes</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-b19e-ce9fa024d32a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>control plane</strong> monitors the cluster state via the API server.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-a03e-f98c4ff3412a" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Automatic Recovery</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-a0a0-ec627dcbcdd5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a Pod fails (e.g., crashes, node goes down), the <strong>ReplicaSet or Deployment controller</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-a908-d41fe1e20d60" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Detects the missing Pod</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c1-84d7-c7ff883924ff" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Creates a <strong>new Pod</strong> on a healthy Node to maintain the desired replica count</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-809b-a380-cf1d8f863d48" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Rescheduling</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-b5d1-e94c44dded5c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a Node becomes <strong>unhealthy or unreachable</strong>, Pods on that Node are <strong>rescheduled</strong> to other Nodes automatically.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c1-8416-fcfa5b04e298"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8013-9dd4-f6ef0df0a091" class=""><strong>Additional Features</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-b423-d4ebdd688b5e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>RestartPolicy</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806e-b262-ca82f7025bca" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Configured per Pod (<code>Always</code>, <code>OnFailure</code>, <code>Never</code>) to determine how kubelet restarts containers.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-9aa9-cfbe9246107d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Probes</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802a-8b29-fed9893a815f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Liveness probe</strong> ‚Üí restarts unhealthy containers automatically.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8003-8405-e74ed81bba17" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Readiness probe</strong> ‚Üí temporarily removes Pod from Service endpoints if not ready.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-be95-cf37597e2356"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8052-b95d-d0bc210943b7" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803a-82cf-d5dd117786fa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Think of Kubernetes self-healing like a <strong>team of caretakers in a hotel üè®</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-8c41-e1eb017768cd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">If a room (Pod) gets damaged or empty, staff automatically <strong>replace or repair it</strong> without manual intervention.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-807e-8058-e6768865b667"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-8b17-e43e4a2e95b7" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-800c-9877-c7d7e9b0ec64" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles self-healing by continuously monitoring Pods and controllers, automatically restarting failed containers or rescheduling Pods to healthy Nodes to maintain the desired state of the cluster.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-84db-d3bc48b6cbc6" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 22:</strong> What is the difference between a horizontal pod autoscaler and a vertical pod autoscaler?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801e-ab34-d92b585517ae" class=""><strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809c-8a61-ebbbfabb1658" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Scales the number of Pods horizontally</strong> based on metrics like <strong>CPU, memory, or custom metrics</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8085-9712-e592453c3cdd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Adds or removes Pods to meet demand.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805a-9676-cbf3c281d6e3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: If traffic spikes, HPA increases the number of Pods from 3 ‚Üí 6; when traffic drops, it scales back.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8006-b052-d85309e01e31" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8045-91f8-c9d00e41c63d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works at the <strong>Deployment, ReplicaSet, or StatefulSet level</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-ae18-f8aee860d66a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Maintains <strong>desired performance</strong> while keeping resource usage efficient.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8044-b78a-f0d0d6d480a2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Configured using <strong>metrics and min/max replicas</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8092-8785-e83c68d8cab2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-a2cd-f09c9c70c60f" class=""><strong>Vertical Pod Autoscaler (VPA)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807d-9d0a-ef09cc7bbf11" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Scales the resources (CPU/memory) of individual Pods vertically</strong>, instead of changing the number of Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-8357-d4f2d3c277fa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Adjusts Pod resource <strong>requests and limits</strong> automatically.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8091-a51b-fb742d421d28" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: If a Pod requires more CPU, VPA can increase its CPU request from 500m ‚Üí 1 CPU.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-8d5b-f42d7ea1d3f0" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-9000-dd508082ae27" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Changes <strong>resource allocation for each Pod</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802e-a270-dd2783ca8719" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for workloads that <strong>cannot scale horizontally</strong>, e.g., stateful applications with local storage.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-8467-d7395e63d504" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can work in <strong>‚Äúauto‚Äù mode</strong> (changes resources automatically) or <strong>‚Äúrecommendation‚Äù mode</strong> (suggests resources).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803e-bcd9-e51bd6034fae"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8052-81d1-c72c446ea2b1" class=""><strong>Quick Comparison Table</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8012-a6da-c66a1fb4becf" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8086-90b5-de216478945f"><th id="aLWT" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="RuHI" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>HPA (Horizontal)</strong></th><th id="m??u" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>VPA (Vertical)</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8007-b5c8-dd706b5b4102"><td id="aLWT" class="">Scaling Type</td><td id="RuHI" class="">Number of Pods (replicas)</td><td id="m??u" class="">CPU/memory resources per Pod</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8056-b6c3-cd49b6f5a352"><td id="aLWT" class="">Use Case</td><td id="RuHI" class="">Stateless, horizontally scalable apps</td><td id="m??u" class="">Stateful apps, single-instance workloads</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8031-b9e4-e24f6dd55da3"><td id="aLWT" class="">Metrics</td><td id="RuHI" class="">CPU, memory, custom metrics</td><td id="m??u" class="">CPU, memory</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8021-b7a9-d641d723d442"><td id="aLWT" class="">Downtime Risk</td><td id="RuHI" class="">Low</td><td id="m??u" class="">Can cause Pod restarts</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8068-bfa6-f4080f025c08"><td id="aLWT" class="">Works With</td><td id="RuHI" class="">Deployments, ReplicaSets, StatefulSets</td><td id="m??u" class="">Any Pod (but StatefulSets need caution)</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-b94a-e57d58b266c9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8003-b187-dc1327d49520" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80df-bb29-c7d52e85c6d7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>HPA</strong> = Hiring more employees when workload increases.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-baf2-fa7e96717bed" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>VPA</strong> = Giving existing employees bigger desks and computers to handle more work.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8041-8789-f87b13b7fb0a"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8016-a35a-f6bd17d2fdb2" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-becc-fd780ced69ca" class=""><em>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler scales the number of Pods based on metrics to handle increased load, while Vertical Pod Autoscaler adjusts the CPU and memory resources of individual Pods to meet demand.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800c-bee5-f4af7db9dcfc" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 23:</strong> What is the significance of the Kubernetes control plane?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-bea5-eaa1b6bb8882" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Control Plane</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8097-a4c3-f57f8290b500" class="">The <strong>control plane</strong> is the <strong>brain of the Kubernetes cluster</strong>. It <strong>makes global decisions</strong> about the cluster (scheduling, scaling, updating) and <strong>manages the overall state</strong> of the cluster.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8062-88ba-de5c7866a7cd"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-b6cc-c3927ac6c886" class=""><strong>Key Components of the Control Plane</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-804c-af4f-edb9fb7f41cb" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>kube-apiserver</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d4-9780-ea2af6fb52c7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>front-end API</strong> of Kubernetes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8088-b961-eb23609ff0aa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">All communications (kubectl, kubelets, controllers) go through it.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b1f8-dafa95988c04" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>etcd</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805b-bbac-f7cc6b055277" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>distributed key-value store</strong> storing the cluster‚Äôs state.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80df-a3a3-f85ad853bb7b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Acts as the <strong>single source of truth</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-92f2-ea52c638c25c" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>kube-scheduler</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8093-9c1a-ea3c7bf4ead8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Decides <strong>which Node a Pod should run on</strong> based on resource availability and scheduling policies.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8097-b365-e57a9fbf08dc" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>kube-controller-manager</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808d-89c7-f81b5b575314" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Runs <strong>controllers</strong> that maintain desired state, e.g., ReplicaSet controller, Node controller, Deployment controller.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-800b-bc99-c6a45a75cabc" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>cloud-controller-manager</strong> (if on cloud)<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8037-8ebc-ef04e098dda9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Integrates Kubernetes with cloud provider APIs (load balancers, storage, nodes).</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-bd6b-f715e68aaa82"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8088-8c11-c15dccf05f81" class=""><strong>Responsibilities of the Control Plane</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8061-8aee-de4f2804d94d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Maintains desired state</strong> of Pods, Nodes, and workloads.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-9400-f0f12c78383c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Schedules Pods</strong> onto appropriate Nodes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-9f4f-d734b2e9a85c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Handles scaling</strong> and self-healing via controllers.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-8e20-d2f9d8ebbdab" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Manages cluster configuration and secrets</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801e-8d01-ec79fc54035b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Provides API endpoints</strong> for users and components.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-b26a-d55acaba720f"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8032-b4c4-dc9398619fc1" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-a669-c269163fbc4d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Think of the control plane as the <strong>CEO and management team of a company üè¢</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-8c93-ff824bfdde55" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">They <strong>decide who works where</strong> (scheduling),</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-bc08-ec931dba7fdc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Monitor performance</strong> (health checks),</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-8fe8-ee8700927909" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Maintain company rules and processes</strong> (desired state),</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-9e26-e1f018b9db42" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">While the employees (worker nodes) execute the actual work.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-8294-f11a6ce2ecee"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-a29d-ed663d30421a" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-805c-96ca-fbabcdcc94de" class=""><em>The Kubernetes control plane is the brain of the cluster, responsible for managing cluster state, scheduling Pods, scaling workloads, and exposing APIs for users and system components.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-bd3f-dc40d8ca581b" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 24:</strong> Explain what a Kubernetes Ingress Controller is.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-ac32-f1f2ddb148b0" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Ingress Controller</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-af3a-d4377fd8f684" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">An <strong>Ingress Controller</strong> is a <strong>specialized load balancer</strong> that <strong>enforces Ingress rules</strong> in a Kubernetes cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80da-9134-e3115a1bc88e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">While an <strong>Ingress resource</strong> defines <strong>what routing rules should exist</strong>, the <strong>Ingress Controller implements them</strong>.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8051-adc8-dc5dfb120b46" class="">üìå Without an Ingress Controller, the Ingress resource has <strong>no effect</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-b5a8-d45e993f1516"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-961f-d80372bb5825" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8099-8200-ed14e74beff9" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Traffic Routing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8094-a60e-e158ccb3d239" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Routes external HTTP/HTTPS traffic to internal Services based on:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-b9c3-e74b2089c0d1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Hostnames</strong> (<code>api.example.com</code>)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-8844-d06fc4dc9c8c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Paths</strong> (<code>/web</code>, <code>/api</code>)</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801e-a930-ffbcb16b26fb" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>TLS/SSL Termination</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-9790-f77a057c4d60" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Handles HTTPS connections, terminating TLS at the controller level.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801f-81cb-ec0d9ad85efa" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Load Balancing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-b7ea-fb252498494e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Distributes traffic to multiple Pods of a Service.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806e-a1b2-eebc93b44727" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can provide <strong>sticky sessions</strong>, request throttling, and other advanced features depending on the implementation.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8078-97ce-f8995215f44f" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Common Ingress Controllers</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-ae79-cdbb57eee546" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">NGINX Ingress Controller</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-8805-e8a5e5894ffc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Traefik</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807c-ae7d-e42c9e7a11ba" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">HAProxy</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-be5b-d4cec597c576" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Istio Gateway (for service meshes)</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-88b7-cae6f387018c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800a-a862-e2da2827b6b4" class=""><strong>How it Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8006-a95f-d2d7928920ce" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>You create an <strong>Ingress resource</strong> with routing rules.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8053-aa20-ca9aea658727" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>The <strong>Ingress Controller watches</strong> the Kubernetes API for Ingress resources.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-b946-ffaee5be4c91" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>It configures itself (e.g., NGINX) to route traffic according to the rules.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805a-a000-f50dfd03cbb2" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li>External clients access the cluster through the Ingress Controller, which forwards requests to the appropriate Service and Pod.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-8508-f4bba6eb936d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f0-b218-e64d729a6be3" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-ae4c-dbc4ef55c9c7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Ingress resource</strong> = Traffic plan / directions üìã</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-85be-d90e8c992167" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Ingress Controller</strong> = Traffic police / router üö¶ that enforces those directions</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-b2fb-ef0718636e69"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800a-a3cf-c77af9689892" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-b59b-c6af23921fca" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Ingress Controller is a component that enforces Ingress rules, routing external HTTP/HTTPS traffic to Services inside the cluster, and handling load balancing, TLS termination, and path/host-based routing.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-babc-d8285ecee506" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 25:</strong> What are the different types of scheduling algorithms used in Kubernetes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-abff-f66a0e2c7e8e" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Scheduling Overview</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-808a-a5be-fe1a29a91b30" class="">The <strong>scheduler</strong> in Kubernetes is responsible for <strong>assigning Pods to Nodes</strong> based on constraints and resource availability. Kubernetes uses <strong>different scheduling algorithms</strong> to decide the ‚Äúbest‚Äù Node for a Pod.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8043-b258-ec57c4c23ef8"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-a017-f00603ba0711" class=""><strong>1. Predicates (Filtering / Feasibility Checks)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8037-970d-d9c69efb177b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Determine <strong>which Nodes are eligible</strong> to run a Pod.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8043-b5b4-f535d9f9082e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Examples of checks:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8063-87aa-ca01e6719bb8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Node has enough CPU/memory (<code>ResourceFit</code>)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80de-8478-c20d3f18c479" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Node matches <strong>NodeSelector</strong> or <strong>affinity rules</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ba-b510-cf156ec80252" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Pod tolerates Node taints (<code>Taints &amp; Tolerations</code>)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-80ad-e209de06602c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Node satisfies Pod‚Äôs <strong>topology constraints</strong></li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8045-830e-ff3843575e8c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a Node fails any predicate, it is excluded.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8059-a443-efeec74fae16"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8058-b22e-cfd1e639d53d" class=""><strong>2. Priorities (Scoring / Ranking)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8013-b9b6-d0912b16275e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Among the eligible Nodes, Kubernetes <strong>scores them</strong> to pick the <strong>most suitable Node</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8071-a543-e0cad2fff1ef" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Examples of scoring strategies:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-822f-dd88155d1a8d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>LeastRequestedPriority</strong> ‚Üí Prefer Nodes with more available resources</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803d-a5ab-d2cfc4f8dad0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>BalancedResourceAllocation</strong> ‚Üí Evenly distribute Pods across Nodes</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-951e-db13f3b0d7f8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>NodeAffinityPriority</strong> ‚Üí Prefer Nodes matching Pod affinity rules</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-a7f7-df22ba751c38"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8065-903c-d0876bdd50a6" class=""><strong>3. Extensible / Custom Schedulers</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-a5d9-cf037c45e3d8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes allows you to <strong>run multiple schedulers</strong> for different workloads.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805d-8e22-f940fb56cff1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Custom schedulers can use your own policies to decide Pod placement.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-8cf9-fc8bdbb6741d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-a365-e380268ae1a9" class=""><strong>Other Advanced Scheduling Features</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801e-9472-fd42fcfea8ee" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Affinity &amp; Anti-affinity</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8026-b611-ff1efe1adecd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Schedule Pods <strong>together</strong> (affinity) or <strong>apart</strong> (anti-affinity) based on labels.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8024-92f9-e279af66b37a" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Taints &amp; Tolerations</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808b-be21-f9c8f4877a8d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prevent Pods from running on certain Nodes unless they ‚Äútolerate‚Äù a taint.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-b98a-e9ff88f5f1d4" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Pod Priority &amp; Preemption</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8043-ae6e-d5d2fb6f3a00" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Higher-priority Pods can <strong>evict lower-priority Pods</strong> if resources are scarce.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-9da2-f90226afa238"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-a48e-d5802b1e8462" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-8b44-e5d1ee78e680" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Predicates</strong> = ‚ÄúCan this person enter the club?‚Äù ‚úÖ/‚ùå</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8055-880f-d073b1541cc2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Priorities</strong> = ‚ÄúWhich table is best for them inside?‚Äù üåü</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-bc7e-d23a02fbdd24" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Affinity &amp; Taints</strong> = Special VIP areas or restricted zones</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804b-9e9a-f66f30b717c9"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8005-9b3e-d44e6b546ee5" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-805d-acd4-da2f5af11257" class=""><em>Kubernetes uses scheduling algorithms that first filter eligible Nodes using predicates, then rank them using priorities, while also supporting affinity/anti-affinity, taints/tolerations, and custom schedulers for advanced workload placement.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80be-8577-ecca1c458e32" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 26:</strong> How do you perform a rolling update in Kubernetes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-b073-ef924262b6a2" class=""><strong>Performing a Rolling Update in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-800e-8bf5-cc36fc8ea6d6" class="">A <strong>rolling update</strong> gradually replaces old Pods with new ones, ensuring <strong>no downtime</strong> and maintaining the desired replica count.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-8147-cef6620434e0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c1-8af5-e4b1ea3a5b01" class=""><strong>Using a Deployment</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8065-8d64-cce13b84d203" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Update the Deployment image or spec</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-803d-b7ee-c23aef63fd8c" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl set image deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt; &lt;container-name&gt;=&lt;new-image&gt;:&lt;tag&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-9a76-f42b27f12eb6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8064-94d6-f603a0a5c65d" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl set image deployment/frontend frontend=nginx:1.25.1

</code></pre></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801b-a661-e9b2ba461de4" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Verify the rolling update</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-807d-bda8-e99ea71ee31e" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout status deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8043-afa6-d89c5c3503c5" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Check rollout history</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8022-bc89-f76ac1abf9dd" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout history deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8096-a145-e7989945e3d2" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Rollback if needed</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-bfa2-e6b10ae39f0a" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout undo deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808c-9d28-fa76035c803d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8062-a1bd-f3252d401c0d" class=""><strong>How Rolling Update Works</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-b952-f564a3134ec6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes <strong>updates Pods gradually</strong> according to the Deployment strategy:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-805a-9e69-c5be09e9b0ad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>maxUnavailable</code> ‚Üí Maximum number of Pods that can be unavailable during the update (default: 25%).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8003-8424-d78e159610cb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>maxSurge</code> ‚Üí Maximum number of extra Pods created above the desired count during update (default: 25%).</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-a9a4-fd33e08ca70b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Old Pods are <strong>terminated one by one</strong> while new Pods are created.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-a73d-d7e27b729112" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures <strong>service availability</strong> throughout the process.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-a870-cf01caf8d552"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-809a-a09a-d7d64f638c9a" class=""><strong>Deployment YAML Example with Rolling Update</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-a467-fee7ea633e45" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: frontend
spec:
  replicas: 4
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: frontend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: frontend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: frontend
        image: nginx:1.25.1

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8046-87c6-dfc78c76a6d3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-9e1c-deccc2348756" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-b319-d18ba117530c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Imagine <strong>renovating a hotel floor by floor</strong> üè®:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-8157-eb6f6b29a3fd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">You renovate one room (Pod) at a time while keeping the rest open.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8007-8603-ebdf37e691a7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Guests (users) don‚Äôt experience downtime.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-8b3a-c527313fba7c"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8060-83e7-f712c5313889" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-a4e9-cba228a22dce" class=""><em>A rolling update in Kubernetes gradually replaces old Pods with new ones in a Deployment, maintaining availability by controlling how many Pods are updated or unavailable at a time, and can be monitored or rolled back using </em><em><code>kubectl rollout</code></em><em> commands.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-85be-e75e69e30c3b" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 27:</strong> What is the purpose of Kubernetes&#x27;s liveness and readiness probes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8088-a94b-cb3898418213" class=""><strong>Liveness and Readiness Probes in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-808f-9dd5-d036c0dbf4e1" class="">Kubernetes uses <strong>probes</strong> to monitor the <strong>health and availability of containers</strong> and take automated actions based on their status.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-b274-c2d3574c0055"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8062-a269-f81161e88745" class=""><strong>1.
