Liveness Probe</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8003-b8c9-fa0a1e858862" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Detects if a container is <strong>alive or stuck</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8007-b880-c408711b6f14" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If the container fails the liveness probe, Kubernetes <strong>restarts it automatically</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-b634-d9450189526d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helps recover from <strong>deadlocks or unresponsive states</strong>.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-800d-93d6-db34f2890e90" class=""><strong>Example Use Cases:</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-af1b-e741d3e41f07" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Application stuck in infinite loop</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d4-9424-d66756d653ff" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Container memory leak causing unresponsiveness</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-a874-e4aafca32eac" class=""><strong>YAML Example:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-ad4a-ea9ff309a66c" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">livenessProbe:
  httpGet:
    path: /healthz
    port: 8080
  initialDelaySeconds: 10
  periodSeconds: 10

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-8299-dfdfe2598285"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-b4e7-ea8781b3bb53" class=""><strong>2. Readiness Probe</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8014-872e-f621a24223d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Detects if a container is <strong>ready to serve traffic</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8077-ad1c-d988716c8565" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If the container fails the readiness probe, Kubernetes <strong>removes it from the Service endpoints</strong> temporarily.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80be-8ad6-d55ed014ef68" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Does <strong>not restart the container</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808b-9bd5-fc844734184c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures <strong>users only receive traffic</strong> to healthy, ready containers.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8003-95b0-ceb603bccca1" class=""><strong>Example Use Cases:</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b5-8d82-c4a990c18a8a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Application is still starting up</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8027-a2a3-f443f56a9f8d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Waiting for database connection or external service</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8083-ba31-f8e5c17259f5" class=""><strong>YAML Example:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8047-95bb-d5e4147ee9fd" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">readinessProbe:
  httpGet:
    path: /ready
    port: 8080
  initialDelaySeconds: 5
  periodSeconds: 5

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-a252-ee9796982064"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8027-a2a4-f93496f8f9d5" class=""><strong>Key Differences</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-a135-c659776a7f75" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8063-a7c5-d8de1585e049"><th id="M|^v" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="UAXc" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Liveness Probe</strong></th><th id="Nj~^" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Readiness Probe</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8001-87a5-ec8da0950447"><td id="M|^v" class="">Purpose</td><td id="UAXc" class="">Is container alive?</td><td id="Nj~^" class="">Is container ready to serve traffic?</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-8b30-ff2b9ec3c224"><td id="M|^v" class="">Action on Failure</td><td id="UAXc" class="">Restart container</td><td id="Nj~^" class="">Remove container from Service endpoints</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-804b-b105-d3d8a12ab562"><td id="M|^v" class="">Use Case</td><td id="UAXc" class="">Deadlocks, crashes</td><td id="Nj~^" class="">Startup, temporary unavailability</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-bce8-fcfe639c3068"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-b05d-e7f4558cfcd3" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805e-a53e-e5dedeaed3fc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Liveness probe</strong> = Checking if a car engine is dead üöó.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8045-8b2d-c6b8a103df9a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Readiness probe</strong> = Checking if the car is ready to drive safely üõ£Ô∏è.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8037-8d1a-e965b9950e24"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8083-aec2-fb7653061a3c" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8027-8cbd-fa754475006b" class=""><em>Kubernetes liveness probes detect if a container is alive and restart it if needed, while readiness probes check if a container is ready to serve traffic and temporarily remove it from Service endpoints without restarting.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-8069-ef5a9e029097" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 28:</strong> Explain the concept of Kubernetes taints and tolerations.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-ad42-e2e49aabd3de" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Taints and Tolerations</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8069-a6c8-d3c3b9a6f73b" class=""><strong>Taints</strong> and <strong>tolerations</strong> are used together to <strong>control which Pods can be scheduled on which Nodes</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-97fc-d70653c1e687"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8068-90ff-d746585b5d9a" class=""><strong>1. Taints (on Nodes)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-99d5-ccc31e098224" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Prevent Pods from being scheduled on a Node <strong>unless the Pod can tolerate it</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-9f17-efd1b03157e5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Applied to Nodes to <strong>‚Äúrepel‚Äù Pods by default</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808b-a495-ca41a755d631" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Syntax:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80df-8308-e9994293c18a" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">key=value:effect

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-a485-f3cafd841ecb" class=""><strong>Effects:</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-9717-d15df6e2540b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>NoSchedule</code> ‚Üí Pod <strong>won‚Äôt be scheduled</strong> unless it tolerates the taint</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806c-9fff-cd12f2f9ed0b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>PreferNoSchedule</code> ‚Üí Kubernetes will <strong>try to avoid scheduling</strong>, but may still schedule if needed</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-939c-e7fd2596f89c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>NoExecute</code> ‚Üí Pod <strong>will be evicted</strong> if it doesn‚Äôt tolerate the taint</li></ul></li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-b936-cf207a1f8365" class=""><strong>Example:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-809e-8562-d05694e5b37d" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl taint nodes node1 key=dedicated:NoSchedule

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-8e06-c0501bb5959b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8047-b5d6-fdfb9b9b7ba4" class=""><strong>2. Tolerations (on Pods)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-9bc7-cad6341618b1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Allow Pods to be scheduled on Nodes with specific taints.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8055-8cd2-deaf8f726e80" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A Pod can <strong>‚Äútolerate‚Äù one or more taints</strong>, overriding the Node‚Äôs default repelling behavior.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-a887-f756ec75da4f" class=""><strong>Example YAML:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8054-9a04-fbc5828d714c" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">tolerations:
- key: &quot;key&quot;
  operator: &quot;Equal&quot;
  value: &quot;dedicated&quot;
  effect: &quot;NoSchedule&quot;

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8040-a14f-c562cd18ff1d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8020-ad5e-f370c542de9b" class=""><strong>How They Work Together</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-b60b-d71276635df5" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Node is tainted ‚Üí repels Pods by default.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801f-ae39-fb410e1a2325" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>Pod has a matching toleration ‚Üí allowed to be scheduled on that Node.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807b-a7c9-de4a36be7c29" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Pod without matching toleration ‚Üí cannot be scheduled (or is evicted if effect is NoExecute).</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8066-be33-d6f67b454bbe"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8071-8546-f28c6f4515c1" class=""><strong>Use Cases</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8063-a5b7-c5aab1eaa784" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Dedicated Nodes for specific workloads (GPU Nodes, high-memory nodes)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8012-a46a-d99cc122a65e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Isolating critical workloads from general workloads</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804e-be72-f9c2972dcfa6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Evicting Pods from unhealthy Nodes</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803e-80a0-eea6c0eef3ab"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8014-9d4e-c262c5aa94e2" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8087-b489-c37d777f2c45" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Taint</strong> = ‚ÄúDo not enter this room without a key‚Äù üö™</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8095-b611-dda2e0b1d932" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Toleration</strong> = Pod‚Äôs ‚Äúkey‚Äù that allows it to enter the room</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8096-bfeb-f19d4f1da622"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8005-b832-f6874d94eba9" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8098-af75-d6ca8243f5d0" class=""><em>Kubernetes taints are applied to Nodes to repel Pods, and tolerations are applied to Pods to allow them to be scheduled on tainted Nodes, enabling fine-grained control of Pod placement.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8036-b949-ec4cadd4998b" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 29:</strong> What is the difference between a Kubernetes Secret and a ConfigMap?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8026-a6c4-eba5b46a39c0" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Secret vs ConfigMap</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-ae5c-cc07b601143b" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-804c-bee0-e2173c164bee"><th id="Otd\" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="c|&lt;T" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:271px"><strong>ConfigMap</strong></th><th id="Jz&lt;n" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:260px"><strong>Secret</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-b564-c4f56ea94e86"><td id="Otd\" class="">Purpose</td><td id="c|&lt;T" class="" style="width:271px">Stores <strong>non-sensitive configuration data</strong></td><td id="Jz&lt;n" class="" style="width:260px">Stores <strong>sensitive information</strong> (passwords, tokens, keys)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-b0f2-f4bf4b2096bc"><td id="Otd\" class="">Data Encoding</td><td id="c|&lt;T" class="" style="width:271px">Plain text</td><td id="Jz&lt;n" class="" style="width:260px">Base64-encoded (not encrypted by default)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8039-a37d-e548390d0b86"><td id="Otd\" class="">Use Case</td><td id="c|&lt;T" class="" style="width:271px">Config values, environment variables, command args</td><td id="Jz&lt;n" class="" style="width:260px">Database credentials, API keys, TLS certificates</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8053-b12b-f667e5874377"><td id="Otd\" class="">Access</td><td id="c|&lt;T" class="" style="width:271px">Mounted as <strong>volume</strong> or environment variables</td><td id="Jz&lt;n" class="" style="width:260px">Mounted as <strong>volume</strong>, environment variables, or accessed by Pods securely</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80cb-bb2f-dd1bd34d3cba"><td id="Otd\" class="">Security</td><td id="c|&lt;T" class="" style="width:271px">Not encrypted by default</td><td id="Jz&lt;n" class="" style="width:260px">Can enable encryption at rest via Kubernetes options</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-bec0-ea1aa43a1021"><td id="Otd\" class="">Example</td><td id="c|&lt;T" class="" style="width:271px">App settings, log level, feature flags</td><td id="Jz&lt;n" class="" style="width:260px">MySQL password, JWT secret, TLS private key</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8027-880b-de567df0ff8d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-966c-c97491e5e535" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8035-a9bf-dce033ba290b" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Both are objects to decouple configuration from Pod images</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-806d-9bec-c8f87bc303db" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Secrets are meant to be sensitive</strong>, so you should <strong>avoid committing them to version control</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807b-b41b-c3c284dfb8e5" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Pods can <strong>consume both via volumes or environment variables</strong>, but Secrets are handled more carefully in the API and kubelet.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-9dda-f05aee1100e1"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8038-a294-f80421c3cae9" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-bd76-c9682715d831" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ConfigMap</strong> = Post-it notes with instructions üìù</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8060-b214-c25cd0b72f70" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Secret</strong> = Locked safe with passwords üîí</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8097-80b2-db483c55fc10"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-b29c-edd4e00772cc" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8060-b77a-d5b334b0f5af" class=""><strong>ConfigMap YAML</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8005-a7af-e88611bb7f58" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: app-config
data:
  LOG_LEVEL: &quot;DEBUG&quot;
  FEATURE_FLAG: &quot;true&quot;

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e9-b930-ea2089b80494" class=""><strong>Secret YAML</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-804d-afa2-d7bcd88b2005" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Secret
metadata:
  name: db-secret
type: Opaque
data:
  DB_PASSWORD: bXlzcWwxcGFzc3dvcmQ=  # &quot;mysql1password&quot; base64-encoded

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8010-8aa2-c6ac7d61978c"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-ada3-e1d46f97881a" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8018-8cf6-ed6d01f21962" class=""><em>A ConfigMap stores non-sensitive configuration data for Pods, while a Secret stores sensitive information like passwords or API keys, often base64-encoded and can be encrypted at rest.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8025-a9db-f6f3382c0877" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 30:</strong> How do you troubleshoot a pod that is stuck in a pending state?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8076-a4f6-dbeacc6a2f44" class=""><strong>Pod Pending State</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-9392-f9a9db6d7d1f" class="">A Pod is in <strong>Pending</strong> state when it has been accepted by the Kubernetes API but <strong>cannot be scheduled onto a Node</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8043-8d7f-dc9aee0341ab"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8083-b822-c68f3bd561cf" class=""><strong>Steps to Troubleshoot a Pending Pod</strong></h3><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8088-9172-f61f7bd497fe" class=""><strong>1. Check Pod Events</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ab-8600-fb5418dfa3d5" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl describe pod &lt;pod-name&gt; -n &lt;namespace&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c2-8ec3-c0aaedd7b21e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Look for <strong>events</strong> at the bottom.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8072-b172-dfb8d0ade319" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Common messages:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80dc-a0fe-f8e4fc713afd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>0/3 nodes are available: insufficient cpu/memory</code></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-a5af-e68db10c68a4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>node(s) didn&#x27;t match Pod&#x27;s nodeSelector/affinity</code></li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80de-8fbb-f85e446b83eb"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-861a-feaa5e6c16ad" class=""><strong>2. Check Node Resources</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8096-b8cb-dc1f7d4f0e94" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get nodes -o wide
kubectl describe node &lt;node-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8081-af60-dfe543cf18a6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Verify that Nodes have <strong>enough CPU, memory, or disk</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801a-aa8c-d3bbaa15a9ca" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Check Node conditions: Ready, DiskPressure, MemoryPressure, NetworkUnavailable.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cb-9fe0-d6b57d098b2d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8014-aff6-c96a061b7477" class=""><strong>3. Check Pod Scheduling Constraints</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80db-b69f-da3500d024aa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>NodeSelector / NodeAffinity</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-87c5-dadffe751cea" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ensure the Pod‚Äôs constraints match available Nodes.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802d-b2d5-d1249fd1aea0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Taints &amp; Tolerations</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802f-9769-fc8f92732341" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ensure the Pod can tolerate Node taints if any.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801d-ad11-cf9025d55e8c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806a-9a65-fe97d71ea2cf" class=""><strong>4. Check Quotas and Limits</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-807b-86f3-d7446287b32b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get resourcequota -n &lt;namespace&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-a25d-f8d85d1f89a1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensure the Namespace has <strong>enough quota</strong> for CPU, memory, or Pods.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-99fe-c8d116660dcb"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805a-8ce2-f73eadf93d04" class=""><strong>5. Inspect PersistentVolume Claims</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-9294-e94d04a284a5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If the Pod uses PVCs, check if <strong>PVCs are bound</strong>:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-808d-8d3e-c4ba55546288" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get pvc -n &lt;namespace&gt;
kubectl describe pvc &lt;pvc-name&gt; -n &lt;namespace&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-a180-e2cb7f0dc352" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pending PVCs can block the Pod from being scheduled.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8052-84b1-e8662df295e0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-b56c-f86461b34d71" class=""><strong>6. Check Cluster Autoscaler / Node Availability</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-8124-d689ee4ae633" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If using autoscaling, ensure the cluster has <strong>enough Nodes</strong> to schedule the Pod.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8015-93db-e68e9cd63d77" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Sometimes scaling up the cluster solves pending Pods.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-b056-cdc7df392073"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-ab7a-cb87db6a6242" class=""><strong>Common Causes of Pending Pods</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806d-ad01-c888ace564c0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Insufficient resources on Nodes (CPU/memory)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805b-b92f-cb77fbc8cbf2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">NodeSelector or affinity rules not matching any Node</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-ab2d-ec2b5706d5a2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pod cannot tolerate Node taints</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-a5e9-ddde4ecc19e5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">PVC not bound / Storage issues</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-a6a3-f380c2c36e28" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ResourceQuota exceeded in Namespace</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804f-bdf0-c95932f4a6c0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8053-9969-e8e0b988a7e8" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804e-b18a-efbba2f400d0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Think of Pending Pods like <strong>people waiting for seats in a crowded theater üé≠</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-8fac-f27b1fbe5324" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">No free seat ‚Üí they wait (Pending)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806c-beb1-d36c3204a939" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Must check seat availability (Node resources), seat restrictions (affinity/taints), and ticket limits (quotas)</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8017-a103-d3828201f64c"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-8b49-d1835461e9bb" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8041-9650-cade47567673" class=""><em>To troubleshoot a Pending Pod, check Pod events with </em><em><code>kubectl describe</code></em><em>, verify Node resources, scheduling constraints (affinity/taints), Namespace quotas, and PVC binding to identify why the Pod cannot be scheduled.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8091-b2da-fe1655de89bf" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 31:</strong> What is the difference between a Kubernetes Cluster and a Node?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-809a-9028-e4235d4d9284" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Cluster vs Node</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8089-b256-e3473682f92f" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-abf5-fdee5af6c46f"><th id="Xeal" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="yyNd" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:285px"><strong>Cluster</strong></th><th id="CR_e" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:273px"><strong>Node</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8090-8e64-e83a92480692"><td id="Xeal" class="">Definition</td><td id="yyNd" class="" style="width:285px">A <strong>set of machines (physical or virtual)</strong> running Kubernetes, managed as a single unit</td><td id="CR_e" class="" style="width:273px">A <strong>single machine</strong> (physical or virtual) in the cluster that runs Pods</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8030-aec6-cc4261ef512a"><td id="Xeal" class="">Scope</td><td id="yyNd" class="" style="width:285px">Cluster-wide</td><td id="CR_e" class="" style="width:273px">Node-specific</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-805c-b565-f8034ef0839b"><td id="Xeal" class="">Components</td><td id="yyNd" class="" style="width:285px">Control plane + Worker nodes</td><td id="CR_e" class="" style="width:273px">Kubelet, kube-proxy, container runtime, Pods</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806c-9224-e3321ad1c666"><td id="Xeal" class="">Role</td><td id="yyNd" class="" style="width:285px">Orchestrates and manages workloads, scheduling, networking, scaling</td><td id="CR_e" class="" style="width:273px">Runs Pods and provides compute resources for workloads</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-87cc-edf3b838f259"><td id="Xeal" class="">Example</td><td id="yyNd" class="" style="width:285px">Entire Kubernetes setup with multiple Nodes</td><td id="CR_e" class="" style="width:273px">A VM or server in the cluster running Pods</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8000-b9b5-d4829eb44cc3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801c-b40c-d4320a666407" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-babb-eb80c2be8693" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Cluster</strong> is the <strong>entire Kubernetes system</strong>, including:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c1-af00-da7ab82e5d72" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Control plane nodes (API server, scheduler, etcd)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8077-aaab-d549ba643f52" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Worker nodes (where workloads run)</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-9ef0-cd9d0333321a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Node</strong> is an <strong>individual worker machine</strong> that provides CPU, memory, and storage for Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-a5e4-d435b794063c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes schedules Pods <strong>from the Cluster level</strong> to appropriate Nodes.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8050-b7a7-d4dc3f695a01"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-a3af-fd3b6da66c04" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-9c22-e7ad455f8731" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Cluster</strong> = The whole city üèôÔ∏è</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-8e8e-edb7a30cb13c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Node</strong> = A single building üè¢ in the city that houses residents (Pods)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cb-97ac-e2e90a8ad9ea"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e9-bcbb-c21d3270ba14" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8028-b12b-ee4cfd8c83fe" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Cluster is the entire collection of machines (control plane + worker nodes) managed as a single system, while a Node is an individual machine in the cluster that runs Pods and provides compute resources.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-a9f5-e8c39fc1e001" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 32:</strong> Explain the concept of &quot;kubectl&quot; and its common commands.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8019-9c30-e8f590719d39" class=""><strong>What is kubectl?</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8007-9717-da33d9060c18" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kubectl</code> is the <strong>CLI (Command Line Interface) tool</strong> for Kubernetes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8065-9abc-c4d3ceddd5e4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It allows you to <strong>communicate with the Kubernetes API server</strong> to:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-a68f-ffadc37245e9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Deploy and manage applications</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802b-8764-ddfb3b1e30ff" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Inspect cluster resources</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8078-846d-c1c9f2aa39d5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Debug and troubleshoot workloads</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-a3d6-d6e9d93d34e8"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8034-a5da-fc107ef7ae82" class=""><strong>Common kubectl Commands</strong></h3><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-9884-cf3cbd699df8" class=""><strong>1. Cluster Information</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8012-916a-e2109d114756" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl cluster-info           # Shows cluster endpoint and info
kubectl get nodes              # Lists all nodes in the cluster
kubectl describe node &lt;node&gt;   # Detailed info about a node

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-bf51-fd376cbaa854" class=""><strong>2. Managing Pods</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8089-990f-c79608a95123" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get pods               # List all pods
kubectl describe pod &lt;pod&gt;     # Show details/events for a pod
kubectl logs &lt;pod&gt;             # View logs from a pod
kubectl exec -it &lt;pod&gt; -- bash # Access pod shell

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-807c-91e9-cce1221ceca5" class=""><strong>3. Managing Deployments</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8039-a464-dca1384ed4e8" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get deployments
kubectl describe deployment &lt;deployment&gt;
kubectl apply -f deployment.yaml
kubectl delete deployment &lt;deployment&gt;
kubectl rollout status deployment/&lt;deployment&gt;
kubectl rollout undo deployment/&lt;deployment&gt;

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-89a7-c5d5ef17242b" class=""><strong>4. Services and Networking</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-807a-8eba-c6d98d8c7d4b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get svc               # List services
kubectl describe svc &lt;service&gt;
kubectl port-forward &lt;pod&gt; 8080:80 # Forward local port to pod

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8041-9ad2-f7b4b9c38413" class=""><strong>5. Configurations</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-8904-c0bd2c676aee" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get configmap
kubectl describe configmap &lt;configmap&gt;
kubectl get secrets
kubectl describe secret &lt;secret&gt;

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8072-bc61-da43a3b1b3cf" class=""><strong>6. Namespaces</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8008-948c-c6b142f89626" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get ns                 # List namespaces
kubectl config set-context --namespace=&lt;ns&gt;  # Switch namespace

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-9f8c-d720d23e6216" class=""><strong>7. General Utilities</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-805e-8cb6-dc0eeab0ddb5" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl apply -f &lt;file.yaml&gt;   # Create/update resources
kubectl delete -f &lt;file.yaml&gt;  # Delete resources
kubectl top pod                # Shows resource usage (CPU/memory)

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80dc-b51e-d142b44c0aef"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-bd24-e7c869786db7" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-bab8-e95c1f0f4457" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kubectl</code> is like a <strong>remote control for Kubernetes</strong> üéõÔ∏è:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8049-b28d-e69e5976e041" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">You can <strong>inspect</strong>, <strong>control</strong>, and <strong>manage</strong> everything in the cluster from your terminal.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806b-b798-d391697f1dfd"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-a36f-d1122e8f2568" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-807c-a3ae-e8415a52f763" class=""><em><code>kubectl</code></em><em> is the Kubernetes command-line tool used to interact with the API server for managing, deploying, and troubleshooting cluster resources, with common commands like </em><em><code>get</code></em><em>, </em><em><code>describe</code></em><em>, </em><em><code>apply</code></em><em>, </em><em><code>logs</code></em><em>, and </em><em><code>exec</code></em><em>.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804d-a05b-e10d8e37b2cc" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 33:</strong> What is the difference between a Kubernetes Service of type <code>ClusterIP</code> and <code>LoadBalancer</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808c-a640-fa6a542bc553" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Service Types: ClusterIP vs LoadBalancer</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8005-a914-cc9ea73895b0" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8026-bcd2-cf1975363726"><th id="@ig&gt;" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="wIqb" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:265px"><strong>ClusterIP</strong> üñß</th><th id="}NIe" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:272px"><strong>LoadBalancer</strong> üåç</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-ab59-c72580c1490e"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">Purpose</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px">Exposes the Service <strong>inside the cluster only</strong></td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px">Exposes the Service <strong>externally to the internet</strong></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806a-925c-d7c5ae6eaace"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">Default?</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px">Yes, default Service type</td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px">No, must be explicitly defined</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-9d1d-e613de8dbaed"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">Access</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px">Accessible only via cluster-internal IP</td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px">Accessible via an <strong>external IP</strong> provided by cloud provider</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-97d8-db926ac16668"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">Use Case</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px">Internal communication between microservices</td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px">Public-facing applications (websites, APIs)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8046-a1e9-c352cd77367c"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">External Traffic</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px">‚ùå Not accessible from outside the cluster</td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px">‚úÖ Accessible from outside the cluster</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8005-8f14-e17fcb50213d"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">Implementation</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px">Uses <strong>cluster-internal routing</strong></td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px">Requires cloud provider integration (AWS ELB, GCP LB, Azure LB)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-804d-b98c-dc4f50389e47"><td id="@ig&gt;" class="">Example Command</td><td id="wIqb" class="" style="width:265px"><code>kubectl expose pod mypod --port=80 --type=ClusterIP</code></td><td id="}NIe" class="" style="width:272px"><code>kubectl expose pod mypod --port=80 --type=LoadBalancer</code></td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8021-905d-ca728801eefa"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8048-9514-ebf8985606ea" class=""><strong>ClusterIP Example (default)</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8087-9e0a-f883f203bcdc" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: my-service
spec:
  selector:
    app: myapp
  ports:
  - port: 80
    targetPort: 8080
  type: ClusterIP

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806d-9463-f32d00cf38b2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Assigned an <strong>internal IP</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8089-8f6e-fd6d73da4c32" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Only accessible <strong>inside the cluster</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8048-a761-f28f8a540378"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8067-a419-e6df1b1a69d0" class=""><strong>LoadBalancer Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8059-9d87-fadc12e01711" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: my-service
spec:
  selector:
    app: myapp
  ports:
  - port: 80
    targetPort: 8080
  type: LoadBalancer

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801f-8e56-c06bd0dba95d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Cloud provider provisions an <strong>external load balancer</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-93a2-d8099edf79fa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The Service gets a <strong>public IP</strong>, making it reachable from the internet.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-bae1-c25268ef5bdb"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-86c6-c70df0ba88a2" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-8304-e3a8636191f8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ClusterIP</strong> = Office intercom üìû (only employees inside can use it).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-a48e-d7e736385cad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>LoadBalancer</strong> = Public phone line ‚òéÔ∏è (anyone outside can call in).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806f-aab7-ff463961ab47"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8091-8088-c5589874f4a4" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-807f-a27d-de3bcbac07f6" class=""><em>A ClusterIP Service exposes applications only inside the cluster using an internal IP, while a LoadBalancer Service provisions an external load balancer to make the application accessible from outside the cluster.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-b3f6-d0db411c6482" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 34:</strong> What is a Kubernetes PersistentVolume (PV) and how is it different from a PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-8c62-ecea9323f804" class=""><strong>PersistentVolume (PV)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-a123-c975bbd6a1c5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>PersistentVolume</strong> is a <strong>piece of storage in the cluster</strong> that has been <strong>provisioned by an administrator or dynamically by Kubernetes</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-940e-e01959f0cb69" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Represents actual storage resources like <strong>NFS, cloud disk, or local storage</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80de-b2b9-d5f969c0a747" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Cluster resource</strong>, independent of any Pod.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-bcc0-f405dce6cba7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example attributes:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8022-922d-d8696232a132" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>capacity</code> (size)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803a-978a-d21475759bc6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>accessModes</code> (ReadWriteOnce, ReadOnlyMany, ReadWriteMany)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-8741-c844a8864960" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>storageClassName</code></li></ul></li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8016-8b42-c93871bb2515" class=""><strong>Example PV YAML:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-800b-ab99-fe21cf179c42" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: PersistentVolume
metadata:
  name: my-pv
spec:
  capacity:
    storage: 10Gi
  accessModes:
    - ReadWriteOnce
  persistentVolumeReclaimPolicy: Retain
  hostPath:
    path: /mnt/data

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8082-820d-e0135249c458"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-b7e9-f6079580cc25" class=""><strong>PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801e-bc73-f4d021716285" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>PersistentVolumeClaim</strong> is a <strong>request for storage by a Pod</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-ae45-fc723401ad3f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods do <strong>not access PVs directly</strong>; they use PVCs to bind to a PV.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8024-ab82-fb81f0c1ca69" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Specifies desired storage:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-93ac-dabff574a728" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>size</code></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-ad1b-ce50bde80454" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>accessModes</code></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-81f0-ea7addd8f6e9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>storageClassName</code></li></ul></li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8079-bc32-d0022b371486" class=""><strong>Example PVC YAML:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-bfb2-fcd949f396c7" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
metadata:
  name: my-pvc
spec:
  accessModes:
    - ReadWriteOnce
  resources:
    requests:
      storage: 5Gi

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-aec4-c1f35f71b972"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-adab-cda663637f3b" class=""><strong>Key Difference</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-9d49-c1b8267a81cb" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806a-8093-df31e1e5550c"><th id="`fG^" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="[;UX" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>PersistentVolume (PV)</strong></th><th id="ZqDk" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8091-a04d-f7c7844d7287"><td id="`fG^" class="">What it is</td><td id="[;UX" class="">Actual storage resource in cluster</td><td id="ZqDk" class="">Request for storage by a Pod</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8097-8d45-fae2693877a1"><td id="`fG^" class="">Scope</td><td id="[;UX" class="">Cluster-wide</td><td id="ZqDk" class="">Pod-level (bound to a PV)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-805f-ad99-eb25e13743de"><td id="`fG^" class="">Provisioning</td><td id="[;UX" class="">Manual or dynamic (by admin or storage class)</td><td id="ZqDk" class="">Always dynamic or binding to available PV</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-a76c-fc6e500485a7"><td id="`fG^" class="">Usage</td><td id="[;UX" class="">Provides storage</td><td id="ZqDk" class="">Used by Pods to consume storage</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-bd5c-c8e94a97bfba"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-809a-8858-f552cba3cffa" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-ac41-cc937f058735" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Admin creates PVs (or they‚Äôre dynamically provisioned).</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e9-b71e-f74c1e2faf79" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>User creates PVC specifying size and access modes.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e9-8030-d5438214b026" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Kubernetes <strong>binds a suitable PV to the PVC</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801d-9a51-c3cb8e4b032c" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li>Pod uses the PVC as a <strong>volume mount</strong> to access storage.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8046-a494-cc4b16b67da3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80be-bb36-dea2a7a7479e" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d4-8562-d210564c2501" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>PV</strong> = Warehouse with storage space üè¨</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800b-93ef-c9f4965220c3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>PVC</strong> = Customer requesting storage space üì¶</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-800b-ddc652f22093" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes matches the request to an available warehouse.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80df-9665-c5634ae32863"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-807b-93d9-d95be20d5beb" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8051-b31c-c8f3e8e7150b" class=""><em>A PersistentVolume is a cluster storage resource, while a PersistentVolumeClaim is a Pod‚Äôs request to consume storage; Kubernetes binds PVCs to PVs to provide persistent storage to Pods.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-b82e-c3ceda92acc5" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 35:</strong> How does Kubernetes handle rolling back a deployment?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-8173-e428460b31a4" class=""><strong>Rolling Back a Deployment in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-80b3-f770a6590be7" class="">Kubernetes allows you to <strong>rollback a Deployment to a previous revision</strong> if the current rollout fails or causes issues.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806e-b898-eacf7d11c7b5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800a-83b6-d7d19d76b63d" class=""><strong>Mechanism</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803a-961d-ea123325f81c" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Revision History</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8094-a792-cc6264c2045a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Each Deployment maintains a <strong>history of revisions</strong> (by default, last 10).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-af02-d9332c8c61b7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Each revision corresponds to a Deployment‚Äôs configuration (container image, replicas, etc.).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8059-9819-cf31cf06766a" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Rollback Command</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-9193-d40c42d8ee22" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout undo deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ba-b8e5-faf9406e5020" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolls back to the <strong>previous stable revision</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8048-b9d9-ec045033f0c6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can also rollback to a <strong>specific revision</strong>:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ba-af61-d859313eb210" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout undo deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt; --to-revision=2

</code></pre></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-891a-fea2dbe6e84b" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Monitor Rollback</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8098-960a-e330f51f7126" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout status deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-804a-93d7-e3f5ac8df8d3" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Verify History</strong><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-b5c5-d6904c7957f2" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout history deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8080-9070-c9950436048d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-bf4b-e7a4530c18f4" class=""><strong>How it Works Internally</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-829d-e48bcaacdff1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes creates <strong>new ReplicaSets</strong> for every Deployment update.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-83bc-d697ccda6e3f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolling back simply <strong>reverts to an earlier ReplicaSet</strong>, scaling it up while scaling down the current one.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8085-824a-eeaea1b33a12" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures <strong>zero-downtime</strong> if the Deployment strategy is RollingUpdate.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805b-894f-e5a90fbd6dc8"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-ac8d-fb91d04cc211" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8098-94c8-e144867b3034" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Think of Deployment rollback like <strong>undoing a software update on your phone</strong> üì±:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-807f-a500-f1fa66427ea2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">The phone reverts to the last working version without losing data.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808f-949b-c6c866a6984d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Users continue using the app without interruption.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802e-9fc2-d3ea3b34a293"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800b-8d0c-ce7ceaa45e18" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8016-8d0d-ec1eee981f5c" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles rolling back a Deployment by reverting to a previous revision‚Äôs ReplicaSet using </em><em><code>kubectl rollout undo</code></em><em>, allowing the cluster to restore a stable state without downtime.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8097-b754-d0974ed527f0" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 36:</strong> What is the role of the Kubernetes Scheduler?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-8b2b-d817801e4e5a" class=""><strong>Role of the Kubernetes Scheduler</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-808a-a5ba-d3cfbdc3d43f" class="">The <strong>Kubernetes Scheduler</strong> is responsible for <strong>assigning Pods to Nodes</strong> in the cluster based on resource availability and scheduling policies.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808a-a84c-cf0ef0042ebf"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802f-9ce1-d2a188f73338" class=""><strong>Key Responsibilities</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8002-b823-e6492310f060" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Pod Placement</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-8763-cdbcd60409a1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Determines the <strong>most suitable Node</strong> for each Pod that does not have a Node assigned.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-98bf-ee97364dfeeb" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Resource Awareness</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8013-ab0b-ef15755e7a6c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Considers <strong>CPU, memory, storage, and GPU</strong> availability on Nodes.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-a422-dfaa3787d0c3" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Constraint Evaluation</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-a757-dfb463e2bf69" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Respects Pod requirements like:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8088-8fd0-e6413fbac0da" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>NodeSelector</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8099-b7b1-e183dddd59a3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Node Affinity / Anti-affinity</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8054-a4dd-c9ecd16036e1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Taints and Tolerations</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8087-959b-f5b7860d93d8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Pod Affinity / Anti-affinity</strong></li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8059-91c4-d8bc8acaa31b" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Prioritization</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-b307-dec74819725a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scores eligible Nodes using algorithms (LeastRequestedPriority, BalancedResourceAllocation, etc.) to pick the <strong>best fit Node</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-9552-e91252383ead" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>Pod Scheduling Lifecycle</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808d-92f2-fb0cfa088c0a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Watches for <strong>unscheduled Pods</strong> via the API server.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8035-b7a0-ca5dc98b6fb2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Binds the Pod to a Node by updating the Pod spec.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806e-8e7e-dbe6e69dfaf1"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-809a-8c5f-df1c268a9b7e" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8055-83fe-c3c4ce078336" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The Scheduler is like a <strong>matchmaker ü§ù</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ed-9bfd-ecc4b8f14cbe" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Matches Pods with Nodes that best meet their requirements, ensuring <strong>efficient resource use</strong> and <strong>balanced workloads</strong>.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803c-9a83-cfef5ee3b247"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a28e-da4676c34fc8" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-a439-c461c5bfa820" class=""><em>The Kubernetes Scheduler assigns Pods to Nodes based on resource availability, constraints, and policies, ensuring optimal placement and efficient cluster utilization.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-a28b-f5974c139657" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 37:</strong> Explain the difference between a Kubernetes StatefulSet and a Deployment.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802a-a88a-eacc04c432f5" class=""><strong>StatefulSet vs Deployment</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8089-bc2a-e4b2dd466454" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a906-fd4cab0e7543"><th id="kjMq" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:267px"><strong>Deployment</strong></th><th id="cPi;" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:270px"><strong>StatefulSet</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-be91-f40901403111"><td id="kjMq" class="">Use Case</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">Stateless applications</td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Stateful applications</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8062-b4af-f7212132bec5"><td id="kjMq" class="">Pod Identity</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">Pods are <strong>interchangeable</strong> (no stable identity)</td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Pods have <strong>stable, unique identities</strong> (<code>pod-0</code>, <code>pod-1</code>, ...)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-b062-ca8a6c396420"><td id="kjMq" class="">Persistent Storage</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">Usually uses PVCs without guaranteed mapping</td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Each Pod gets a <strong>stable PersistentVolume</strong> that persists across rescheduling</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-9b42-e3a5fba8fb48"><td id="kjMq" class="">Pod Ordering</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">Pods are created/updated <strong>in parallel</strong></td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Pods are created, updated, and deleted <strong>in order</strong> (sequentially)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8029-ae51-d1f5efbfea09"><td id="kjMq" class="">Network Identity</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">IPs can change when Pods are rescheduled</td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Each Pod gets a <strong>stable DNS name</strong> (<code>pod-0.service</code>)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8014-bdfe-c017d902039f"><td id="kjMq" class="">Scaling</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">Easy to scale up/down</td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Scaling is supported but order matters</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80be-aed5-cae29103e585"><td id="kjMq" class="">Examples</td><td id="k&gt;Q&lt;" class="" style="width:267px">Web servers, stateless APIs</td><td id="cPi;" class="" style="width:270px">Databases (MySQL, MongoDB), Kafka brokers</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-a776-f4d08f3d65be"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-89bd-ce69f3b67952" class=""><strong>Key Differences</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8030-a24b-f27f30cc4be1" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Pod Identity</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-a956-f22c9722a5d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deployment: Pods are identical and interchangeable.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8024-98ff-e808455fb8c9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">StatefulSet: Each Pod has a <strong>persistent identity</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8019-a4d6-d6801c9e57e9" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Storage</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808b-afe6-e8a19521a01d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deployment: PVCs may get remapped to different Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-85b3-d866a2480327" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">StatefulSet: PVCs are <strong>bound to a specific Pod</strong> and remain after rescheduling.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805f-a200-f28e77485bdf" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Updates</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8030-a4ed-ceb6047847e0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deployment: Supports <strong>rolling updates</strong> in parallel.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-ac0f-fda64f58a543" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">StatefulSet: Updates occur <strong>one Pod at a time</strong>, preserving order and stability.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803b-9e9e-de599f2015a0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800f-9d07-fb6bfeb124cf" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-b2e2-e20860ef24f6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Deployment</strong> = Fleet of taxis üöï: any car can pick up any passenger.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-8b3a-f929c9478869" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>StatefulSet</strong> = Apartment buildings üè¢: each resident (Pod) has a fixed apartment (PersistentVolume) and address (DNS).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80db-8e15-ffa2610533bf"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800a-9ae7-fd61412485db" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8002-aefd-c93997980b04" class=""><em>A Deployment manages stateless Pods that are interchangeable and can scale/rollout in parallel, while a StatefulSet manages stateful Pods with stable identities, ordered deployment, and persistent storage.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8068-98c1-d639f9d0b328" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 38:</strong> What is a Kubernetes ConfigMap, and how is it used?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806e-98d5-d78183539bcd" class=""><strong>Kubernetes ConfigMap</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-b754-cc5cf2c43062" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>ConfigMap</strong> is an object used to <strong>store non-sensitive configuration data</strong> for Pods separately from application code.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-95e0-e1857f932fad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Allows you to <strong>inject configuration into Pods</strong> without rebuilding images.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-800c-8b64-cd0b30b511a3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8049-bb53-de3825769b76" class=""><strong>How ConfigMaps Are Used</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807b-884d-fac0dc6afa7d" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>As Environment Variables</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8066-8ebe-d4aec01b8b44" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: app-config
data:
  LOG_LEVEL: DEBUG
  FEATURE_FLAG: true

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-8359-f5f1cd729d1d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pod can use these as environment variables:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8063-94c8-cf024f7d7aa2" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">envFrom:
  - configMapRef:
      name: app-config

</code></pre><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a60b-f14832450404" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>As Command-Line Arguments</strong></li></ol><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b6c2-f76e1ea898a1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods can read ConfigMap values as <strong>args</strong> or <strong>commands</strong>.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-809b-aae2-fea641e6c364" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>As Volumes</strong></li></ol><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804f-bfb4-e2b596b8e459" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ConfigMap can be <strong>mounted as a file</strong> inside a Pod:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-9b1e-ffeb885a97ac" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">volumes:
  - name: config-volume
    configMap:
      name: app-config

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8099-8548-e9c438ff4201" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Application can read files for configuration.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-ae82-d71abbc19293"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-9a5b-f36a5f22db85" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8074-92d1-dbfa1d202e61" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ConfigMaps <strong>do not store sensitive data</strong>; use Secrets for that.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-b146-c48f86cd1d25" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Supports <strong>key-value pairs</strong>, <strong>file-based config</strong>, or <strong>entire directories</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8090-aa45-c5a1f8b6f424" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Updates in ConfigMap can <strong>propagate to running Pods</strong> if mounted as a volume.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-83e0-e12330e69d32"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8096-b488-ca8783c3dc64" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8093-b820-f1946b9c9cbb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ConfigMap = <strong>Post-it notes with instructions</strong> üìù</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801f-bb81-c71f676daee0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Secret = <strong>locked safe with sensitive info</strong> üîí</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-858a-ee1f6e778735"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-9078-fe10bca59870" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-a8f3-c343ab13cadf" class=""><em>A Kubernetes ConfigMap stores non-sensitive configuration data separately from Pods and can be consumed as environment variables, command-line arguments, or mounted volumes, allowing dynamic configuration without rebuilding images.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-be97-ee602ddff641" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 39:</strong> How can you secure communication between pods in a Kubernetes cluster?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800e-bb0e-e441afe13d1b" class=""><strong>Ways to Secure Communication Between Pods</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-8a88-ffb7aa0a5fa4" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Network Policies</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-bf5b-d0de3d3df17a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes <strong>NetworkPolicy</strong> objects control <strong>which Pods can communicate with each other</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8048-a3da-cea2524aa9c8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can define rules for <strong>ingress and egress traffic</strong> based on:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-9477-ebe4dd66343b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Pod labels</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-8677-c00dd3282f3f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Namespace</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-9cb1-d2021b06fd7f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ports and protocols</li></ul></li></ul><ul
