id="272378cb-b17f-8045-bd79-c7884fcf255b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8014-8736-ea16c64249b7" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: NetworkPolicy
metadata:
  name: allow-app-traffic
  namespace: default
spec:
  podSelector:
    matchLabels:
      app: frontend
  policyTypes:
  - Ingress
  ingress:
  - from:
    - podSelector:
        matchLabels:
          app: backend
    ports:
    - protocol: TCP
      port: 8080

</code></pre></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8050-ba31-f0aa3dceb2af" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>mTLS (Mutual TLS)</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803c-96b5-cc6cbe7b8be5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Encrypts traffic <strong>between Pods</strong> and ensures <strong>both client and server authenticate each other</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-b55f-c5b132ddc636" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Often implemented using <strong>service meshes</strong> like Istio, Linkerd, or Consul.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8024-ad9b-c707db05c61a" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Secrets for Credentials</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-92dd-e1e0e36d8794" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>Kubernetes Secrets</strong> for sharing API keys, certificates, or tokens between Pods securely.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8022-a16a-d44fe05308cf" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Pod Security Context &amp; RBAC</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f0-8c35-e543e4912508" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Limit what Pods can do in the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-bde8-d648150a6e31" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>ServiceAccounts</strong> and <strong>RBAC</strong> to restrict access to APIs and resources.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-802c-a5a0-eba794f800ac" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>Encryption in Transit</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8090-bc8a-da9295221a0a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Enable <strong>TLS for all internal services</strong>, even if traffic is internal to the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8020-9420-e60ccfe326ac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Service meshes can automate this.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8060-8880-fd29108269a0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8043-8d19-ef25c9dbc693" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80af-9714-eaf4dfb74641" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">NetworkPolicy = <strong>fences and gates between buildings</strong> üè¢</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801b-9786-fbe76917c649" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">mTLS = <strong>secret handshake and encrypted letters</strong> ‚úâÔ∏èüîí</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801b-8162-fe1ccc72568e"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800d-ac7b-c97f9564c7f0" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8077-811a-eef9d42388c1" class=""><em>Pod-to-Pod communication in Kubernetes can be secured using NetworkPolicies to control traffic, mTLS for encrypted and authenticated connections, Secrets for credentials, and RBAC to limit access to cluster resources.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-b74c-c9b7e6975ebb" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 40:</strong> What are Kubernetes network policies, and how do they work?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8003-bec0-c41a43f7860c" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Network Policies</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803d-abef-d4df889fb9f2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>NetworkPolicies</strong> are Kubernetes resources that <strong>control traffic flow between Pods</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-ad49-cefac07ca036" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">They define <strong>rules for ingress (incoming) and egress (outgoing) traffic</strong>, effectively acting as a firewall at the Pod level.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8078-b9e8-f65fcc55b614" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Without a NetworkPolicy, <strong>all Pods can communicate freely</strong> within the cluster (default allow).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-aaaa-ff6027556623"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8053-8ce6-eea0881ce860" class=""><strong>Key Components of a NetworkPolicy</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8044-a84a-cd131a7364bf" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Pod Selector</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8070-b681-df3f394f8081" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Specifies <strong>which Pods the policy applies to</strong> (via labels).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8040-8e88-e846a033f605" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Policy Types</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-9ef2-c91cfdf94327" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>Ingress</code> ‚Üí Controls <strong>incoming traffic</strong> to Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-84eb-c8f599d9b40b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>Egress</code> ‚Üí Controls <strong>outgoing traffic</strong> from Pods.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807f-a87b-de3df3a748a2" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Rules</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ab-95f6-d1ab8d057bc5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Define <strong>sources/destinations</strong>, <strong>ports</strong>, and <strong>protocols</strong> allowed or denied.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802e-9aeb-c206b31f41ee"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8002-a66b-eed6a2e79cd9" class=""><strong>Example: Allow Traffic from Backend Pods Only</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8018-91c3-ca96fb671281" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: NetworkPolicy
metadata:
  name: frontend-policy
spec:
  podSelector:
    matchLabels:
      app: frontend
  policyTypes:
  - Ingress
  ingress:
  - from:
    - podSelector:
        matchLabels:
          app: backend
    ports:
    - protocol: TCP
      port: 8080

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8002-9cd0-e4be57bdbae0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Only Pods labeled <code>app: backend</code> can access <code>frontend</code> Pods on port 8080.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b7da-cbd23205b88d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808b-b37f-c5525aa62491" class=""><strong>How They Work</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-b388-de391f997815" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Network plugin (CNI) enforces policies at the network layer.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8098-bf50-ccedeff4c2a9" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>If no policy applies, traffic is <strong>allowed by default</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80cb-80df-ff495c392864" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>If a policy exists, <strong>only traffic explicitly allowed is permitted</strong>, everything else is blocked.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-ace2-c3106899db5b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805c-9e3d-ca2dcc765fe0" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804e-a322-cd959d27a796" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">NetworkPolicy = <strong>gates and fences around houses</strong> üè†<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8069-a1e3-e8e2253e4266" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">You decide <strong>who can enter and leave</strong> each house (Pod).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802c-a139-feeac1f39bcf"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-801f-89df-c54d6d178bf5" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-809b-b198-cdf89d69c62c" class=""><em>Kubernetes NetworkPolicies control ingress and egress traffic between Pods using selectors, ports, and protocols, enforcing pod-level network segmentation through the cluster‚Äôs network plugin.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800b-a6e2-c7de4ed1128e" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 41:</strong> What is the difference between <code>kubectl exec</code> and <code>kubectl run</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8035-bc01-f10e9fdd61d8" class=""><strong>Difference Between </strong><code><strong>kubectl exec</strong></code><strong> and </strong><code><strong>kubectl run</strong></code></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80da-ae2b-f72f420d167a" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-91e7-e2b9fdcb153e"><th id="&lt;PuR" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="byb}" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:259px"><strong>kubectl exec</strong></th><th id="_f&lt;L" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:274px"><strong>kubectl run</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8052-9189-db5acdaf49a1"><td id="&lt;PuR" class="">Purpose</td><td id="byb}" class="" style="width:259px">Execute a command <strong>inside an existing Pod</strong></td><td id="_f&lt;L" class="" style="width:274px">Create and start a <strong>new Pod</strong></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8094-96e6-d54de01772cd"><td id="&lt;PuR" class="">Use Case</td><td id="byb}" class="" style="width:259px">Debugging, inspecting, or running commands in a running container</td><td id="_f&lt;L" class="" style="width:274px">Quickly deploy a test Pod or container</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-b77c-ef68c562def3"><td id="&lt;PuR" class="">Pod Requirement</td><td id="byb}" class="" style="width:259px">Pod must <strong>already exist</strong></td><td id="_f&lt;L" class="" style="width:274px">Creates a Pod if it does not exist</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-8d33-c1c689e69f47"><td id="&lt;PuR" class="">Example</td><td id="byb}" class="" style="width:259px"><code>kubectl exec -it my-pod -- bash</code></td><td id="_f&lt;L" class="" style="width:274px"><code>kubectl run my-pod --image=nginx --port=80</code></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ed-a341-d4622aaf3915"><td id="&lt;PuR" class="">Interactivity</td><td id="byb}" class="" style="width:259px">Can be <strong>interactive</strong> (<code>-it</code>)</td><td id="_f&lt;L" class="" style="width:274px">Not meant for interactive sessions (but can run in background)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-807d-93ac-eb52f59fc2f0"><td id="&lt;PuR" class="">Lifecycle Impact</td><td id="byb}" class="" style="width:259px">Temporary execution inside Pod</td><td id="_f&lt;L" class="" style="width:274px">Creates a persistent Pod in the cluster</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-8ca1-dc526b237fae"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8009-a4ea-e12cecedaace" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8016-bcec-c5a44b6bf0e5" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><code><strong>kubectl exec</strong></code><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8013-9434-c3bb8cf43afc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Runs commands inside <strong>existing containers</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-8660-fdbdf112a3b5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Common for debugging, checking logs, or running shell commands.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805b-a5c1-ebcca43fc869" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><code><strong>kubectl run</strong></code><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8054-808e-e2c4197776ef" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Used to <strong>create a new Pod quickly</strong> for testing or deployment.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8020-91b5-fb3254a87f4f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Often replaced by <code>kubectl create deployment</code> for production workloads.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8034-8674-dbb3dd2ecee2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806f-a1c4-f91cbd610dc1" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-a57c-c716b783fef8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kubectl exec</code> = <strong>going inside an apartment to check or fix things</strong> üè†</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-bf49-f6b8ff944d60" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kubectl run</code> = <strong>building a new apartment and moving in</strong> üè¢</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-8311-d82c8a7f8d56"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-9922-f171ba3e6541" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-802e-be85-f6ddaa58d6a7" class=""><em><code>kubectl exec</code></em><em> runs commands inside an existing Pod for debugging or inspection, while </em><em><code>kubectl run</code></em><em> creates and starts a new Pod in the cluster.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80da-8c4f-fe5e4ee5df00" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 42:</strong> Explain the concept of &quot;pod affinity&quot; and &quot;anti-affinity.&quot;</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8060-8f0e-db6c233b890d" class=""><strong>Pod Affinity and Anti-Affinity in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8080-8591-f4c8b0ce8a7c" class="">These are <strong>scheduling rules</strong> that influence <strong>which Nodes a Pod can be placed on</strong> based on the presence or absence of other Pods.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8090-b5cd-e5c2de5e0882"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804c-84dd-f14eb2f0e02b" class=""><strong>1. Pod Affinity</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808d-a407-c40920e1f84e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Schedule a Pod <strong>close to other Pods</strong> based on labels.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808e-8222-d15cf62b9cfc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures <strong>co-location</strong> for better communication, lower latency, or data locality.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-92f9-e8ce9dd540f2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: You want frontend Pods to run on the same Node as backend Pods.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8004-a966-dc2bf93fbd2c" class=""><strong>YAML Example:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8021-bcaa-d25cf175a357" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">affinity:
  podAffinity:
    requiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution:
    - labelSelector:
        matchLabels:
          app: backend
      topologyKey: &quot;kubernetes.io/hostname&quot;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8031-8307-d32db7c32ba1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>requiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution</code> ‚Üí <strong>hard requirement</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-830e-fb5e36c98ba1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>topologyKey</code> ‚Üí Node label to enforce placement (e.g., same hostname, zone)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e9-85c3-e3027fe3f9ab"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cb-a2ab-ed142f1708fa" class=""><strong>2. Pod Anti-Affinity</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-b980-e90d9d32bf7f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Schedule a Pod <strong>away from other Pods</strong> based on labels.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8087-ad70-e4085dc63776" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prevents Pods from being on the same Node to improve <strong>availability and fault tolerance</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-940d-d4ffc75e40d2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Avoid placing multiple replicas of a database on the same Node.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8024-8529-df7ceedce8bd" class=""><strong>YAML Example:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80c7-b4c0-e485d755679c" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">affinity:
  podAntiAffinity:
    requiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution:
    - labelSelector:
        matchLabels:
          app: database
      topologyKey: &quot;kubernetes.io/hostname&quot;

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8082-a287-e5079cc31516"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-8b2b-e19abb7501be" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8032-81fb-f428109d6347" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Both use <strong>label selectors</strong> to identify target Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-9b30-e8bacf8d3600" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Both can be <strong>hard (</strong><code><strong>required</strong></code><strong>) or soft (</strong><code><strong>preferred</strong></code><strong>) rules</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-a71e-d7ee2693f299" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Controlled via <code><strong>affinity</strong></code><strong> field</strong> in Pod spec.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-8147-c090f57372e9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-b4dd-c6a4a29aca4e" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808e-9962-eb5b153baf4e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Pod Affinity</strong> = ‚ÄúSit near your friends at lunch‚Äù üçΩÔ∏è</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-8272-c5b76ead5220" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Pod Anti-Affinity</strong> = ‚ÄúSit away from people with the same job to avoid risk‚Äù üö∂</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-800e-905b-f91631ccb60f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-809e-9f37-fee2fc08dc94" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-801b-bd7a-c9f84154daa0" class=""><em>Pod affinity schedules Pods close to other Pods with specific labels, while pod anti-affinity schedules Pods away from certain Pods to improve fault tolerance or distribution.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80df-8e49-dadd3f2a8219" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 43:</strong> What is the purpose of the Kubernetes API Gateway?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802d-9aa2-f471301c6201" class=""><strong>Kubernetes API Gateway</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-800a-984a-e6263eaa82e1" class=""><strong>Purpose:</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800e-9297-d6218b894bf0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">An <strong>API Gateway</strong> acts as a <strong>single entry point</strong> for external clients to access services running inside a Kubernetes cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-803b-fc36f17ea5fb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It <strong>manages, routes, secures, and monitors API requests</strong> to multiple microservices.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8059-8708-fdf2722db3d7"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-814f-d8b2de5e7df7" class=""><strong>Key Functions of an API Gateway</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8097-89d2-fac82f2cc237" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Request Routing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-87b8-c8016432b489" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Routes incoming requests to the appropriate service or microservice.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8067-8cd8-e36cbc342bd5" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Load Balancing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-a810-c270387d2314" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Distributes traffic across multiple instances of a service.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8030-9dd7-d488826e6408" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Security</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8021-8cbd-e4b142e24b77" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Handles <strong>authentication</strong>, <strong>authorization</strong>, <strong>TLS termination</strong>, and <strong>rate limiting</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-ae60-f436a1a68e64" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Protocol Translation</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8072-b4f0-f402ffdfbddd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can translate protocols (e.g., HTTP to gRPC).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-880e-cd51f05e8cd4" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>Monitoring and Logging</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8005-97ea-ea47be30edca" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Collects metrics, logs, and traces for requests passing through the gateway.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ab-bd0b-dbf53ef8ab6b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806f-aa88-d073ebb542a9" class=""><strong>How It Works in Kubernetes</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808e-a458-d672594f9b5a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Typically implemented via <strong>Ingress Controllers</strong> or standalone API gateways (like <strong>Kong, Ambassador, or Istio Gateway</strong>).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8029-b4fc-dbb2f7dbc9e5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example with Ingress:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-9efe-df210fbfb891" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Ingress
metadata:
  name: my-ingress
spec:
  rules:
  - host: myapp.example.com
    http:
      paths:
      - path: /
        pathType: Prefix
        backend:
          service:
            name: my-service
            port:
              number: 80

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8091-8893-ce42a5dd1288" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The API Gateway (Ingress Controller) listens to requests and routes them to <code>my-service</code>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8016-a5d5-c24111ae1c44"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802a-9e6f-fedabe875c28" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-9803-f25edc01a55b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">API Gateway = <strong>reception desk at a large office building üè¢</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80de-b025-fff549d3173d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Routes visitors to the correct department, checks IDs, and ensures only authorized access.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8059-bc78-f2a46c65d17c"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-805f-a64f-f0e69ffe64c6" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-804d-9010-e79c12c99b39" class=""><em>A Kubernetes API Gateway serves as a single entry point for external clients, routing requests to services, providing load balancing, security, and monitoring in the cluster.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80b0-89d0-ef211ef2b181" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 44:</strong> How do you monitor a Kubernetes cluster?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801c-a9ab-ff28280c37af" class=""><strong>Monitoring a Kubernetes Cluster</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80bd-aaef-eee44f3905c4" class="">Monitoring involves <strong>tracking the health, performance, and resource usage</strong> of the cluster, nodes, and applications.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-aa3c-f744a93a85b3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802f-8465-d90c7c7a74ec" class=""><strong>1. Metrics Collection</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809f-9598-c50f410eae57" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>CPU, memory, disk, network usage</strong> at cluster, node, and Pod levels.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-934a-d62b7415b6ae" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Tools:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-a7a0-fd7d304ab01e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Prometheus</strong> (metrics collection and alerting)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804c-8abf-cd32fbbc245f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Metrics Server</strong> (lightweight metrics API for kubectl top)</li></ul></li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-805f-b91f-eec1884655d6" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl top nodes      # View node metrics
kubectl top pods       # View Pod metrics

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8098-af81-c964d8b2bc3b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800e-99ef-c62bbcf1dcca" class=""><strong>2. Logging</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800b-b258-edda8c628835" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Collect and analyze logs from Pods, Nodes, and cluster components.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8033-9a91-ef043625f27f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Tools:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8004-beba-fe8e6679ca97" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>ELK Stack</strong> (Elasticsearch, Logstash, Kibana)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-9b6f-d696b96d62b2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Fluentd / Fluent Bit</strong> (log collection)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809e-a4c2-f63b89ffe707" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Loki + Grafana</strong></li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-b96c-c2b1683e0923"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808c-9e16-d80dc7df30fd" class=""><strong>3. Health Checks</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8015-be81-daa5a5148c00" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Liveness and Readiness Probes</strong> ensure Pods are running and ready.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806c-958d-f2578db59f94" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Monitor <strong>controller and API server health</strong> using metrics and events:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-801c-83c3-fd0b46b607ba" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get events -A
kubectl get componentstatus

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80dc-b6f0-ca3e6d863673"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-9d8c-d23b16c7e011" class=""><strong>4. Alerts and Notifications</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-a1cc-fe77a87b64ff" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Configure <strong>alerts</strong> for high CPU/memory usage, node failures, or Pod crashes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8054-b4bd-e51001640a86" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prometheus Alertmanager can send alerts via <strong>email, Slack, or PagerDuty</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-800e-bd8d-df32ca32c99f"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-8161-c2d5f06ae315" class=""><strong>5. Visualization</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-ace1-d478d891d181" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>Grafana</strong> dashboards to visualize metrics, cluster resource usage, and trends.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-9756-e4f6d513d898"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80da-be24-c4e092e05e9a" class=""><strong>6. Audit and Security Monitoring</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-89f0-de46ab2b03eb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Enable <strong>Kubernetes Audit Logs</strong> to track API access and security events.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806f-909f-fce999f65109" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Tools: <strong>Kubernetes Audit, Falco, Open Policy Agent (OPA)</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805a-9d36-d5ca0b858393"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8037-b710-f501b21b3737" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-bed6-e0ef5a292284" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Monitoring Kubernetes = <strong>dashboard in a spaceship üöÄ</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8007-b514-eee0d94398d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">You track fuel (CPU/memory), engine health (Pods/nodes), alarms (alerts), and logs (mission events).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8005-a397-ebbc2a66ca9f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8075-844e-d065bcfd3af3" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-804c-b3d3-f7ae9101f7d7" class=""><em>A Kubernetes cluster is monitored using metrics (Prometheus, Metrics Server), logs (ELK, Fluentd), health checks (liveness/readiness probes), alerts (Alertmanager), and dashboards (Grafana) to ensure performance, availability, and security.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80a0-a1f5-d2955d6674f2" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 45:</strong> What is the purpose of a Kubernetes service account?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8097-88d8-e4a7d993106c" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Service Account</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8055-b687-fdcfc961bfe5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>ServiceAccount (SA)</strong> provides an <strong>identity for Pods</strong> to interact with the Kubernetes API.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-ad28-c9088b8be768" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It is used to <strong>authenticate and authorize Pods</strong> when they access cluster resources.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8055-b3ab-db593d1a0c11"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-8a7a-c2b173f1dda5" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8074-81ba-f1d4dd1637ed" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Default ServiceAccount</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8092-89c9-f52093411b7a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Every namespace has a default ServiceAccount.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-8a45-ea8e0ad0b1bd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If a Pod does not specify one, it uses the default.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-8cf1-cf5ff47b7bad" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Custom ServiceAccounts</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806b-9c13-ecba97c4487a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can create SAs for <strong>specific permissions</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8007-8b9a-d3de5dd098df" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Bind them to <strong>Roles/ClusterRoles</strong> using <strong>RoleBinding/ClusterRoleBinding</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8021-9799-f77a66b8d43c" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Use Cases</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8088-a543-f89fc9cc3051" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods accessing the Kubernetes API securely (e.g., controllers, operators).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8006-bc2e-d30791c230b8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Granting fine-grained permissions for automation or CI/CD tools.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8073-b626-c37a40cddfda"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-9d28-d4627ab13b56" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-90ce-e1c6ce2e0320" class=""><strong>Create a ServiceAccount:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8065-9961-f8e97029d662" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: my-service-account
  namespace: default

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-99d6-c1c8519d17c2" class=""><strong>Bind it to a Role:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-8bc8-e5de0347fcf0" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBinding
metadata:
  name: read-pods-binding
  namespace: default
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: my-service-account
  namespace: default
roleRef:
  kind: Role
  name: pod-reader
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io

</code></pre><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-950e-de70f35859fd" class=""><strong>Use in a Pod:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-930f-dd3433c1656a" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
metadata:
  name: my-pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: my-service-account
  containers:
  - name: my-container
    image: nginx

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8090-9db6-d6efba577b8a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8032-a8cd-dd35e67391a4" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-8794-f53ce55fd3d3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ServiceAccount = <strong>ID card for a worker üÜî</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-a184-d6500f0f22cf" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">The worker (Pod) can only perform actions permitted by its ID (Role/ClusterRole).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8094-996e-f5e3e1bdc066"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-9b3e-c6841fbaeaea" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8064-aeee-f6198700139b" class=""><em>A Kubernetes ServiceAccount provides an identity for Pods to authenticate with the API server, enabling secure and controlled access to cluster resources.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80cf-bec2-d1433a2dee89" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 46:</strong> Explain the difference between a Kubernetes Horizontal Pod Autoscaler and a Cluster Autoscaler.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8021-b1c0-d9c8b6dafe1a" class=""><strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA) vs Cluster Autoscaler (CA)</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-802a-a29d-c78fbe2d3779" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80c7-8f5c-ef230cd87dfd"><th id="Sve;" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="ENp}" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:250px"><strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA)</strong></th><th id="uuLc" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:266px"><strong>Cluster Autoscaler (CA)</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8007-a028-f31c2375eece"><td id="Sve;" class="">Purpose</td><td id="ENp}" class="" style="width:250px">Automatically scales <strong>Pods</strong> in a Deployment, ReplicaSet, or StatefulSet</td><td id="uuLc" class="" style="width:266px">Automatically scales <strong>Nodes</strong> in the cluster up or down</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8096-8232-cafff6a25627"><td id="Sve;" class="">What It Scales</td><td id="ENp}" class="" style="width:250px">Number of Pod replicas</td><td id="uuLc" class="" style="width:266px">Number of Nodes (VMs or physical machines)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8014-a0ab-f96878962c49"><td id="Sve;" class="">Metric Basis</td><td id="ENp}" class="" style="width:250px">CPU, memory, custom metrics</td><td id="uuLc" class="" style="width:266px">Unschedulable Pods / Node resource pressure</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-b11e-d646db61e00b"><td id="Sve;" class="">Scope</td><td id="ENp}" class="" style="width:250px">Application-level</td><td id="uuLc" class="" style="width:266px">Cluster-level</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8009-9eff-ca56fc575ea9"><td id="Sve;" class="">How It Works</td><td id="ENp}" class="" style="width:250px">Adjusts the number of Pod replicas based on metrics</td><td id="uuLc" class="" style="width:266px">Adds or removes Nodes to meet Pod scheduling needs</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8050-b379-ed27bc2074a6"><td id="Sve;" class="">Example Use Case</td><td id="ENp}" class="" style="width:250px">Scale web server Pods when CPU usage exceeds 70%</td><td id="uuLc" class="" style="width:266px">Add a Node when HPA wants more Pods but Nodes are full</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f0-a3e5-e5add439f88c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804c-8e82-c60c5c5332e1" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8045-8393-cf16ed246034" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>HPA</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fa-9cc8-da7e8e44e40f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Watches metrics like CPU or custom metrics.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8042-80c3-f80b5045c1d6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Increases/decreases <strong>replicas</strong> of a Deployment or StatefulSet.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-83eb-f010c07a8921" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Keeps application responsive under load.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-802a-88e8-eeab452b1510" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Cluster Autoscaler</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8067-bb95-e964273bba8f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works with cloud provider APIs (AWS, GCP, Azure) or on-prem infrastructure.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807f-ad4f-fa6e40ca1a4d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Adds Nodes when Pods cannot be scheduled due to insufficient resources.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-9b43-c4be928a1367" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Removes idle Nodes to save cost.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80da-9d01-d2afa6e483a2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-b76b-dcec41becb06" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808e-aa59-e43c03d74de8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">HPA = <strong>adding more cashiers üè™ in a store when customers increase</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8067-883a-ed5ec128440b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Cluster Autoscaler = <strong>opening new store branches üè¢ when the store is full</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-87e7-d287605659c2"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-804e-b67d-c0f7784fa1b8" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8047-bc8c-f21ba78f67b8" class=""><em>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler scales the number of Pods based on metrics, while Cluster Autoscaler scales the number of Nodes in the cluster to ensure Pods can be scheduled efficiently.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80e0-9be0-e4b722fc1d0d" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 47:</strong> What is a Kubernetes helm chart, and how is it used?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8074-a08e-d8cb98bd1760" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Helm Chart</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-a55e-d5183cb5ab41" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Helm</strong> is a package manager for Kubernetes, similar to <code>apt</code> or <code>yum</code> for Linux.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8029-8e3f-fb2dd780242a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Helm Chart</strong> is a <strong>collection of YAML templates and metadata</strong> that defines a Kubernetes application.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-93ce-f5a9f3946843" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It allows you to <strong>deploy, version, and manage applications consistently</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-94d8-e4a5576cbcf0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8005-8825-d7def35131a1" class=""><strong>Key Components of a Helm Chart</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-8e79-d97e2ba8e625" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Chart.yaml</strong> ‚Äì Metadata about the chart (name, version, description).</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-806c-8226-c4f24b18cd51" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>values.yaml</strong> ‚Äì Default configuration values that can be overridden.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-802c-851a-ee91192e0a91" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Templates/</strong> ‚Äì Kubernetes resource templates (Deployment, Service, ConfigMap, etc.) using Go templating.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8015-8da0-d1ca813a776e" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>charts/</strong> ‚Äì Subcharts or dependencies.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-809a-9d9b-d94484e0e037" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>README.md</strong> ‚Äì Documentation.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80da-b4ac-f8b08ca36763"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-a2d7-d380d9812077" class=""><strong>How Helm Charts Are Used</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801b-89c3-eb385fef4cab" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Install an Application</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-a109-e8667c67d19b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">helm install my-app ./my-chart

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-a425-e4fda9bbf5f5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deploys all resources defined in the chart with default or custom values.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8025-b7da-d092df21fcbc" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Upgrade an Application</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-89d9-cfe63b3c4ec2" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">helm upgrade my-app ./my-chart

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8064-9af3-e746edcf6ed3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Updates resources while preserving state.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-991c-fc5f574b1130" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Rollback an Application</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-8fe6-f837ea914c92" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">helm rollback my-app 1

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8086-9ff6-fa7c98afa3d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolls back to a previous release version.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-802d-9908-e507d930657d" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Uninstall an Application</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-a98d-fad0920bf99b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">helm uninstall my-app

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-bce4-e0088da50a6b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Removes all resources created by the chart.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8038-b168-c301c0620b51"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-8083-f649e82c011c" class=""><strong>Benefits of Helm Charts</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8082-9dec-cb50389b3a08" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Reusable templates</strong> ‚Üí Consistent deployments across environments.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-8f73-d69ff97be66f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Versioning</strong> ‚Üí Track and roll back application releases.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800b-b4e6-df2d99c0cf53" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Parameterization</strong> ‚Üí Easily customize applications using <code>values.yaml</code>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-8663-f381b6219a94" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Dependency management</strong> ‚Üí Charts can include subcharts.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8062-8b87-cde7800e1222"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-ae73-e1d9b4ab3c66" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802a-be97-da1b2bbc5820" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm Chart = <strong>Docker Compose for Kubernetes with templates üì¶</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-9751-d25e839cf99e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Define your app once, deploy anywhere with different configurations.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-8394-f43371b8da3a"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8063-95af-da9403bdd340" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-b4a9-cc56b0dbecbc" class=""><em>A Helm Chart is a packaged collection of Kubernetes manifests and templates used to deploy, manage, and version applications consistently across environments.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8062-a9ec-ca97649ef7fe" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 48:</strong> How does Kubernetes handle resource requests and limits?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-812e-e71e5c16f0d8" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Resource Requests and Limits</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-809e-9f6f-d656a8608d74" class="">Kubernetes uses <strong>resource requests and limits</strong> to <strong>control CPU and memory usage</strong> for Pods and containers.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801a-b507-cfb40aaa4100"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-badc-d26c7ed55706" class=""><strong>1. Resource Request</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-b07c-fa3f6586897b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Definition:</strong> The amount of CPU/memory a container <strong>guarantees</strong> to get.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-92c8-d75d6c526fe3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Used by the <strong>Scheduler</strong> to determine <strong>which Node can run the Pod</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80db-8669-f2988f4e4408" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-89b5-e18c91f3849d" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">resources:
  requests:
    cpu: &quot;500m&quot;
    memory: &quot;256Mi&quot;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804c-84d2-c894a4d5fab0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scheduler ensures the Node has <strong>at least 500m CPU and 256Mi memory available</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-8c9e-e3a959de45f5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808a-853c-dbe2125c9838" class=""><strong>2. Resource Limit</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8093-bef3-ff6d43d1c16a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Definition:</strong> The <strong>maximum amount of CPU/memory</strong> a container can use.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-b4f5-f70de5a3e15b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prevents a container from <strong>hogging Node resources</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-ada1-d46393611c15" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8044-8ab3-fcc0698c2a7f" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">resources:
  limits:
    cpu: &quot;1&quot;
    memory: &quot;512Mi&quot;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803e-a629-f28c31e1ae95" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The container <strong>cannot exceed 1 CPU core or 512Mi memory</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8089-8c6c-ffd0f00b5602"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-b36b-fc73a9f1aa3b" class=""><strong>Behavior</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-87b9-e2148ddd80c2" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-890b-f9d058b5a8c3"><th id="BeSm" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Scenario</strong></th><th id="A=rl" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>CPU</strong></th><th id="Ut_|" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Memory</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-a939-c1a9a236b589"><td id="BeSm" class="">Exceed Request</td><td id="A=rl" class="">Pod may use more CPU temporarily</td><td id="Ut_|" class="">N/A</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-8da5-c320cff5a713"><td id="BeSm" class="">Exceed Limit</td><td id="A=rl" class="">CPU throttled</td><td id="Ut_|" class="">Pod killed (OOMKilled)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8037-a108-fc63497a6f9d"><td id="BeSm" class="">Scheduler Placement</td><td id="A=rl" class="">Considers <strong>requests</strong>, not limits</td><td id="Ut_|" class="">Considers <strong>requests</strong>, not limits</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-88cf-e44b4758d0d4"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804d-90a5-f0be954cb24c" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8035-899d-c9a09d89ccef" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Requests = <strong>what a container is guaranteed</strong> ‚Üí Scheduler uses it.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8000-8e48-c79f381a171e" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>Limits = <strong>what a container is allowed to consume</strong> ‚Üí Runtime enforces it.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8004-b845-d7cba8ea288e" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Helps prevent <strong>resource contention</strong> and <strong>cluster instability</strong>.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-a423-d12b7f042760"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-af9a-e9c1dc5b283b" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8044-ba0c-f0023c6cca6d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Requests = <strong>reserved seat on a bus üöå</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809c-8972-d016cb856c0e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Limits = <strong>maximum weight allowed per passenger ‚öñÔ∏è</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8011-94e2-ed28d1d4d91e"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8092-8773-e2c3e87b8982" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-801f-ac99-c2111eacdb73" class=""><em>Kubernetes uses resource requests to guarantee CPU and memory for Pods during scheduling, and resource limits to cap their usage, ensuring efficient and fair allocation of cluster resources.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8042-85a6-fc00c5d9377b" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 49:</strong> What is the role of a Kubernetes ingress resource?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8006-abeb-f995cae7d4d0" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Ingress Resource</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-87e5-e75f5a620189" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">An <strong>Ingress</strong> is a Kubernetes resource that <strong>manages external access to Services</strong>, typically via HTTP and HTTPS.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8012-8af5-d7050e392e32" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It acts as a <strong>layer 7 (application layer) router</strong> inside the cluster.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80da-958d-ea31fe31b7f9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8010-a858-cb8a843a1e9f" class=""><strong>Key Roles</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-9268-d4a433b45283" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Routing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8030-a57a-ed5faba02499" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Routes requests to the correct Service based on:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80df-ae51-c70e1a39209c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Hostname (<code>host</code>)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-a85d-f88adc9ec597" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">URL path (<code>path</code>)</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-8756-cb9838e2f060" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>TLS/SSL Termination</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8084-a516-d71690781590" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can manage HTTPS traffic by terminating TLS at the Ingress controller.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805b-8d4b-da98e34093d8" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Centralized Access</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-b950-f7fbb1f63ee0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Provides a <strong>single entry point</strong> for multiple Services, reducing the need for multiple LoadBalancers.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8002-b3b1-f4ae8476985b" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Advanced Features</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8058-b5bf-c1ade6e42d73" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can implement <strong>URL rewrites, redirects, authentication, and rate limiting</strong> (via Ingress Controller).</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8097-9559-ebbf52be7c03"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804d-9e92-d7a549589614" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-802c-bd83-efd443815e1e" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Ingress
metadata:
  name: my-ingress
spec:
  rules:
  - host: myapp.example.com
    http:
      paths:
      - path: /api
        pathType: Prefix
        backend:
          service:
            name: my-service
            port:
              number: 80
  tls:
  - hosts:
    - myapp.example.com
    secretName: tls-secret

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8087-9fdb-f288ffa5aef2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Requests to <code>myapp.example.com/api</code> are routed to <code>my-service</code> on port 80.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8097-8050-cc355348ddea" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">TLS is handled using <code>tls-secret</code>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8036-a455-f8a6f60e9c96"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8016-8989-ee34a846a49e" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8019-bb98-eb0b9bd92a81" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Create an Ingress resource.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-9175-f8a6f92ec1a4" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>Deploy an <strong>Ingress Controller</strong> (e.g., NGINX, Traefik, HAProxy).</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8038-a27f-cb345b629552" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Controller monitors the Ingress resource and <strong>configures routing rules</strong> for incoming traffic.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-b332-e08fcc318817"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-ae30-eb0de6563068" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-83a6-e26a1825c280" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ingress = <strong>reception desk of a building üè¢</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-807d-bad1-f6078013ae4e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Visitors come in one door, and the receptionist directs them to the correct office (Service) based on their request (URL/host).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8080-a572-f2dca20ed355"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8037-be9d-ddf3684a1616" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a345-ce02d3fdf73d" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Ingress resource manages external HTTP/HTTPS access to Services, providing routing, TLS termination, and centralized entry for multiple Services in the cluster.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80ef-80ee-c9b7e130f452" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 50:</strong> Explain how Kubernetes handles service discovery.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80dc-be33-d05f59e9fda0" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Service Discovery</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-9d58-fcf8a297ea0c" class="">Kubernetes provides <strong>mechanisms to let Pods find and communicate with each other</strong> without hardcoding IPs.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8006-b635-dcd77c3e51d0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-9b5d-fcc81ecd9be4" class=""><strong>Mechanisms</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-a2d7-c53f6483d72e" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>DNS-Based Service Discovery (Default)</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-b1af-e351f779e8bd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes runs a <strong>DNS add-on</strong> (like CoreDNS).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-9b98-f3c162a184b1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Every Service gets a <strong>DNS name</strong>:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-9dde-ce51c680f08f" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">&lt;service-name&gt;.&lt;namespace&gt;.svc.cluster.local

</code></pre></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8060-9b47-f0cf1323679f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods can use this DNS name to reach the Service regardless of the Pod IPs behind it.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-a4e3-e441812155f4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8050-9c66-c69b4e149faf" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">curl http://my-service.default.svc.cluster.local:80

</code></pre></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803a-8a02-cc2b5dacc836" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Environment Variables</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8062-a4fe-ceb7ccec18cc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">When a Pod starts, Kubernetes injects <strong>environment variables</strong> for Services in the same namespace:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-9940-f2fcf2ba9ae0" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">MY_SERVICE_SERVICE_HOST=10.0.0.42
MY_SERVICE_SERVICE_PORT=80

</code></pre></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80dc-baf3-c37c9a84c106" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for legacy applications that rely on env variables.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-9eb6-f380847f4905" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Kubernetes Services</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-94db-dfbaba420586" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Services (ClusterIP, NodePort, LoadBalancer) provide a <strong>stable endpoint</strong> (virtual IP) for Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-af2f-e00e52f66b93" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods behind the Service can scale dynamically, but the Service IP remains constant.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8020-a18b-c479a844e3bf"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8010-b4a9-f98c6e966291" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-ba62-ca8bd786f4e3" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>Pods register implicitly when a Service selects them via <strong>labels</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-809c-8494-dcf099291316" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>Service maintains a <strong>list of active Pods</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8018-ac28-dfe245c5469e" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>DNS or ClusterIP resolves the Service name to one of the Pods (usually via <strong>round-robin load balancing</strong>).</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8093-ac3a-d88458971e77"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-bf71-ce9b31a97b35" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8033-8d6e-cd76800758ea" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Service discovery = <strong>company directory üìû</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8003-8bc6-da78539adc77" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Employees (Pods) can call a department (Service) by name, not by individual desk numbers (Pod IPs), even if desks change.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8071-a374-ecc0ffe994cc"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-875b-f99deae5e06f" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8043-9fcb-e63c84ffa238" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles service discovery via DNS names and environment variables, allowing Pods to find and communicate with Services through stable endpoints, even as Pod IPs change dynamically.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8088-87da-e6bd0a81e278" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 51:</strong> What is the purpose of a Kubernetes readiness probe?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ab-932d-ea9cfa7d15ed" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Readiness Probe</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c7-ab22-c4e83fbd739e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>readiness probe</strong> determines whether a <strong>Pod is ready to accept traffic</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800d-a9ea-d1bb1043f7d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If the probe fails, <strong>the Pod is removed from the Service endpoints</strong>, so it does not receive requests.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8018-a9e3-ee745f1c6ee0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80da-bca1-cd5ea5ed6297" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-a897-ebfb9f93582c" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Purpose</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8058-ae81-eafd993321c1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures only <strong>healthy and ready Pods</strong> receive traffic.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80be-af00-c67eed962f11" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful when a container is <strong>running but not yet initialized</strong> (e.g., warming up cache, loading configuration).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-890e-ef39519182e8" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Probe Types</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-9e98-ce8e16d95445" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>HTTP GET</strong>: Sends an HTTP request to a specific endpoint.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-8f2a-c3fc7420ec82" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>TCP Socket</strong>: Checks if a TCP port is open.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8096-8360-c4071d98e1a3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Exec</strong>: Runs a command inside the container; success indicates readiness.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805b-998c-ff845338341e" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Example YAML</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8016-9cb6-f4a6b79bae00" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">readinessProbe:
  httpGet:
    path: /healthz
    port: 8080
  initialDelaySeconds: 5
  periodSeconds: 10

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-821e-f212b1458396" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Checks <code>/healthz</code> every 10 seconds after waiting 5 seconds initially.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8055-8282-ccc6d201b312" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pod is marked ready only if the probe succeeds.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8057-90f2-d2c263e93ab4" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Difference from Liveness Probe</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-8bb3-c64ec742ac86" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Readiness</strong> ‚Üí Traffic routing decision.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8064-96a0-d46cf773116a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Liveness</strong> ‚Üí Container restart decision.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804b-a47c-da893515cb37"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-a472-ed753624ed86" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-bb57-fef0d55231e2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Readiness probe = <strong>restaurant ‚ÄúOpen‚Äù sign üçΩÔ∏è</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8078-b89d-ee256ee9504d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">If the kitchen isn‚Äôt ready yet, the sign stays off and customers (traffic) don‚Äôt enter.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806d-9dc4-f47ae3715fe4"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e9-a520-cd3ecd3f0aea" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8086-ba9c-c61d02cd2f87" class=""><em>A Kubernetes readiness probe checks whether a Pod is ready to serve traffic and removes it from Service endpoints if it is not, ensuring only fully initialized containers receive requests.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8087-9035-e221725572c8" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 52:</strong> How do you scale a deployment in Kubernetes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-9162-d495230ebf9e" class=""><strong>Scaling a Deployment in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-808b-b00f-ddc37fac6b92" class="">You can scale a Deployment <strong>manually or automatically</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8062-830a-e2564a33d5eb"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-b244-dd64f6cb3375" class=""><strong>1. Manual Scaling</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ed-9cae-f3860fc92b4e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Change the number of Pod replicas directly.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800f-ba83-f50ceefd00e7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Command:</strong></li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8006-b673-c2d67c0ea9f3" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl scale deployment &lt;deployment-name&gt; --replicas=&lt;number&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-a08a-fcb57a3da6c4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8096-a8cd-e26b81bbd785" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl scale deployment nginx-deployment --replicas=5

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-873c-ea7fdb87d3a2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">This will increase/decrease the number of Pods managed by the Deployment.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8008-9a8e-fa365de847ea"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-803a-9705-d4e993090498" class=""><strong>2. Declarative Scaling</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8018-95c5-fcf9605955ac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Update the <strong>Deployment manifest</strong> (<code>replicas</code> field) and apply changes:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8094-b605-c732d779b424" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: nginx-deployment
spec:
  replicas: 5
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: nginx
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: nginx
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: nginx
        image: nginx:latest

</code></pre><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80bd-9fc0-cc3d0ff7da0b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl apply -f deployment.yaml

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-b4e7-c5995d5626b8"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806e-bc70-c230cf1ac91d" class=""><strong>3.
