Automatic Scaling</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-8839-f29492eba929" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA)</strong> to scale Pods based on metrics like CPU or memory:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8066-99eb-c731dae951d4" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl autoscale deployment nginx-deployment --cpu-percent=50 --min=2 --max=10

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800a-b854-d6e4696f8527" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes automatically adjusts the number of replicas between <code>min</code> and <code>max</code> based on CPU usage.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8050-8c62-c0c52716f39b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-850b-c7e4b70c6e7b" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8036-a19e-e889643f0442" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scaling changes are <strong>managed by the Deployment controller</strong>, ensuring Pods are created or terminated safely.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8066-adaf-d6628fb61910" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works seamlessly with <strong>readiness probes</strong>, so traffic only goes to ready Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800a-88c3-d673caa196ce" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can be combined with <strong>Cluster Autoscaler</strong> to add/remove nodes if resources are insufficient.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802e-abba-d462c14240d3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80de-a361-c324a7a03aab" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-9efc-e84e4a689197" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scaling a Deployment = <strong>adding/removing cashiers üè™</strong> depending on customer load.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8001-a976-f17565e6bf7b"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8065-b494-db4b7298c611" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-a190-ebab61e8e7cd" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Deployment can be scaled manually using </em><em><code>kubectl scale</code></em><em>, declaratively by updating the replicas in the manifest, or automatically via Horizontal Pod Autoscaler based on resource usage metrics.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80ba-b5ae-cb3ef57e2fde" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 53:</strong> What is the difference between a Kubernetes Service and an Ingress?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-bffb-d90a7e22f5a0" class=""><strong>Difference Between a Kubernetes Service and an Ingress</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-abdd-f0fde0085b2a" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8035-95c4-e99f5910dfc6"><th id="Iu|^" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="QY\|" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:269px"><strong>Kubernetes Service</strong></th><th id="T&gt;DS" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:254.796875px"><strong>Kubernetes Ingress</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-807a-b7ab-cc60f3711fb8"><td id="Iu|^" class="">Purpose</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">Provides a <strong>stable internal or external endpoint</strong> for Pods</td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">Manages <strong>external HTTP/HTTPS access</strong> to Services</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-807b-ac4c-fd0f2e3c60fd"><td id="Iu|^" class="">Layer</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">L4 (Transport Layer: TCP/UDP)</td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">L7 (Application Layer: HTTP/HTTPS)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-9aea-ce022151848a"><td id="Iu|^" class="">Exposure</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">Can expose Pods internally (ClusterIP) or externally (NodePort, LoadBalancer)</td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">Exposes multiple Services via a <strong>single entry point</strong> with routing rules</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-b765-c3e53f2cc67c"><td id="Iu|^" class="">Routing</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">Basic routing to Pods based on <strong>labels</strong></td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">Advanced routing based on <strong>hostnames and paths</strong></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-a16a-f7a940ba87d3"><td id="Iu|^" class="">TLS/SSL Termination</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">Not supported natively</td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">Supported via Ingress Controller</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-b4ea-e6f07f5442a1"><td id="Iu|^" class="">Complexity</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">Simple</td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">More complex; requires Ingress Controller</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8001-a195-c3fbeaf8ad92"><td id="Iu|^" class="">Example Use Case</td><td id="QY\|" class="" style="width:269px">Expose a database, cache, or microservice internally</td><td id="T&gt;DS" class="" style="width:254.796875px">Route <code>myapp.com/api</code> to one Service and <code>myapp.com/web</code> to another</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8075-8abe-e5f9578305e0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-9909-c8842969be64" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803c-861e-d5fc2ab03ed7" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Service</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-b954-ca3c0a0fbdd8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Provides <strong>stable IP or DNS name</strong> for Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-8d35-f73bd26f5cff" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Handles <strong>internal or basic external traffic</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8060-b46d-f57b3b9f308b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Types: <code>ClusterIP</code>, <code>NodePort</code>, <code>LoadBalancer</code>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-9139-ead071b1cc3c" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Ingress</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807e-b2cd-c6eebbf0abe6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Provides <strong>centralized routing</strong> for multiple Services.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800d-ba6d-cfc16398eb71" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Handles <strong>HTTP(S) traffic</strong>, TLS termination, and host/path-based routing.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-88ff-d28a48133b44" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Requires an <strong>Ingress Controller</strong> (like NGINX, Traefik, or Istio).</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8079-9fbe-cfac53c5efd3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-b286-c86a6a87a095" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-a938-df058a6e1458" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Service = <strong>individual taxi üöï for each passenger</strong>, giving them a stable ride.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8072-a99b-d96dad613957" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ingress = <strong>taxi dispatcher üè¢</strong>, routing passengers to the correct taxi based on destination (host/path).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8011-85e5-c259cfecb44a"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-802d-b146-fe14a1a6e67b" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-9c8e-d2ac00f67727" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Service provides stable endpoints to access Pods and can handle internal or external traffic, while an Ingress manages external HTTP/HTTPS traffic with advanced routing, TLS, and centralized access to multiple Services.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-803e-a956-c89a18456de0" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 54:</strong> Explain the concept of &quot;Kubernetes namespaces&quot; and their use cases.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8098-97b1-c89f7409284c" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Namespaces</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8017-8a51-de4bcf7f9dac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Namespace</strong> is a <strong>virtual cluster within a Kubernetes cluster</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808f-9063-e4521fdec34b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It allows you to <strong>organize resources</strong> (Pods, Services, ConfigMaps, etc.) and <strong>apply isolation</strong> between different environments or teams.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-83da-fdb775316268"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a518-edc06f8c646e" class=""><strong>Key Features</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-bd98-eabe0893944a" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Resource Isolation</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804f-9889-dc0fecef2428" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Namespaces provide a <strong>scope for names</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803f-83b0-e09ac1f7e58a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can have the same resource name in different namespaces:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8065-9a98-cf6f74713aa3" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">default/nginx
dev/nginx

</code></pre></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801c-84c9-e959d917470b" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Access Control</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8068-9c5e-c0e32180cd3b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Combine with <strong>RBAC</strong> to restrict user access to certain namespaces.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-b88e-e7724ecd3b5e" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Resource Quotas</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-9ae8-d864daa126f4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Limit CPU, memory, or number of Pods per namespace using <strong>ResourceQuota</strong> objects.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-9e1d-d037c37ea1b3" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Organization</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8031-b558-d4e3f10b7438" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for separating:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-b741-e64097d8fbba" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Development, testing, and production environments.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-b629-fcb05a6187f3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Different teams or projects.</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806a-91f6-d5eb71977744"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808d-95ef-d7c173de34af" class=""><strong>Common Namespaces</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80df-9c7c-f33c80905f7b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>default</code> ‚Üí Default namespace for user-created resources.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8027-9cc4-ed20fa5dc26b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kube-system</code> ‚Üí System Pods and components.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8090-a514-c12f39807e84" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kube-public</code> ‚Üí Public resources accessible to all users.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8084-ab42-e76f2753b7af"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808c-900c-db2d5b0f1d5e" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8008-be1b-f6375a1aebbd" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl create namespace dev
kubectl get pods -n dev
kubectl apply -f deployment.yaml -n dev

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8013-adfe-c464b17a1fcf"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8080-8fe5-f74c41e684a0" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8053-867a-f8210b09c181" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Namespace = <strong>office floors in a building üè¢</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d4-a426-cb322eb83cef" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Each floor (namespace) has its own rooms (resources) and rules, preventing interference with other floors.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803a-a963-fa08ffce342d"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-854b-c0e1ef6458f9" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-805e-8569-f9394e9ffde1" class=""><em>Kubernetes namespaces provide a way to divide cluster resources into virtual clusters for isolation, organization, access control, and resource management across teams or environments.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8048-a4b9-d2966d303a99" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 55:</strong> What is a Kubernetes daemon set, and when would you use one?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-b28b-c3971b12fe84" class=""><strong>Kubernetes DaemonSet</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-8569-c6a8b8449eb3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>DaemonSet</strong> ensures that <strong>a copy of a Pod runs on all (or selected) Nodes</strong> in a cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809e-b336-d52c43344395" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">When new nodes are added, Pods are automatically scheduled on them.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8077-8d71-f4ba2bf7c32d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">When nodes are removed, the Pods on those nodes are deleted.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-a637-f738859e582b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8099-9cd4-c76f8198d7e0" class=""><strong>Use Cases</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807c-b0ae-c0af2f87362e" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Node-level system services</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8060-9e17-f1a19d214723" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Monitoring agents (Prometheus Node Exporter, Datadog)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8066-a3d2-d2e06ce25463" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Log collectors (Fluentd, Filebeat)</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8067-8130-e736409cf570" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Network services</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809c-8481-f0cd08fb87ce" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">CNI plugins (Calico, Flannel)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-a0a4-f8fa1cd2a4a3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Proxy services</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-b813-cf8c8f9431d8" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Hardware-specific workloads</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804a-bb09-d80c5f013024" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">GPUs or specialized devices available on certain nodes</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-b93c-d958fbc3a9fb"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8037-aead-daf1d9b60e4a" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80af-bc4e-f2c77ce5f63e" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: fluentd-daemon
  namespace: kube-system
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: fluentd
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: fluentd
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: fluentd
        image: fluentd:latest

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-937b-cf4480a81dd6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">This ensures <strong>Fluentd runs on every node</strong> for log collection.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d4-b945-e64c4897f197"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808d-8379-c0ced5b4c002" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8029-b082-e295b0c0e8f6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Unlike Deployments, DaemonSets <strong>run exactly one Pod per node</strong> (unless affinity rules change that).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8075-bb27-e00f0e55262d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can target <strong>specific nodes</strong> using <strong>node selectors, labels, or taints/tolerations</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-a2a5-f95f77c9b5ac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for <strong>node-level monitoring, logging, or network infrastructure tasks</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-8fef-e6e46e5d2908"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-9715-ff636ec4a2a3" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-8ef9-ffcd8b932ab2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">DaemonSet = <strong>a cleaning robot assigned to every room in a hotel üè®</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-903a-dc0bcaf12ccd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Each room (node) automatically gets a robot (Pod).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-84f3-c1dce09425b3"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8071-a6bf-e10f3110f1e3" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-809b-b7f2-f1c9880255b9" class=""><em>A Kubernetes DaemonSet ensures that a specific Pod runs on all or selected nodes, typically for node-level services like monitoring, logging, or networking.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-804c-acb2-cc3b749fd752" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 56:</strong> How does Kubernetes handle logging and monitoring?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8006-839a-fb1ca2f8bf40" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Logging and Monitoring</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-804b-a16a-e421b53123f6" class="">Kubernetes provides mechanisms to <strong>collect, centralize, and visualize logs and metrics</strong> from Pods, nodes, and cluster components.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8031-95fc-cc1dfd470a44"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8014-807c-e61382267482" class=""><strong>1. Logging</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-8440-cf8cacaeaa21" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Pod Logs</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-b16a-d3c8fccf2a13" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Each container writes logs to <strong>stdout and stderr</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-8653-dd6ad6a7a599" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Access logs using:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-807e-8829-ffcd06d4a1e6" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl logs &lt;pod-name&gt;

</code></pre></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8061-8b92-f39a79ed5b1f" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Cluster-Level Logging</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-ae00-daf9196ef1ef" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>log collectors</strong> to aggregate logs from all nodes and containers:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8026-8336-d23ded4811b2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Fluentd</strong> / <strong>Fluent Bit</strong> ‚Üí Collect and forward logs</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8053-a892-e1d5431ec206" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>ELK Stack</strong> (Elasticsearch, Logstash, Kibana) ‚Üí Store, search, and visualize logs</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806f-991f-f625a14d3b8d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Loki + Grafana</strong> ‚Üí Lightweight logging solution</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807e-befd-f40faa69b861" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Audit Logs</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-8180-edd09195c7e3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Track <strong>API access and cluster changes</strong> for security and compliance.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8000-8c4b-f932741e0bc2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8095-9055-f170c2a2f698" class=""><strong>2. Monitoring</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8081-a933-c69b8259c763" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Metrics Collection</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-921f-fad708fcd6e5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>CPU, memory, disk, network usage</strong> at Pod and node levels.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-8ce2-cb744f584a81" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Tools:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8063-aa95-c2135517e65e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Metrics Server</strong> ‚Üí Provides metrics for <code>kubectl top</code></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8048-a0c1-c52d4e55f792" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Prometheus</strong> ‚Üí Collects and stores metrics for alerting and visualization</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8026-b870-cc9bf9d4f5ce" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Health Checks</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8021-a703-f3a8ead11450" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Liveness probes</strong> ‚Üí Ensure containers are running</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-9b29-c9aa019547a7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Readiness probes</strong> ‚Üí Ensure Pods are ready to serve traffic</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-9b18-ecccd0e3a238" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Visualization</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801c-a6b0-ebe605b4707e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Grafana</strong> ‚Üí Dashboards for metrics and trends</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8003-a32c-c39e52adc9fa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Kubernetes Dashboard</strong> ‚Üí Basic cluster monitoring</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8020-8527-f69d9fee0a10" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Alerting</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-b991-edd054d0776a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prometheus Alertmanager or third-party tools notify teams about <strong>high CPU, memory usage, or Pod failures</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801b-b899-c03dbba55747"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-8e7b-f8cb87d17789" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8097-a75a-c40958310df5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Logging = <strong>keeping a diary of all actions in a company üìù</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801a-a44e-f8d9389d8b7c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Monitoring = <strong>a live dashboard with gauges and alarms üö®</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808d-a6a4-ff5f98389c7c"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-85a1-c73d2d4bbf38" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-8745-d5a3456e2757" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles logging by collecting container stdout/stderr logs and aggregating them via log collectors like Fluentd, while monitoring is done using metrics (Metrics Server, Prometheus), health probes, dashboards (Grafana), and alerts for observability and troubleshooting.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8021-adaa-f48c51bf3c17" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 57:</strong> What is the difference between a Kubernetes Job and a CronJob?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bd-bbe1-c3404fc87c5c" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Job vs CronJob</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8043-a872-da0e204ea9c7" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8003-9fbf-e98a17a0cadf"><th id=";Wvn" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="?fDN" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Job</strong></th><th id="_WPI" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>CronJob</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8064-af0d-ee993e65b967"><td id=";Wvn" class="">Purpose</td><td id="?fDN" class="">Run a <strong>one-time task</strong> to completion</td><td id="_WPI" class="">Run <strong>scheduled tasks</strong> repeatedly</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-808e-83df-c4137b0498db"><td id=";Wvn" class="">Execution</td><td id="?fDN" class="">Executes <strong>once</strong> until successful completion</td><td id="_WPI" class="">Executes <strong>repeatedly</strong> based on a schedule</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8039-91c1-e13c90e2594a"><td id=";Wvn" class="">Scheduling</td><td id="?fDN" class="">No schedule; triggered manually or by a controller</td><td id="_WPI" class="">Uses <strong>cron format</strong> (e.g., <code>0 0 * * *</code>)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8041-8622-f3b984649a5d"><td id=";Wvn" class="">Example Use Case</td><td id="?fDN" class="">Database migration, batch processing</td><td id="_WPI" class="">Daily backup, periodic report generation</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8057-bc6a-d242cc73a005"><td id=";Wvn" class="">Controller</td><td id="?fDN" class="">Job Controller manages Pods until completion</td><td id="_WPI" class="">CronJob Controller creates Jobs at scheduled times</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-802c-93f9-ea67c8be5d2a"><td id=";Wvn" class="">Pod Lifetime</td><td id="?fDN" class="">Ends when task completes</td><td id="_WPI" class="">Each scheduled run creates a new Job/Pod</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805b-bced-c6ac0c750dbd"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8052-a6b1-c245a92d11af" class=""><strong>Example: Job</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8061-be00-d35b9298a224" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: db-migration
spec:
  template:
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: migrate
        image: my-migration-image
      restartPolicy: OnFailure

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8051-81cc-c6092d9c968a" class=""><strong>Example: CronJob</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8027-9180-e2ebb1e8d372" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: CronJob
metadata:
  name: daily-backup
spec:
  schedule: &quot;0 2 * * *&quot;  # Runs daily at 2 AM
  jobTemplate:
    spec:
      template:
        spec:
          containers:
          - name: backup
            image: backup-image
          restartPolicy: OnFailure

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8023-991b-e06c09d64fa2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806b-81dd-c15874948cb9" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8046-bf61-c7f635be7de7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Job</strong> = one-time task; ensures <strong>completion</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-8641-c3186f26240d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>CronJob</strong> = scheduled task; creates Jobs automatically based on <strong>cron schedule</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-a93a-e3c0e088f45d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Both support <strong>retries</strong> if Pods fail (<code>restartPolicy: OnFailure</code>).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8058-ad24-d23d75e10d71"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8005-937f-ed3a89a4f73c" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8082-94ce-ee27a8e5f6ca" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Job = <strong>sending a single email üì®</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806c-abd7-f8e06f3e86c6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">CronJob = <strong>sending daily email newsletter üóìÔ∏è</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d0-9198-c8b041b8cd3a"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-806d-bbac-d0baabc52464" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-808e-b6ae-d469ed20dac6" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Job runs a task to completion once, while a CronJob runs tasks on a scheduled basis repeatedly, creating Jobs automatically according to the cron schedule.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80f6-9e47-dd2d289e0de8" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 58:</strong> What is the function of the Kubernetes kube-proxy?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8086-840b-fe2fcd5da94a" class=""><strong>Kubernetes kube-proxy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-9093-f645d208d757" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>kube-proxy</strong> is a <strong>network proxy</strong> that runs on each node in a Kubernetes cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80de-9df5-f2d0c7446e59" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It maintains <strong>network rules</strong> to allow <strong>Pods to communicate with Services</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-9673-dc22a4e6667a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-9b7c-df5a7fec92a8" class=""><strong>Functions of kube-proxy</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-96fb-ddc47631297d" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Service Load Balancing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8071-b7f6-c16a7af45f62" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Distributes traffic to Pods backing a Service, typically using <strong>round-robin</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-8828-c90d56913365" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures <strong>stable access</strong> to Service endpoints despite Pod changes.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8085-8bc9-c3c012aa0735" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Network Routing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803c-b83f-dcc983c12d45" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Uses <strong>iptables, IPVS, or userspace proxying</strong> to route traffic from Service IP to Pod IPs.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8048-9007-fe43b86647fb" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Pod-to-Pod Communication</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800a-ba82-c2bc9f20b7b1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Enables Pods to <strong>reach other Pods across nodes</strong> via ClusterIP or NodePort.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-b82e-cb4d49bd3dd9" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Maintains Service Endpoints</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809c-b3fc-facc68d1ff3c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Monitors the Kubernetes API for changes to Services and endpoints, updating routing rules automatically.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8043-857a-d244d9e56ab6"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8051-9b96-ceb29f90ef26" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-bc4f-c40ed2e1c71e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">When a Pod sends a request to a Service IP:<ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8077-b839-ef958d547685" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>kube-proxy intercepts the request.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8089-a993-f27e2e778325" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>Routes the request to one of the backend Pods based on the chosen algorithm.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8032-8ca5-caa9e90f31cc" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Handles changes in Pod availability dynamically.</li></ol></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8029-8c2b-fb9facabf9af"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-807d-b794-f06a004fa327" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80be-8a58-eb13ac0e3d6e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kube-proxy = <strong>traffic cop üö¶</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-8183-f2df9ec5fa1f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Directs network traffic from a stable address (Service) to the correct destination (Pod), even as destinations change.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8092-9993-de1b9280f703"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8055-9085-e642c714c8c7" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8043-b167-c5ce47d05099" class=""><em>Kube-proxy runs on each node to maintain network rules, enabling communication between Pods and Services, performing load balancing, and routing traffic to the correct backend Pods dynamically.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80f3-a2bf-cb68db3ef7ed" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 59:</strong> How do you manage configuration and secrets in Kubernetes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8080-b874-c347b3fad1c2" class=""><strong>Managing Configuration and Secrets in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8075-bf73-e65f53b440fb" class="">Kubernetes provides <strong>ConfigMaps</strong> and <strong>Secrets</strong> to manage configuration and sensitive data separately from application code.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8007-a0aa-f298d8ebc4f6"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8092-b94f-dd02905ac08c" class=""><strong>1. ConfigMap</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-b2cd-f478f3ef2d9e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Store <strong>non-sensitive configuration data</strong> (like environment variables, config files, or command-line arguments).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-9f8d-cf300c964b7c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can be <strong>mounted as files, environment variables, or command arguments</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-8a65-f2cff4b11186" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Example:</strong></li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-b682-db3611db9d86" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: app-config
data:
  DATABASE_HOST: db.example.com
  LOG_LEVEL: debug

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-b92a-ecb88a7d1c39" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use in Pod:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8005-b72a-cf5efcb29686" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">envFrom:
- configMapRef:
    name: app-config

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-8f7b-c0e1606f9cd3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8050-a36a-dac4670ce6d7" class=""><strong>2. Secret</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8030-8096-d73c4f29aa82" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Purpose:</strong> Store <strong>sensitive data</strong> (like passwords, API keys, tokens).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8059-81fb-c3794bdb0ae9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Stored <strong>base64-encoded</strong>, not plaintext.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-b144-ce7ac12eea58" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Example:</strong></li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8019-907f-dbe8aa05b10b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Secret
metadata:
  name: db-secret
type: Opaque
stringData:
  username: admin
  password: s3cr3t

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80da-b896-d6877626b4b6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use in Pod:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-994a-ed4bbe9222e1" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">envFrom:
- secretRef:
    name: db-secret

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8080-bcad-f5df241c938c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8028-85a7-ee078a0c9677" class=""><strong>3. Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8089-8877-df9cd10c0a60" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ConfigMaps</strong> ‚Üí non-sensitive data, can be updated without restarting Pods (if volume mounted).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8015-9231-ccf0fc68d5c1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Secrets</strong> ‚Üí sensitive data, should be encrypted at rest.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-ac59-e9ca2a363dab" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Both</strong> can be injected as:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8070-8967-eb47f7d8a0ad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Environment variables</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8088-ac78-d0930ccca291" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Mounted files in volumes</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-ac76-f98c78d4e9da" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Command-line arguments</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-9e33-c24d9a45ddbf"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8059-bf54-d5bdc5dbac64" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8040-a8f9-cd5234a2e161" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ConfigMap = <strong>instruction manual üìò</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-b525-cac8cb9408aa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Secret = <strong>safe with passwords üîí</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-ad9e-fd3e089d6532"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8010-807e-e959e5d528dc" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-809f-96a6-dad91b6e83ba" class=""><em>Kubernetes manages configuration using ConfigMaps for non-sensitive data and Secrets for sensitive data, which can be injected into Pods via environment variables, files, or command arguments.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80be-9048-ff4f36f1b58b" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 60:</strong> Explain the concept of &quot;Kubernetes pod disruption budgets.&quot;</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800e-895b-fdc4389c2eb6" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Pod Disruption Budget (PDB)</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-8123-c42e3c27885b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Pod Disruption Budget</strong> defines <strong>the minimum number or percentage of Pods that must remain available</strong> during voluntary disruptions (like node maintenance or scaling operations).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8021-904e-d0a3f2821f09" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It <strong>prevents too many Pods from being taken down simultaneously</strong>, ensuring service reliability.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805d-8e80-cf1f1712103d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800d-9732-c2fddc058368" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-804a-ab20-d03fc1d3a5d5" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Voluntary vs Involuntary Disruptions</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8057-845d-f8e0e806f432" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Voluntary</strong>: Admin actions (e.g., <code>kubectl drain</code>, rolling updates).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8094-908c-eb11dd8e996e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Involuntary</strong>: Node failure, hardware crash (PDB does <strong>not prevent</strong> these).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-82c4-df0b204833d7" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Specifying a PDB</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-abb2-e1beead0abcf" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>minAvailable</code>: Minimum number or percentage of Pods that must remain running.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8068-9aaa-de95be37aec8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>maxUnavailable</code>: Maximum number or percentage of Pods that can be unavailable.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8064-b377-d7d17bd81b6e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Only one of <code>minAvailable</code> or <code>maxUnavailable</code> is required.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-a1ac-e1450cf3b53f"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801d-8586-f7f27c8454ee" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-808a-bb93-cb4ced63c76c" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: policy/v1
kind: PodDisruptionBudget
metadata:
  name: myapp-pdb
spec:
  minAvailable: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: myapp

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-9850-d2c2114c33f4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures at least <strong>2 Pods</strong> of <code>myapp</code> are always running during disruptions.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8012-ab06-ef9c5f7f6b2a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805a-9bcc-f77958841762" class=""><strong>Use Cases</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-b3de-fb4edff741cc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensure <strong>high availability</strong> during node upgrades.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-8c20-d7d3702a6657" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prevent <strong>rolling updates from taking down too many replicas</strong> at once.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8004-b24e-d7df24aedc8c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Maintain <strong>SLA for critical applications</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-8847-f614d78a94c1"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8033-90d0-f780602c4757" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-a974-fae2a99c3364" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">PDB = <strong>fire drill rules in an office üè¢</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-b5fd-f79fe97a3f5b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Even if some employees leave (Pods disrupted), a minimum number must stay to keep operations running.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806b-a922-f1aab799ce67"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8021-b17b-f514b842b139" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80db-84cf-da4dacb5740b" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Pod Disruption Budget defines the minimum number or percentage of Pods that must remain available during voluntary disruptions, ensuring high availability of applications.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80b0-9021-e57300f61812" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 61:</strong> What is the purpose of the Kubernetes control plane components?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-a22c-f8c5e102783f" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Control Plane Components</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8060-85ba-d9825c60f204" class="">The <strong>control plane</strong> is responsible for <strong>managing the cluster, making global decisions, and maintaining the desired state</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801d-93ea-e1298f23c22d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-885e-d3fdf314f90b" class=""><strong>Key Components and Their Purpose</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8042-a62e-da4350912fc4" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8047-be67-e57007584f29"><th id="DEZk" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Component</strong></th><th id="yZeT" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Purpose</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-b2ef-c9266fbbf4fa"><td id="DEZk" class=""><strong>kube-apiserver</strong></td><td id="yZeT" class="">Frontend API server; handles all API requests and serves as the <strong>communication hub</strong> for the cluster.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-801b-a769-e7d32b94ab7c"><td id="DEZk" class=""><strong>etcd</strong></td><td id="yZeT" class="">Distributed key-value store; stores <strong>cluster state and configuration data</strong>.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-805d-af9c-d72421252bbf"><td id="DEZk" class=""><strong>kube-scheduler</strong></td><td id="yZeT" class="">Assigns Pods to nodes based on resource requirements, affinity rules, and constraints.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-800b-b892-e824faf48dbb"><td id="DEZk" class=""><strong>kube-controller-manager</strong></td><td id="yZeT" class="">Runs <strong>controllers</strong> that manage cluster state (e.g., Node controller, ReplicaSet controller, Job controller).</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8065-9021-c18182f7e47b"><td id="DEZk" class=""><strong>cloud-controller-manager</strong></td><td id="yZeT" class="">Manages cloud-specific components (like LoadBalancers, Node lifecycle) when running on a cloud provider.</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8033-b053-c99ea0cf6435"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-97f9-d7b3c5fb036a" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-8a1b-eaa787c022a0" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>User or automation submits a <strong>request</strong> to the kube-apiserver.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807b-ba81-d74c8de24cf4" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Scheduler</strong> assigns Pods to appropriate nodes.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8075-86b5-d9f85351d9b1" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Controller Manager</strong> ensures the cluster state matches the desired state.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-90a7-ef40d6a972ff" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>etcd</strong> persists all cluster data.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8056-bac8-dc9e0128b2f8" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li>Optional <strong>cloud-controller-manager</strong> integrates with cloud provider APIs.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8018-9ee2-f41f13290cea"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8091-b468-e73052e6cbab" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-a326-fa530121199e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Control Plane = <strong>mission control üöÄ</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-93ed-fdf9ee5102d1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">kube-apiserver = communications hub</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-9ea0-cfacea474a17" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Scheduler = mission planner</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8043-a538-fe024a51b94d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Controllers = operators ensuring tasks are completed</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-86b4-eeb3dd89d5d5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">etcd = mission log</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-930e-de6e8585e09f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80be-9915-e70d05f4b3e5" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-805d-9c81-de0bc159d308" class=""><em>The Kubernetes control plane consists of components like kube-apiserver, etcd, scheduler, and controller manager, which collectively manage cluster state, schedule workloads, and ensure the cluster operates according to the desired configuration.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80fd-9131-e6e9ce3a8a6f" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 62:</strong> How do you perform a canary deployment in Kubernetes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-a13d-f98a10b8894f" class=""><strong>Canary Deployment in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-bc7e-d21751d155e9" class="">A <strong>canary deployment</strong> is a strategy where a <strong>new version of an application is rolled out to a small subset of users or Pods first</strong>, while the majority of users continue using the stable version. This allows you to <strong>test the new version in production</strong> and <strong>monitor for errors</strong> before a full rollout.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-bb60-e965f3b1d9c0"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804f-b493-dace4b73134a" class=""><strong>Steps to Perform a Canary Deployment</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8085-8a41-cccfa99e52ad" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Deploy the Stable Version</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8063-abf0-fccf1bf822e5" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: myapp
spec:
  replicas: 5
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: myapp
      version: stable
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: myapp
        version: stable
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: myapp
        image: myapp:v1

</code></pre><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-b78c-c4e0d34b22df" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Deploy the Canary Version</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-9518-e12e9d497930" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: myapp-canary
spec:
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: myapp
      version: canary
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: myapp
        version: canary
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: myapp
        image: myapp:v2

</code></pre><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8063-b96a-c77b8e088271" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Update Service to Split Traffic</strong></li></ol><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-bc5f-e79c3eced6ed" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use a <strong>Service selector</strong> or an <strong>Ingress with weighted routing</strong> to send a <strong>small percentage of traffic</strong> to the canary Pods.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-9626-e1385b74c70e" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Monitor Metrics and Logs</strong></li></ol><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-b28b-f9a7d641795c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Check application performance, errors, and user experience.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-b0ba-f736e1109605" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Full Rollout</strong></li></ol><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-a674-d2cca15e5b65" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If stable, scale up canary and scale down the old version:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8047-a144-cfd0e3099a31" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl scale deployment myapp --replicas=0
kubectl scale deployment myapp-canary --replicas=5

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8070-924d-d68314de7407"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-bcd3-fd493e18d831" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8048-adc8-f269f0a3fcdd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Canary deployments <strong>reduce risk</strong> by gradually introducing changes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8052-9138-d3fc9eaf873b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Often combined with <strong>monitoring tools</strong> (Prometheus, Grafana) for automated validation.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-bf25-d3313dd355fa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can be implemented with <strong>multiple Deployments, Services, or Ingress weight-based routing</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-a445-c01d62c8dce6"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800c-89a8-c426c6677e58" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8081-a682-d8c1a291a631" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Canary deployment = <strong>sending a few beta testers üê§ before releasing a new app version to all users</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8026-ba12-dd72ea05f492"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-802e-b966-cb53cc575bd4" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-803a-bc42-cc12b1be46b1" class=""><em>A canary deployment in Kubernetes gradually rolls out a new version to a small subset of Pods, monitors performance, and then gradually shifts traffic to the new version to minimize risk.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-803d-a64e-f9331237110e" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 63:</strong> What is the difference between <code>kubectl apply</code> and <code>kubectl create</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8048-9d63-f39e794c3607" class=""><strong>Difference Between </strong><code><strong>kubectl apply</strong></code><strong> and </strong><code><strong>kubectl create</strong></code></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-9a8a-f461b9836d6f" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806f-b584-e5b3438d807a"><th id="Ze_x" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="=j{H" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>kubectl create</strong></th><th id="&lt;&lt;Wo" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>kubectl apply</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-aa6a-e780911580af"><td id="Ze_x" class="">Purpose</td><td id="=j{H" class="">Create a new resource <strong>from scratch</strong></td><td id="&lt;&lt;Wo" class="">Create or <strong>update a resource declaratively</strong></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8073-b2c4-fb30ec360b79"><td id="Ze_x" class="">Idempotency</td><td id="=j{H" class="">Not idempotent ‚Äî running it again will fail if resource exists</td><td id="&lt;&lt;Wo" class="">Idempotent ‚Äî can run multiple times without error; updates existing resources</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8073-a9e2-e8be5fd62444"><td id="Ze_x" class="">Use Case</td><td id="=j{H" class="">When you want to <strong>create a new Pod, Deployment, or Service</strong></td><td id="&lt;&lt;Wo" class="">When managing resources via <strong>version-controlled YAML manifests</strong></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-808f-af43-c405fe16fafb"><td id="Ze_x" class="">Example</td><td id="=j{H" class=""><code>kubectl create -f deployment.yaml</code></td><td id="&lt;&lt;Wo" class=""><code>kubectl apply -f deployment.yaml</code></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80bd-af86-d4ed98d0a59b"><td id="Ze_x" class="">Behavior on Existing Resource</td><td id="=j{H" class="">Fails if resource already exists</td><td id="&lt;&lt;Wo" class="">Updates resource to match YAML (merge changes)</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-81b9-e4192be1b6cf"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8092-a3fd-d8c25c1bafb7" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805f-90e3-e5056df4d11e" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>kubectl create</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-ad97-ef586db40807" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Used to <strong>create resources only once</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8097-8d3d-c40b176e053c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If resource exists ‚Üí <strong>error</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b5-af0e-f629c852c7f4" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>kubectl apply</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807b-b817-ff4fb5ce9407" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Uses <strong>declarative configuration</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-88c8-fe8b854dc976" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can <strong>update existing resources</strong> by merging YAML changes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-8e9a-daf9713e3ce3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Recommended for <strong>GitOps and CI/CD workflows</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-b2af-d8195c075358"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8002-b7c6-ee186b32e6ab" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805f-a49d-cbeb792ded2a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kubectl create</code> = <strong>painting a brand-new house üé®</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8026-872b-e039cfe543e1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>kubectl apply</code> = <strong>renovating an existing house üè†</strong> ‚Äî you can modify rooms or colors without demolishing it.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804c-a486-d915a4d166e6"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-bd87-f565c4a0b853" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-9629-d5340e5295b1" class=""><em><code>kubectl create</code></em><em> creates a resource from scratch and fails if it exists, while </em><em><code>kubectl apply</code></em><em> is declarative, idempotent, and can create or update existing resources based on the YAML manifest.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80a9-bd85-f8c434575917" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 64:</strong> What are the main differences between Kubernetes and Docker Swarm?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8071-8493-e85c19e707d5" class=""><strong>Differences Between Kubernetes and Docker Swarm</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-801d-8354-c786f9636a65" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8066-9da2-f3f686bc3b73"><th id="jnEb" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="&lt;Rcv" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Kubernetes</strong></th><th id="buzE" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Docker Swarm</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-803b-9801-f40a48567528"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Architecture</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Master-worker architecture with multiple control plane components</td><td id="buzE" class="">Simpler manager-worker architecture</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-802f-99b6-c08f150d9fce"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Installation</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">More complex; requires setting up control plane and worker nodes</td><td id="buzE" class="">Easier to set up; integrated with Docker CLI</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80c7-ad55-d2dd2f664955"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Scaling</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Supports <strong>automatic scaling</strong> (HPA, VPA, Cluster Autoscaler)</td><td id="buzE" class="">Manual scaling; limited auto-scaling features</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8038-b77f-e9b9b0112d09"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Networking</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Uses <strong>CNI plugins</strong>; supports advanced networking, service discovery, and network policies</td><td id="buzE" class="">Built-in overlay network; simpler, less flexible</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8041-b0d6-d488f198855e"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Load Balancing</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Built-in L4/L7 load balancing via Services and Ingress</td><td id="buzE" class="">Internal routing mesh for service load balancing</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8044-ae69-cee82f3f594d"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Storage</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Supports <strong>PersistentVolumes, StorageClasses</strong>; dynamic provisioning</td><td id="buzE" class="">Limited storage support; mostly Docker volumes</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-ab46-c1ec4e2a7353"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Self-Healing</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Automatic <strong>restart, reschedule, and replication</strong> of failed Pods</td><td id="buzE" class="">Basic self-healing; only restarts failed containers</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8056-a65d-e3e8f8c2eadc"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Community &amp; Ecosystem</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Large, active community; extensive ecosystem (Helm, Prometheus, Istio)</td><td id="buzE" class="">Smaller ecosystem; less widely adopted</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-bbc0-e595a384da62"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Updates &amp; Rollbacks</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Advanced strategies (rolling update, canary, blue-green)</td><td id="buzE" class="">Simple rolling updates; limited rollback options</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-b3ae-c45d739fb2aa"><td id="jnEb" class=""><strong>Use Cases</strong></td><td id="&lt;Rcv" class="">Large-scale, production-grade clusters, multi-cloud</td><td id="buzE" class="">Small clusters or simple deployments</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-806b-9a5e-e95e0af8da9e"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b9e8-c30578afbec4" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8002-a344-c6f24aed37c5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes is <strong>feature-rich, production-ready, and highly extensible</strong>, but more complex.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8059-9d3d-c045ea608551" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Docker Swarm is <strong>simpler, easier to set up</strong>, and suitable for <strong>smaller workloads or development environments</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-aa4e-e48e39d64c8e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes is the <strong>industry standard</strong>, especially for multi-cloud, microservices, and enterprise deployments.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-809f-b461-cdd3f15c3b69"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8027-bc93-dac81668116d" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-8a8b-e891b552b45d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes = <strong>air traffic control tower üõ´</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-80b7-c89bce9e0edb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Handles hundreds of flights, complex routing, and emergency handling.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8000-923e-e0c9a835dd1b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Docker Swarm = <strong>small regional airport üõ¨</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8023-8ac0-dca8cdc7d2d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Simple operations, fewer features, easier to manage.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-a2a2-ddaa7f1c3300"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-aa8a-cd741ffe1f4f" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-800c-befa-eec00cf15d22" class=""><em>Kubernetes is a complex, feature-rich container orchestration platform with advanced networking, scaling, and self-healing, while Docker Swarm is simpler, easier to set up, and suited for smaller clusters with basic orchestration features.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-806e-8715-d373bdb8a1d4" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 65:</strong> Explain how Kubernetes handles service discovery and DNS.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800b-9e51-e6d5a68210e9" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Service Discovery and DNS</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8020-bc43-c2694d17cc45" class="">Kubernetes provides <strong>built-in service discovery</strong> mechanisms so that Pods can communicate <strong>without knowing IP addresses</strong>, which can change dynamically.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-807c-a62c-e5f6b4de01e4"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-80d7-d58fdcc5a518" class=""><strong>1. DNS-Based Service Discovery</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8048-bab2-ce9d8a47c0f3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes runs a <strong>DNS add-on</strong> (like <strong>CoreDNS</strong>) inside the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-8451-c6872b54a94d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Every Service gets a <strong>DNS name</strong> in the form:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8095-bb9f-d6ca753bd950" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">&lt;service-name&gt;.&lt;namespace&gt;.svc.cluster.local

</code></pre></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-a8cf-c22c84605834" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods can use this DNS name to reach the Service:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-802e-beeb-d7c107ef0560" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">curl http://my-service.default.svc.cluster.local:80

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806b-9d54-e0c30fcefb1e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">DNS resolves the Service name to the <strong>ClusterIP</strong> and automatically routes traffic to available Pods.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8042-bc02-dbbf83b5eca5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-98b1-d96811301fdb" class=""><strong>2. Environment Variables</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801f-907d-e96611632289" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes injects <strong>environment variables</strong> for Services into Pods when they start:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-bcdf-ca9524b6f4e7" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">MY_SERVICE_SERVICE_HOST=10.0.0.42
MY_SERVICE_SERVICE_PORT=80

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8039-9ddb-fa69729e0599" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for legacy applications that rely on environment variables for configuration.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-809a-a174-ea1bf92abd4c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-9d45-f03270167ebd" class=""><strong>3. How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-8757-e79f7776d106" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Service creates a stable ClusterIP</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8095-9cc2-f1738f1ec157" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>CoreDNS watches the API server</strong> for Service and Pod changes.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8029-974a-ef7c0bd53a5d" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Pods query DNS</strong> to find the Service IP.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8018-8222-d7b7340c6074" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>kube-proxy routes traffic</strong> from the Service IP to the selected Pod(s).</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8098-a2e6-f5fad8d78e1c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-bfb2-fb155bd86608" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807d-a622-f45ecea80b1a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Pods do not need to know the IPs</strong> of other Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807e-8860-e42bdb9f91cc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>DNS names are stable</strong>, even if underlying Pods are replaced.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8001-93f3-f511d05880b9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works for <strong>internal communication</strong>; external traffic may require <strong>Ingress or LoadBalancer</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-9779-e27af45d8687"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-b726-f9b0fdd0d997" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8016-bf94-c094e1cea931" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Service discovery = <strong>company directory üìû</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-bd28-e5a7be5eb876" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Employees (Pods) call a department (Service) by name, not by individual desk numbers (Pod IPs), even if desks change.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-af36-c5fd9bad0d53"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8010-b917-d17b6a751c52" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-890d-ee78208afee9" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles service discovery via DNS names and environment variables, allowing Pods to find Services by stable names, while kube-proxy routes traffic to the correct Pods dynamically.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80b8-a263-c2a3c587130a" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 66:</strong> What is the purpose of the Kubernetes API server‚Äôs admission controllers?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-80ad-e8863843b55c" class=""><strong>Kubernetes API Server Admission Controllers</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-bf5b-ef7382498e56" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Admission controllers</strong> are <strong>plugins that intercept requests to the Kubernetes API server</strong> <strong>after authentication and authorization</strong>, but <strong>before the object is persisted</strong> in etcd.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-bffc-eccdbda9fc5f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">They can <strong>modify, validate, or reject requests</strong> to enforce policies and maintain cluster security and consistency.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8073-8440-f5b04d654d39"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-9d05-d47572d62eec" class=""><strong>Types of Admission Controllers</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-a54a-f01786fee694" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>ValidatingAdmissionWebhook</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8092-bd7b-e35737520a2b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Validates requests against custom policies.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809b-bb1f-e8faecbded28" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Reject Pods without specific labels.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8033-b8ba-e0076da3e686" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>MutatingAdmissionWebhook</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808b-812e-c0efcc97414d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Modifies requests before they are stored.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8025-a760-f074797826c2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Example: Automatically add default labels or inject sidecar containers (e.g., Istio sidecar).</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-802e-ae69-f4f83c2519eb" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Built-in Controllers</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8021-b6f6-c4a1d02bf603" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>NamespaceLifecycle</strong> ‚Üí Ensures resources aren‚Äôt created in terminating namespaces.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-9e8e-fd9842b0dc13" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ResourceQuota</strong> ‚Üí Enforces CPU/memory limits.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-8362-f446690545a3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>LimitRanger</strong> ‚Üí Sets default limits on Pods or containers.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-86d5-dd0519c31985" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>NodeRestriction</strong> ‚Üí Limits which nodes can be assigned to Pods.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8085-ac14-dcafbb06734d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-a71b-d186c55bb92c" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8096-8379-f21e51acb4fd" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>User sends a request to <strong>kube-apiserver</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-804b-bcee-dc383c701fb6" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>Request passes <strong>authentication ‚Üí authorization ‚Üí admission controllers</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-806e-9661-ee565e0fd8f7" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Admission controllers may <strong>modify, accept, or reject</strong> the request.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-a4c1-c754f7efa9a0" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li>If approved, the object is <strong>stored in etcd</strong> and acted upon by controllers.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803d-ae66-f53432dca71d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8015-8a4e-fbb8af5b6cfa" class=""><strong>Use
