Cases</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8077-ab7b-ded4e1edfb0d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Enforce <strong>security policies</strong> (e.g., no privileged containers).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-882c-d8f13ad9e520" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensure <strong>resource limits and quotas</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8064-8a98-de67baa22c34" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Automatically inject <strong>sidecar containers or labels</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8025-8389-e010c2d5dcf4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Reject misconfigured resources before they affect the cluster.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802a-8a7d-d342081aab4d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8068-972b-ce3497dff26b" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8077-a991-fb70029db087" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Admission controller = <strong>security checkpoint at an airport üõ´</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8035-b489-fcbc5dcb75a9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Passengers (requests) are screened, possibly redirected or stopped, before entering the plane (cluster).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-ad1b-f8da7472ce47"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-bb3a-faa017c59191" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-807e-8c45-fd5381a47ce0" class=""><em>Kubernetes API server admission controllers intercept API requests to validate, modify, or reject resources, enforcing security, policy, and cluster consistency before objects are persisted in etcd.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-801d-b806-e8edc1a0e6c1" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 67:</strong> How do you configure resource requests and limits for a pod?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-9083-e0895e495dde" class=""><strong>Resource Requests and Limits in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-804e-9169-e676df8fce89" class="">Kubernetes allows you to specify <strong>CPU and memory requirements</strong> for each container in a Pod:</p><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-806b-a2d8-caf4556b7df3" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Resource Requests</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-a386-cdce7d4dcd2e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>minimum resources</strong> a container needs.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-b570-d48e32f9f966" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes uses this for <strong>scheduling</strong> ‚Äî a Pod is placed on a node that has at least the requested resources.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8047-9f57-d20fd7e90e97" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Resource Limits</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8024-9dc5-fc3c9c26f17a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>maximum resources</strong> a container can use.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800f-9411-e2e62d88400f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes <strong>enforces limits</strong> using the container runtime. If a container exceeds the limit:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-8672-c9e6377f20ca" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">CPU: throttled</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-8d69-ff8553141498" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Memory: may be terminated (OOMKilled)</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-9c41-e0a726091bba"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-8ed4-c690009e6fe5" class=""><strong>Example YAML</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8046-a6dd-c1ea1b28570d" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
metadata:
  name: resource-demo
spec:
  containers:
  - name: myapp
    image: nginx
    resources:
      requests:
        memory: &quot;256Mi&quot;
        cpu: &quot;250m&quot;
      limits:
        memory: &quot;512Mi&quot;
        cpu: &quot;500m&quot;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8042-8a25-c70e751dcd3d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>requests</code> ‚Üí Pod will be scheduled on a node with at least 256Mi memory and 0.25 CPU.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802b-a3b5-eedbd5d2dacf" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>limits</code> ‚Üí Pod cannot exceed 512Mi memory and 0.5 CPU.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-800f-8f40-c55c41fe29fb"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8062-96fb-e94b0cec2121" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ab-9ba2-cd6978906a72" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helps <strong>prevent resource contention</strong> in the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-8cdd-f7d5c5965760" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Required for <strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler</strong> to work properly.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8077-9af8-da0909c93a15" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for <strong>QoS classification</strong>:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f0-8c82-f7529e570063" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-b8d9-e3c01db3e48c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800f-bf84-d2c1c6d80b23" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802b-99e8-c33e8e363865" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Requests = <strong>minimum ingredients ü•£</strong> to cook a dish</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8091-9e43-e6792f40f9ac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Limits = <strong>maximum ingredients üç≤</strong> you can use without overflowing</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-9def-fa4648bab79f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-9ccc-dd7131e39745" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-a858-f07d863566c5" class=""><em>Resource requests and limits in Kubernetes are specified per container in a Pod to define the minimum (requests) and maximum (limits) CPU and memory usage, ensuring proper scheduling and resource enforcement.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8016-9c14-e04765d3ba35" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 68:</strong> What is the significance of the Kubernetes API versioning?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80af-8bd5-e68a0ce686af" class=""><strong>Kubernetes API Versioning</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800c-9e7a-d10a16573d0d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes APIs are <strong>versioned</strong> to indicate the <strong>stability and maturity</strong> of a resource or feature.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801d-83a0-cf0035a51a78" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Versioning helps users and developers <strong>understand which APIs are safe to use</strong> and <strong>plan upgrades</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8097-9cb8-eaada544896c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804d-8c6b-f2969485d1e2" class=""><strong>Common API Versions</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805e-b000-fa9bf83d98bf" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>alpha</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8068-af8a-dff924ba3bd5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Early-stage features.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-80d7-dd0896af5bad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">May <strong>change or be removed</strong> in future releases.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8052-8316-fe28b6c3ae9f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Disabled by default in many clusters.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8013-85e8-e13941a890b2" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>beta</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a3-985a-d4e548fd4a8f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Features are <strong>more stable</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805f-bf5e-ffb9dd328e6a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can still change but generally <strong>safe to use in testing</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8021-a727-f8655c1c358f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Enabled by default.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8007-b23a-c9b0935d0aee" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>stable (v1)</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-80ed-cbe42aceca87" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Fully <strong>production-ready</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-8429-da60312b08a0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">API changes are <strong>backward compatible</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801e-b796-fff79d813a1d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-b287-f111a623a201" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80cd-8ba6-c7e4130d0c42" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: apps/v1   # stable
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: my-deployment
spec:
  replicas: 3
  template:
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: nginx
        image: nginx:latest

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-81a7-f4352189a924" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Older alpha versions (e.g., <code>extensions/v1beta1</code>) may be <strong>deprecated or removed</strong> in newer Kubernetes releases.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-9402-cbfc3f5de891"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8065-b44a-ef98c19f4bac" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-8968-f92c119113ad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">API versioning ensures <strong>cluster stability</strong> during upgrades.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-a3d9-c4232b32cc63" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Developers can choose features based on <strong>stability needs</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c1-9936-e174c5179d54" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deprecated APIs are <strong>phased out</strong> gradually with warning messages.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8063-8f76-d2188fc6f9f4"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8062-9c33-e732cced5ae3" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-abd2-d249a61e64e3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">API versioning = <strong>software release stages üì¶</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8058-8636-fc85373eef24" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Alpha = experimental</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8072-85cc-e722c4639b73" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Beta = testing</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-8132-e73ed7ece7cd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Stable = production-ready</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-b8a1-faf2f29ab644"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-804d-b7f6-d92f83cac4f2" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8086-ace8-c67e4da1fe14" class=""><em>Kubernetes API versioning indicates the stability and maturity of a resource or feature, helping users choose safe APIs, maintain backward compatibility, and plan cluster upgrades.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8099-a75e-c43e0f8324d8" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 69:</strong> Explain the concept of &quot;Kubernetes pod lifecycle.&quot;</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-a782-ea76136d49e9" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Pod Lifecycle</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-805a-9f45-f19a0c3975a3" class="">A Pod goes through <strong>several phases from creation to termination</strong>, which Kubernetes uses to manage its state.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-985d-ff5c9e51e05b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-807a-bd9a-c8b045db0f9c" class=""><strong>Pod Phases</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8080-bdd9-cdd9c72275e6" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8059-9d2d-c3d0a2925c88"><th id="^eFi" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Phase</strong></th><th id="uT:y" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Description</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80da-aca5-eeef1be2ffee"><td id="^eFi" class=""><strong>Pending</strong></td><td id="uT:y" class="">Pod has been accepted by the API server but <strong>not yet running</strong>. Images may still be pulling.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-b22f-da231be5fc4c"><td id="^eFi" class=""><strong>Running</strong></td><td id="uT:y" class="">Pod has been scheduled to a node, <strong>containers are running</strong>, and at least one is ready.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8058-a4e1-d98a1c6f13ce"><td id="^eFi" class=""><strong>Succeeded</strong></td><td id="uT:y" class="">All containers in the Pod have <strong>terminated successfully</strong>. No restart needed.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8066-b1c8-cfbf71a8f245"><td id="^eFi" class=""><strong>Failed</strong></td><td id="uT:y" class="">All containers have terminated, <strong>at least one failed</strong>, and will not restart.</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-b50b-cf9c2ca9c72c"><td id="^eFi" class=""><strong>Unknown</strong></td><td id="uT:y" class="">The <strong>state of the Pod cannot be determined</strong> (e.g., node failure or communication issues).</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808e-b401-c15d2a1e8f5f"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808d-9c6e-f7b22bdfa2e0" class=""><strong>Container Lifecycle Within a Pod</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-805c-83e9-f30cd9e143f9" class="">Containers have <strong>lifecycle hooks</strong> for managing initialization, running, and termination:</p><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-8d4a-feda7f8f1623" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>PostStart</strong> ‚Äì Executes immediately after container starts.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8046-90fa-dc357dcb4ff4" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>PreStop</strong> ‚Äì Executes before container termination for cleanup.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ca-9698-c77eee42fc2b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8043-a93d-e3775c526fe7" class=""><strong>Key Events</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8038-b122-f524d54d38dc" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Scheduled</strong> ‚Äì Pod assigned to a node by the scheduler.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-805d-bcf2-c66e1b956ebb" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Initialized</strong> ‚Äì Init containers (if any) have completed.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8017-9fd1-f1e88905ffff" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Ready</strong> ‚Äì Pod is ready to serve traffic (readiness probe passes).</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803b-a9a5-f8e39f1748cd" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Termination</strong> ‚Äì Pod deletion triggers shutdown hooks and container cleanup.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-afd6-d30c25d1a9af"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-a27d-f8339e63bd46" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-8185-dcfddc968bdc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pod lifecycle = <strong>life stages of a student üéì</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-a4de-db2b4d4d53a8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Pending = Admission accepted</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fa-bd0d-fa87ee14f92d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Running = Attending classes</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805b-a4a2-c06545519c57" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Succeeded = Graduated</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8053-8ee9-f4dd3526a7b1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Failed = Dropped out</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802b-8acb-fb74e8aa5017" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Unknown = Lost contact</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-93a5-c4a79365e9a4"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8066-85e7-d57da30f2eac" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-a91e-d350210d8cee" class=""><em>Kubernetes Pod lifecycle describes the phases a Pod goes through ‚Äî Pending, Running, Succeeded, Failed, or Unknown ‚Äî along with container lifecycle events to manage initialization, readiness, and termination.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8061-a457-ffc050d0b7a3" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 70:</strong> What are the key differences between Kubernetes and traditional virtual machines?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8017-b847-fe419e9d91d2" class=""><strong>Key Differences Between Kubernetes (Containers) and Traditional Virtual Machines (VMs)</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80de-b87a-d1bf5238eeab" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-80c8-fd53dbccf57f"><th id="Zm=k" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="tq_C" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:274px"><strong>Kubernetes / Containers</strong></th><th id="&lt;NOT" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:256.28125px"><strong>Traditional Virtual Machines</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-803f-b06b-cf66253e94aa"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Resource Overhead</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Lightweight; share OS kernel; fast startup</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Heavy; each VM has its own OS; slower boot</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8077-9542-ec5194314db1"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Isolation</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Process-level isolation using namespaces and cgroups</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Full OS-level isolation via hypervisor</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-9860-d6ce48740eaf"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Portability</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Highly portable; can run anywhere with container runtime</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Less portable; depends on hypervisor and OS</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-8d6e-f4821c1524a7"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Deployment Speed</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Very fast; seconds to start a container</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Slower; minutes to boot a VM</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-bc7b-e01520161b8a"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Scaling</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Easy and dynamic via Kubernetes scaling</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">More complex; requires provisioning new VMs</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8063-93da-ea527ee5a4b5"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Resource Utilization</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Efficient; multiple containers per host</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Less efficient; each VM has fixed overhead</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8060-b56b-fe268a10699a"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Management</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Managed via orchestrators like Kubernetes</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Managed via virtualization platforms (VMware, Hyper-V)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-9dbe-d59eb7358c0e"><td id="Zm=k" class=""><strong>Use Case</strong></td><td id="tq_C" class="" style="width:274px">Microservices, stateless apps, cloud-native</td><td id="&lt;NOT" class="" style="width:256.28125px">Legacy applications, full OS isolation required</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802a-909f-fea796f9fdf9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8049-a4db-de46f9a1a57e" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806e-92fe-e802723b5ba0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Containers focus on lightweight, fast, and portable applications</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8079-bd51-fb38392a95de" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>VMs provide full OS isolation</strong>, suitable for legacy workloads or security-critical applications.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-ade2-e1d7fc7ba089" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes orchestrates <strong>containers at scale</strong>, while traditional VMs are managed individually.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-87a5-c56d715c12cd"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-95ac-c4f8742bec9a" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-924c-deb6594ef679" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Containers = <strong>apartments in a building üè¢</strong> (share infrastructure efficiently)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8096-b864-e890b17376f2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">VMs = <strong>separate houses üè†</strong> (each with its own foundation and utilities)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80be-9bf1-caa47e29c228"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-82b9-c63375fcfca2" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-803a-b4ad-feaacfd03c4b" class=""><em>Kubernetes manages lightweight, portable containers with fast startup and efficient resource use, whereas traditional virtual machines provide full OS isolation but are heavier, slower to deploy, and less resource-efficient.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-804c-b2a1-ccf36d90934d" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 71:</strong> What is the role of the Kubernetes scheduler, and how does it make scheduling decisions?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-802b-880e-cfab8462e2b9" class=""><strong>Role of the Kubernetes Scheduler</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804c-9df4-e1e8156b2e4a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>Kubernetes scheduler</strong> is responsible for <strong>assigning Pods to nodes</strong> in the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-9c03-f6b4c7d94752" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It ensures that Pods are placed on nodes that <strong>meet resource requirements, constraints, and policies</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8037-9bc1-d7ff16364c7c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It runs after the <strong>API server accepts a Pod</strong> but before the Pod starts running.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808d-8fa5-f4758fc6a429"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-a81f-f8a95aeaff7c" class=""><strong>How Scheduling Decisions Are Made</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-aa0f-c15466981a43" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Filtering (Predicates)</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-9453-d6e93263fa7d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The scheduler first <strong>filters nodes</strong> that can run the Pod based on:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8052-bdcb-cdbb7449b741" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Resource requests (CPU, memory)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-ab7e-d94fb8ac8fc0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Node selectors and labels</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-bfa9-c6f5dbf165f7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Taints and tolerations</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8041-8cbd-efb9eb78e417" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Node affinity rules</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b5-ab54-f765a685f56e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Pod affinity/anti-affinity</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8095-acc3-ce6eea88eaa5" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Scoring (Priorities)</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-9d67-f126e5b248e5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Each eligible node is scored based on:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-8085-ae06-fbb1684b9712" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Least resource usage (spread Pods evenly)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8066-8c80-cf77022c84cb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Affinity/anti-affinity preferences</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-a30c-eb4a94b0bd94" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Custom scheduling policies</li></ul></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-95e6-c6b313a60776" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Binding</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8010-8053-f4db27feb7d5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scheduler chooses the <strong>best-scored node</strong> and binds the Pod to it.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805e-a0a6-c81b9077d5b0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kubelet on that node then <strong>creates the Pod‚Äôs containers</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b2-a07d-e23083423dff"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fa-93c0-da0a05c8b816" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80db-9872-ce3389c70cc8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scheduler only <strong>assigns Pods</strong>; it does <strong>not start containers</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-b0a3-eca0b04e8c28" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Supports <strong>custom schedulers</strong> for specialized workloads.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800b-9578-c80a6ee82efa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works with <strong>resource requests, limits, affinity, and taints/tolerations</strong> to ensure optimal placement.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80da-889e-e11fba4a90d2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a8-81b3-e2d320c6d7f2" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8028-8756-f4bfb022e2c7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scheduler = <strong>school principal assigning students to classrooms üè´</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8069-8ea4-e4f09dc3e869" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ensures each class has enough space, proper facilities, and students are distributed evenly.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-961f-dc4d22682ee5"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8076-88a9-c6731d53a805" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8043-aad8-d31abc69004d" class=""><em>The Kubernetes scheduler assigns Pods to suitable nodes by filtering nodes that meet resource and policy constraints, scoring them based on priorities, and binding the Pod to the optimal node for execution.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8059-a0fb-ffe2a834706f" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 72:</strong> Explain the difference between a Kubernetes <code>Secret</code> and a <code>ConfigMap</code>.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-b369-f06f8c2ee284" class=""><strong>Difference Between Secret and ConfigMap</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8075-9a9d-fe43552eafb0" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-9f6d-ca1434ad7294"><th id="a;sI" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="k]ul" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:290px"><strong>ConfigMap</strong></th><th id="RCVD" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:267px"><strong>Secret</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-803b-80c9-f8380c3d6f3b"><td id="a;sI" class=""><strong>Purpose</strong></td><td id="k]ul" class="" style="width:290px">Store <strong>non-sensitive configuration data</strong></td><td id="RCVD" class="" style="width:267px">Store <strong>sensitive data</strong> (passwords, tokens, keys)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ac-bba6-e9c67aace69e"><td id="a;sI" class=""><strong>Data Encoding</strong></td><td id="k]ul" class="" style="width:290px">Plaintext</td><td id="RCVD" class="" style="width:267px">Base64-encoded (adds minimal obfuscation)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-a408-df6e43d1d135"><td id="a;sI" class=""><strong>Use Case</strong></td><td id="k]ul" class="" style="width:290px">Environment variables, config files, command args</td><td id="RCVD" class="" style="width:267px">Passwords, API keys, TLS certificates</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806b-8f7f-e7b893f9ae5c"><td id="a;sI" class=""><strong>Access</strong></td><td id="k]ul" class="" style="width:290px">Mounted as env variables or files</td><td id="RCVD" class="" style="width:267px">Mounted as env variables, files, or imagePullSecrets</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-8bdf-ff7b25dfc2d6"><td id="a;sI" class=""><strong>Security</strong></td><td id="k]ul" class="" style="width:290px">No encryption by default</td><td id="RCVD" class="" style="width:267px">Can be encrypted at rest (with KMS or etcd encryption)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-804a-9f2d-eecc23ea92b7"><td id="a;sI" class=""><strong>Example Usage</strong></td><td id="k]ul" class="" style="width:290px">Database host, log level, feature flags</td><td id="RCVD" class="" style="width:267px">DB password, OAuth token, TLS private key</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8051-9c86-d44df1acc67e"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8049-894e-e557dc0e41a7" class=""><strong>Example ConfigMap</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-9fbe-f6b8ccb7b496" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: app-config
data:
  DATABASE_HOST: db.example.com
  LOG_LEVEL: debug

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8001-9470-ea11d2f62bfc" class=""><strong>Example Secret</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8004-bafe-f6f97ed7698f" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Secret
metadata:
  name: db-secret
type: Opaque
stringData:
  username: admin
  password: s3cr3t

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8074-a260-fd199077f938"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8018-85bb-d6abcebf7ab5" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-a121-de0e209fdfaa" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ConfigMaps</strong> = non-sensitive configuration</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8043-9ec4-c4d8b44850a9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Secrets</strong> = sensitive information, stored securely</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-8179-f7de932ef5e1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Both can be <strong>injected as environment variables, files, or command-line arguments</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801f-b657-ce0359221194"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800a-b712-c580a76a72cc" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808d-91e0-f4b731ba97b2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ConfigMap = <strong>instruction manual üìò</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b5-8219-d28dbcd2d7c5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Secret = <strong>safe with passwords üîí</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8024-ac22-f7114c1ab8ca"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800a-a3a5-c74b067322a3" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-9a4a-ea91bb418c66" class=""><em>A ConfigMap stores non-sensitive configuration data in plaintext, while a Secret stores sensitive information in a base64-encoded format and can be encrypted, both of which can be injected into Pods via environment variables or files.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8080-ab0f-d0365057f041" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 73:</strong> What is the purpose of Kubernetes <code>taints</code> and <code>tolerations</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-aca2-f8f1f1397df7" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Taints and Tolerations</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d8-905b-d2ad0900d62f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Taints</strong> are applied to <strong>nodes</strong> to <strong>repel Pods</strong> that are not explicitly allowed to run on them.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b5-871f-c833b02c61af" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Tolerations</strong> are applied to <strong>Pods</strong> to <strong>allow them to be scheduled on tainted nodes</strong>.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8040-b3c3-f9ebfb17ff3e" class="">Together, they provide <strong>fine-grained control over Pod scheduling</strong>.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c7-90e6-d16103f33dd2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800c-88bb-e23e22181936" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a7c1-f1aa07741d80" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Taint a Node</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ba-8933-eb3714047b95" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl taint nodes node1 key=value:NoSchedule

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8013-8122-f4233a23c2c5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>NoSchedule</code> ‚Üí Pods that do not tolerate the taint <strong>cannot be scheduled</strong> on the node.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8093-8f79-cdfb94058056" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Other effects:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-802a-a2d2-c450df2cd634" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>PreferNoSchedule</code> ‚Üí Kubernetes <strong>tries to avoid</strong> scheduling Pods there.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808d-9658-e821483907a6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><code>NoExecute</code> ‚Üí Existing Pods not tolerating the taint are <strong>evicted</strong>.</li></ul></li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8035-803a-e2eafb108e9b" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Tolerate the Taint in a Pod</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8063-a46f-f8994ace8c4c" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">tolerations:
- key: &quot;key&quot;
  operator: &quot;Equal&quot;
  value: &quot;value&quot;
  effect: &quot;NoSchedule&quot;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8062-94bb-f88177fd30fd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">This Pod <strong>can now be scheduled</strong> on the tainted node.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-808f-d5e98cdaa64d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8040-bde2-cebe695f34f2" class=""><strong>Use Cases</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-acf0-e5e4b3539db3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Reserve nodes for <strong>special workloads</strong> (e.g., GPU nodes).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-ab17-c894d86973f7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Separate critical workloads</strong> from normal workloads.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8074-a95f-ff61d3f3ace4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Evict Pods during <strong>maintenance</strong> using <code>NoExecute</code>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-800c-8dbc-c47adbde3f4c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-9f72-cf03105bcd4a" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-9f93-fabe8d73c611" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Taint = <strong>‚ÄúStaff Only‚Äù sign üö™</strong> on a room (node)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800b-9332-c8b85ad8ada6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Toleration = <strong>special pass üé´</strong> allowing certain people (Pods) to enter</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-aa12-deaf28e7e873"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-800c-8adf-f1fc0910e266" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-99ba-efed4a7f44c6" class=""><em>Kubernetes taints repel Pods from nodes, while tolerations allow Pods to be scheduled on those nodes, providing fine-grained control over Pod placement and node usage.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8055-979d-daa0d1657b79" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 74:</strong> How do you perform a rollback of a deployment in Kubernetes?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-be8f-c2f3cfe0ac06" class=""><strong>Rollback of a Deployment in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8014-9a17-e9b98c01a3fe" class="">Kubernetes allows you to <strong>rollback a Deployment to a previous revision</strong> if the current version is failing.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802d-9045-e576263b5da6"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-964f-f7449ca24339" class=""><strong>Steps to Perform a Rollback</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-800e-a7ce-caf94f91c32a" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Check Deployment History</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-806d-bc74-d4d94aeaee95" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout history deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804e-b057-e0cf80fff395" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Shows all revisions of the Deployment.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-8cbd-e1de31d5bc8b" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Rollback to Previous Revision</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-91cd-da7a61b5fbc6" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout undo deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-86c4-d6b7e98d9608" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolls back to the <strong>previous stable version</strong>.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8031-8c48-d591cbf0ccdf" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Rollback to a Specific Revision</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-9cea-c0a16894846e" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl rollout undo deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt; --to-revision=2

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-9705-e453a414d7d9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolls back to a <strong>specific revision</strong> in the Deployment history.</li></ul><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803d-8412-d3d75b4602b4" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Verify Rollback</strong></li></ol><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-802e-a296-fdb7778c6e91" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get deployments
kubectl rollout status deployment/&lt;deployment-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-a495-c4528771c0d7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures Pods are running the <strong>desired previous version</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8099-b458-c6d451739cfc"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8070-ae2b-d337afd0a56b" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804f-a300-c938945f0906" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes <strong>automatically keeps a history of Deployment revisions</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-9b63-e3e5954ed6a6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rollbacks are <strong>safe and declarative</strong>, no manual Pod deletion is needed.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-822d-fe7ed782a3af" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful in <strong>canary deployments</strong> or after a <strong>failed rolling update</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-b61f-c84dd9d1c3ad"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8021-81c6-db4a8a3769fb" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-9496-cf61cf346791" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deployment rollback = <strong>undo button ‚è™ in a document editor</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-8000-ef4dcdda3cb0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Reverts to a previous version without losing everything.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-809d-92bc-f211759ef91a"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ba-a0a0-df9a9842f959" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8063-a31f-f565d52764c2" class=""><em>A Kubernetes deployment can be rolled back using </em><em><code>kubectl rollout undo</code></em><em>, which reverts the Deployment to a previous revision from its revision history, ensuring safe recovery from faulty updates.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8095-998f-cd6061dfc4d8" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 75:</strong> What is the function of the <code>kubelet</code> in a Kubernetes node?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80de-af32-cc2065468d30" class=""><strong>Function of the kubelet</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-9940-d4af7f2a6fa9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">The <strong>kubelet</strong> is an <strong>agent that runs on every node</strong> in a Kubernetes cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-90fb-cb5000f3305c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It <strong>ensures that the containers in Pods are running and healthy</strong> according to the PodSpec provided by the API server.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801b-a351-f471dda0a739"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801b-9ab6-eac89466532c" class=""><strong>Key Responsibilities</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-8889-f9257a7b09cb" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Pod Management</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805c-8b66-e015ff1b0ae4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Watches the <strong>API server for assigned Pods</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8041-9a9a-f0ca4d99d75f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Creates, updates, or deletes containers as needed.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8091-a38a-c920ac9c0d7d" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Node Health Reporting</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806d-b564-d86d5d100fed" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Reports node and Pod status back to the API server.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8059-bc71-c3372503e127" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Container Runtime Interface</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-8013-d053a63c7512" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Communicates with the container runtime (Docker, containerd, CRI-O) to manage containers.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-a1af-efaf686d421f" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Liveness &amp; Readiness Checks</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809a-bf73-c59e485f53e7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Executes <strong>liveness and readiness probes</strong> and updates Pod status accordingly.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8060-b74c-e444173cd610" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li><strong>Volume Management</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-b6d3-ffafd3e4958b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Mounts persistent volumes specified in the PodSpec.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-b585-d32cb4e7652a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80be-87ce-e92be4dac9a8" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-8ff3-d3da92ea0597" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kubelet <strong>does not schedule Pods</strong>; it <strong>runs Pods assigned by the scheduler</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800a-9043-dc68fe157b01" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ensures that Pods <strong>match the desired state</strong> defined in the Deployment, StatefulSet, or PodSpec.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808f-9e1a-c797fe2c2a22"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-b3b0-c61cc5c079ec" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-8d4b-c5c44bee95bd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kubelet = <strong>node-level caretaker üõ†Ô∏è</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8027-b236-d66f261dbc4e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ensures each Pod/container on the node is running properly and reports back to the control plane.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8087-af9a-c8da012d6c88"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8006-a7ed-fb3201c9855b" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-9951-d590b8b6d9bf" class=""><em>The kubelet runs on each Kubernetes node, monitoring and managing Pods and containers, ensuring they match the desired state, reporting node and Pod status, and handling volume mounts and health probes.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8011-938c-d3a3f1d3ccea" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 76:</strong> Explain how Kubernetes handles service discovery.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8008-a089-f80cf1f49d4c" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Service Discovery</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8076-9d59-e388d10fc8c5" class="">Kubernetes provides <strong>built-in service discovery</strong> so that Pods can communicate without knowing each other‚Äôs IP addresses, which can change dynamically.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-803d-a62e-de5c83be9b71"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801d-b790-f1a267b3cd51" class=""><strong>Mechanisms for Service Discovery</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-801e-84d5-fd5beef40d56" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>DNS-Based Service Discovery</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-9983-f27a5c54eb6f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes runs a <strong>DNS service</strong> (CoreDNS) inside the cluster.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8010-b241-ea5cc98cfaa9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Every Service gets a <strong>stable DNS name</strong>:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d5-9dec-f9fe0713ff90" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">&lt;service-name&gt;.&lt;namespace&gt;.svc.cluster.local

</code></pre></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807d-8d72-f60e8a86f92b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods can communicate using this DNS name instead of IPs:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8061-94e4-c540fa9a2e12" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">curl http://my-service.default.svc.cluster.local:80

</code></pre></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-8628-ca3cf0ec1613" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">CoreDNS automatically updates DNS records when Pods are added or removed.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8011-9570-f2bf9ca2a3d1" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Environment Variables</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805d-ba05-ea591da52ed1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes injects environment variables for each Service into Pods when they start:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8089-b6ca-e1dce442aae9" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">MY_SERVICE_SERVICE_HOST=10.0.0.42
MY_SERVICE_SERVICE_PORT=80

</code></pre></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8067-a7ec-f82fb8030d68" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for legacy applications relying on env vars.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80df-8c0c-ff2114ecb409" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>kube-proxy Routing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8012-89bf-e43cf03d99f4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kube-proxy manages <strong>ClusterIP routing</strong>, so traffic sent to a Service DNS or ClusterIP is forwarded to the correct Pod(s) automatically.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-9533-f5f5bfe2f9e1"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8079-b26a-f5c780a97deb" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-9368-f6ee54c79e91" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods do <strong>not need to know IP addresses</strong> of other Pods.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d3-bd54-df93d2581162" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">DNS names are <strong>stable</strong>, even if underlying Pods are replaced.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f0-bc36-c0f9e6f47e73" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works for <strong>internal communication</strong>; external access requires <strong>Ingress or LoadBalancer</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8098-a7b1-ea33fe6ff2c9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8002-929d-e43f3225c55b" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8054-9d1d-c0e207b52476" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Service discovery = <strong>company directory üìû</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8096-b51a-f5b110671b6b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Employees (Pods) contact a department (Service) by name, not by changing desk numbers (Pod IPs).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-9fc8-cb8bcaa34388"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-809c-b4eb-ffdd46c1884e" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8017-adb1-c614fa9ce3ba" class=""><em>Kubernetes handles service discovery using DNS and environment variables, allowing Pods to find Services via stable names, while kube-proxy routes traffic to the appropriate Pods dynamically.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80f0-a277-d3dda6475e45" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 77:</strong> What is a <code>Kubernetes Ingress</code>, and how does it differ from a <code>Service</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-bb85-f6e2b5d45625" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Ingress</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8038-987e-ded5897320c9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Ingress</strong> is a Kubernetes resource that manages <strong>external access to Services</strong>, typically HTTP/HTTPS traffic.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8096-af58-df433a39b612" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Provides <strong>URL-based routing, SSL termination, and virtual hosting</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ff-b783-dbb54dba71f1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Requires an <strong>Ingress Controller</strong> (e.g., Nginx, Traefik) to implement the rules.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8074-bd49-ff37677d96a3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8048-a4ca-fc9c5760fd3e" class=""><strong>Example Ingress YAML</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-803a-bacc-ce9c80395a02" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Ingress
metadata:
  name: example-ingress
spec:
  rules:
  - host: example.com
    http:
      paths:
      - path: /app1
        pathType: Prefix
        backend:
          service:
            name: app1-service
            port:
              number: 80
      - path: /app2
        pathType: Prefix
        backend:
          service:
            name: app2-service
            port:
              number: 80

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-bd6f-e9b7de1b95dc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Routes traffic based on <strong>host and path</strong> to different Services.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8060-affe-f75e7e069e73" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can handle <strong>TLS termination</strong> for HTTPS traffic.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801a-b291-f873cefadc99"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801b-9a42-d25ff3c901d7" class=""><strong>Difference Between Ingress and Service</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8078-80a3-e0b6451d7afe" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8064-9ac5-f7e853474551"><th id="}{|:" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="sI@F" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Service</strong></th><th id="skbj" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Ingress</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-803c-8338-ddc88ae840d9"><td id="}{|:" class=""><strong>Purpose</strong></td><td id="sI@F" class="">Exposes Pods internally or externally (ClusterIP, NodePort, LoadBalancer)</td><td id="skbj" class="">Manages external HTTP/HTTPS access to Services</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8028-a0dc-e38a68fe9492"><td id="}{|:" class=""><strong>Traffic Type</strong></td><td id="sI@F" class="">Any protocol (TCP/UDP)</td><td id="skbj" class="">HTTP/HTTPS only</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-808c-9ee3-c44dab274464"><td id="}{|:" class=""><strong>Routing</strong></td><td id="sI@F" class="">Simple; based on IP and port</td><td id="skbj" class="">Advanced; based on host, path, headers</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806e-9ce1-dfb05a127415"><td id="}{|:" class=""><strong>TLS Support</strong></td><td id="sI@F" class="">Limited</td><td id="skbj" class="">Built-in TLS termination</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-9e17-c1a354f2a3eb"><td id="}{|:" class=""><strong>Requires Controller</strong></td><td id="sI@F" class="">No</td><td id="skbj" class="">Yes (Ingress Controller like Nginx, Traefik)</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8038-9cfa-dd6dd7fa5e3a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-b884-d4359edc3beb" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-8ad6-f53573382d62" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Services expose Pods on <strong>IP and port level</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8011-b511-c722e088746e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ingress exposes Services at the <strong>HTTP/HTTPS layer</strong>, with <strong>routing rules and TLS</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8042-86bf-d6d494ccb949" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Often, <strong>Ingress + Service</strong> are used together: Ingress routes traffic to Service ‚Üí Service routes to Pods.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804a-bbcf-fbc3a80f6b82"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804c-b0d1-ea20dc6df1ae" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8062-843f-c1d3c753413a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Service = <strong>building entrance üö™</strong> for a floor (Pod group)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8087-9ed0-cb2c25a852d1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Ingress = <strong>reception desk üè¢</strong> directing visitors based on room number (path/host)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8089-b5db-cbd2357ef37d"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-8797-c4a0cf862d3d" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8017-908a-de853f407792" class=""><em>A Kubernetes Service exposes Pods at the IP/port level, while an Ingress manages external HTTP/HTTPS traffic with host/path routing and TLS, often directing traffic to Services.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8032-b97d-c614cce8da94" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 78:</strong> What are Kubernetes <code>labels</code> and <code>selectors</code>, and how are they used?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8056-bf37-e7cdad1ddd40" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Labels</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-9b66-e522fea97a42" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Labels</strong> are <strong>key-value pairs</strong> attached to Kubernetes objects (Pods, Services, Deployments, etc.).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-8498-d19dcd502635" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">They are used to <strong>categorize and organize resources</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-816e-d22b40c6b6f7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Labels do <strong>not affect the semantics</strong> of the resource; they are <strong>metadata for identification</strong>.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8021-be2f-df4b23805a2d" class=""><strong>Example of Labels in a Pod:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-801c-938d-dfe8d0e20dff" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">metadata:
  labels:
    app: nginx
    environment: production

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-9b67-ec7a2a326095"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-9668-ef4182682098" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Selectors</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804c-bc91-dacdcbffe220" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Selectors</strong> allow you to <strong>query or filter resources</strong> based on labels.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805d-9679-d48f4357ae16" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Commonly used in <strong>Services, ReplicaSets, and Deployments</strong> to select which Pods they manage.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80bf-9d48-c47560606e1a" class=""><strong>Example of a Selector in a Service:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-802c-9608-d48e8e61ea7e" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">spec:
  selector:
    app: nginx
    environment: production

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-8eea-d7f5ea0f2344" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">This Service routes traffic to <strong>all Pods matching the labels</strong> <code>app=nginx</code> and <code>environment=production</code>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8036-8fde-eb663470deda"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f9-b2f8-df3fbbc44dd5" class=""><strong>Types of Selectors</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-8fa3-f93a62de2b6a" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Equality-based</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d2-b05f-f171d454117a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Matches Pods with exact label values:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-800f-82d9-f5545fee5598" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">env = production
tier != frontend

</code></pre></li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-809a-b95a-c404cdb0b0fc" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Set-based</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8051-a4ef-d2bc37fba4ba" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Matches Pods where the label is in a set:<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-b221-ccb9fa8f5be0" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Plain Text" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">env in (production, staging)
tier notin (frontend, backend)

</code></pre></li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8008-8b50-ccab0f03d9ab"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8016-a65b-cf4010f2b0a5" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8084-9ac1-d8ffbe52755d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Labels = <strong>tags for Kubernetes objects</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-999b-fcfc40465225" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Selectors = <strong>filters to target objects based on labels</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-ad48-e08311098c18" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">They enable <strong>dynamic grouping</strong> for deployments, scaling, and service routing.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-807f-9bcb-ffffb5bd7c32"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805d-b2da-ee094c56e3ea" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802c-a29f-f0c9d5733a34" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Labels = <strong>stickers on products üè∑Ô∏è</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-ae27-c3247829e845" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Selectors = <strong>filtering products by stickers</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802c-bec9-c77dbdfc60f2"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-808e-8eb5-e23135c7d5de" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-804e-baaa-edd5aa4fac99" class=""><em>Kubernetes labels are key-value pairs used to tag resources, and selectors are queries that filter resources based on those labels, enabling grouping, management, and service routing.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8051-bc73-fdf96ed9dd8c" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 79:</strong> Explain the concept of <code>Kubernetes namespaces</code> and their benefits.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-b9fc-d67f8c1b6ff6" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Namespaces</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-94bb-f7b786fbc6f1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">A <strong>Namespace</strong> is a <strong>logical partition of the cluster</strong> that groups Kubernetes resources (Pods, Services, Deployments, etc.).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808b-94af-c3137b563425" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Namespaces allow <strong>multiple teams or projects to share the same cluster</strong> without resource conflicts.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8011-ac3f-e4caac842aaa"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-809d-b0b3-c0d8ee611439" class=""><strong>Key Benefits</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-9511-c40dd5ecfd55" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Resource Isolation</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f1-938d-c034eb249c11" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Namespaces <strong>prevent name collisions</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-919f-eeb7d0bbcd05" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can have <code>nginx</code> Deployment in both <code>dev</code> and <code>prod</code> namespaces.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80f7-9cf0-c2e3801d82d7" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Access Control</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-890f-c1c89d275222" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">RBAC (Role-Based Access Control) can be applied per namespace.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809d-aae2-e0bdef87f170" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Teams get <strong>permissions only in their namespace</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-a050-c8f7a78386cc" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Resource Quotas</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-93d5-fc43d3cdafa9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Limit CPU, memory, and storage usage <strong>per namespace</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800a-a5f7-d3ef3b4bdd3a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Prevents one team from exhausting cluster resources.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8034-87db-e533b9c5c517" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li><strong>Organizational Clarity</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-a427-c216181b9ff7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helps <strong>group resources by environment, team, or project</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8036-9a7c-cb3d1cfaba17" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Makes it easier to monitor and manage workloads.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8073-82c2-fb6fd75ac643"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8058-a9bc-c30a254a275c" class=""><strong>Common Commands</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-8c09-d1fbc348a1e7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">List namespaces:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-98d8-d0c1a3aaf91a" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get namespaces

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803e-aea7-c2576743bcbf" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Create a namespace:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-9462-df47d6281079" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl create namespace dev

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8042-a226-c05b8194cf08" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Apply resources to a namespace:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b7b9-da39b3ebf60b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl apply -f pod.yaml -n dev

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8019-b2df-ee9ce0e02849"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801b-87fe-f6f90960f5e5" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8020-a609-c87afa8954f9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Namespace = <strong>apartments in a building üè¢</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807b-b8a6-c27dec41047d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Each team (tenant) has its own apartment (namespace) to live and manage resources independently.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80de-ba7b-e65b44da0f96"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8028-95ab-e5b1f9798243" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8068-8267-fea7cc02664c" class=""><em>Kubernetes namespaces are logical partitions of a cluster that provide resource isolation, access control, and organizational clarity, enabling multiple teams or projects to share the same cluster safely.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80cf-b3b3-d5d1d0fc3993" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 80:</strong> What is the difference between <code>kubectl apply</code> and <code>kubectl create</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8052-9d01-c72acc97cc5b" class=""><strong>Difference Between </strong><code><strong>kubectl apply</strong></code><strong> and </strong><code><strong>kubectl create</strong></code></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-a759-e71c4cf236cd" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-913c-cc43539be8d7"><th id="=pgv" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="c`HU" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:267px"><strong>kubectl create</strong></th><th id="nHaj" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:270px"><strong>kubectl apply</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-800c-aa01-c6d2c486711b"><td id="=pgv" class=""><strong>Purpose</strong></td><td id="c`HU" class="" style="width:267px">Creates a new resource in the cluster</td><td id="nHaj" class="" style="width:270px">Creates or updates a resource declaratively</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8037-b7e2-f41197aa9e90"><td id="=pgv" class=""><strong>Usage</strong></td><td id="c`HU" class="" style="width:267px"><code>kubectl create -f pod.yaml</code></td><td id="nHaj" class="" style="width:270px"><code>kubectl apply -f pod.yaml</code></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8047-a8ab-e02c1458273b"><td id="=pgv" class=""><strong>Idempotency</strong></td><td id="c`HU" class="" style="width:267px"><strong>Not idempotent</strong>; fails if resource exists</td><td id="nHaj" class="" style="width:270px"><strong>Idempotent</strong>; updates existing resources</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80de-a6f3-df77363f7ced"><td id="=pgv" class=""><strong>Updates</strong></td><td id="c`HU" class="" style="width:267px">Cannot update an existing resource</td><td id="nHaj" class="" style="width:270px">Can update fields of existing resources</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-801d-a5f9-e82830eb294f"><td id="=pgv" class=""><strong>Common Use Case</strong></td><td id="c`HU" class="" style="width:267px">Quick creation of new resources</td><td id="nHaj" class="" style="width:270px">Managing resources declaratively in GitOps</td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804f-8f5c-c751b2ee93b5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8037-98ee-c2fa26eba783" class=""><strong>Example</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-89c0-ed4046554902" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all"># Create a Pod (fails if Pod exists)
kubectl create -f pod.yaml

# Apply a Pod manifest (creates if not exists, updates if exists)
kubectl apply -f pod.yaml

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-809a-aec2-ebc206ebbc90"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-801a-8898-d8d9574d3d2c" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-8b07-ebee870c3d2e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <code>create</code> for <strong>one-time resource creation</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8051-95da-cb297da545de" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <code>apply</code> for <strong>declarative management</strong> and <strong>version-controlled manifests</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-b5ea-d971bafd6cce" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><code>apply</code> keeps track of <strong>configuration changes</strong> via annotations
