id="272378cb-b17f-8087-b9c9-e19d58c419df"><td id="_;Cr" class=""><strong>Recreate</strong></td><td id="]h|q" class="">Deletes all old Pods first, then creates new ones (downtime occurs)</td></tr></tbody></table><p id="272378cb-b17f-8062-8407-e97cb7bec15b" class=""><strong>RollingUpdate Parameters:</strong></p><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-ad85-f3536f0574fd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>maxUnavailable</strong> ‚Üí Max Pods allowed to be unavailable during update.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-be5d-f1950edfe550" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>maxSurge</strong> ‚Üí Max extra Pods created above desired replicas during update.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8030-89ed-cde6305cc1d1"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-b32b-cc41aa7beaa8" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8095-908f-fd0319c40d24" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolling updates = <strong>zero-downtime updates</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8067-8b6b-cd4ca80e99d6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rollbacks = <strong>quick recovery to a previous stable version</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803e-a5d3-c24819d5e9fe" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deployment keeps <strong>revision history</strong> for rollbacks</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8090-8493-c882f40d27b5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8050-b2c3-c9d10638f5e2" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804b-a37b-c49234466188" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rolling update = <strong>replacing light bulbs one by one üí°</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ce-9875-fc57f1d8bac0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Rollback = <strong>putting back old bulbs if new ones fail</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-808a-b9f5-e7e167bf4874"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8081-8e09-ce9e1765ce46" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-ae9e-ddf07f497a14" class=""><em>Kubernetes rolling updates gradually replace old Pods with new ones to ensure zero downtime, and rollbacks allow reverting to a previous stable version if the update fails.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8055-881b-e45dcb027e67" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 93:</strong> What is the difference between a <code>Kubernetes deployment</code> and a <code>statefulset</code>?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8072-b1c6-c2168bb7466a" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Deployment vs StatefulSet</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-8052-b69b-e82582a23812" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8043-bc3c-de60186fe0af"><th id="Bae&lt;" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="wwgq" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Deployment</strong></th><th id="qytt" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:300px"><strong>StatefulSet</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80ec-81b1-cac6525cc601"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Purpose</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">Manages <strong>stateless applications</strong></td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">Manages <strong>stateful applications</strong> (databases, queues)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80b1-8ade-cdc7bf7651a5"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Pod Identity</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">Pods are <strong>interchangeable</strong>, no stable identity</td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">Pods have <strong>stable, unique identities</strong> (hostname &amp; network)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-ab0e-c0eec09977d1"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Pod Naming</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">Random names</td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">Predictable names: <code>&lt;statefulset-name&gt;-&lt;ordinal&gt;</code></td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8022-8e1c-c642cd3f30d8"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Storage</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">Usually ephemeral or shared storage</td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">Each Pod can have <strong>dedicated persistent storage</strong> via PVCs</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80df-a609-d5ade7acfd90"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Scaling</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">Pods can scale up/down arbitrarily</td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">Pods scale in <strong>orderly sequence</strong> (one at a time)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8007-90ad-d812df1b4dd3"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Update Strategy</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">RollingUpdate or Recreate</td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">RollingUpdate or OnDelete (controlled, ordered updates)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-b3bd-ef7f72e50724"><td id="Bae&lt;" class=""><strong>Networking</strong></td><td id="wwgq" class="">No stable network ID</td><td id="qytt" class="" style="width:300px">Each Pod gets <strong>stable network identity</strong></td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8032-90ba-c7d51110392e"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-8026-c4746d0bda8d" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c5-8af4-edec17041d74" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Deployment</strong> ‚Üí Best for web servers, APIs, stateless apps.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-8ba1-ec4674e35cb6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>StatefulSet</strong> ‚Üí Best for databases, Kafka, Zookeeper, or any app requiring <strong>stable identity and storage</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-81e3-fde4497e87b5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">StatefulSets maintain <strong>ordered deployment, scaling, and termination</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80df-b924-d682af1450df"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-803a-a490-fe5e4adafd9f" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8070-a5b5-ed5e0b5f86ab" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deployment = <strong>identical robots ü§ñ</strong> (any one can replace another)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d4-89d2-ce92f4522504" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">StatefulSet = <strong>employees with personal desks üßë‚Äçüíª</strong> (each has a unique identity and workspace)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8000-b675-e4ecdbae307a"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e4-8bb0-fcb3133368c2" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8040-bfce-e801dcc4a280" class=""><em>A Deployment manages stateless Pods with interchangeable identities, while a StatefulSet manages stateful Pods with stable identities, persistent storage, and ordered deployment and scaling.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8034-9518-cb508886b1c4" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 94:</strong> How do you ensure high availability in a Kubernetes cluster?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8022-8984-cd726078506c" class=""><strong>Ensuring High Availability in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-808b-b605-c94a08622296" class="">High availability means <strong>services remain operational even if some components fail</strong>. Kubernetes provides HA at both <strong>cluster</strong> and <strong>application</strong> levels.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-802a-a352-d3262ae4fa1a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8083-b382-c37d3ea22a02" class=""><strong>1. Cluster-Level High Availability</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801c-a989-d3295e5cefe8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Multiple Control Plane Nodes</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8009-9ea4-cc414cfe8542" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Run <strong>3 or more master nodes</strong> to avoid a single point of failure.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8017-bcdb-dad5e8c54348" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Use <strong>etcd clusters</strong> with quorum to ensure consistent state.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-804f-9195-dd48778b1e56" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>etcd Backup and Redundancy</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807a-9f14-e05b2012bc4a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Regular backups and replication across nodes.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-99d8-ec84d4c7e1a6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Load Balancer for API Server</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-84c5-caa7bf4b1704" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Expose a single endpoint that distributes requests to multiple control plane nodes.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8014-929d-cd6051809a66"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805e-96fa-c4a2e1883c46" class=""><strong>2. Node-Level High Availability</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-94bc-f46166db94d4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Multiple Worker Nodes</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8082-8943-f53f76547a73" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Distribute Pods across nodes to avoid downtime if a node fails.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8068-a520-f125e551546b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Pod Anti-Affinity</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-acb6-f2b2597d91e1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Prevents all replicas of a service from being scheduled on the same node.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805b-ae11-ea09fdb0d700"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808f-8811-ebb4fd67027b" class=""><strong>3. Application-Level High Availability</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8049-aa16-cec27bb67cf6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Deployments with Multiple Replicas</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8001-83f1-de0fbf9b025a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ensure multiple Pod instances for each application.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-99b6-ebf798ceaced" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA)</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802c-a6b7-f83de7b77c45" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Automatically adjusts Pod count under load.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801d-abef-f5996f8e4e2c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>StatefulSet with Persistent Storage</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8069-8def-e07922a66dd4" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Use persistent volumes replicated across nodes.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-802c-bd13-ec6fdc93abf7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Readiness and Liveness Probes</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8083-b467-e83026865e66" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Ensure only healthy Pods receive traffic.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8056-ace3-d34e7d7414a7"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80be-9b41-e9f6c1e387e2" class=""><strong>4. Network and Storage Redundancy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8070-9d30-e076b2d0300a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>CNI Plugins supporting HA</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8056-b9bf-c27cc9529ad5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Reliable networking between Pods.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800c-859b-eeca545fb9fb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Distributed Storage</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8026-a1ff-ecfa67ec1b3a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Storage solutions like Ceph, Portworx, or cloud provider PVs with replication.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f8-9dda-fcae8d30fd0b"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805f-b0f4-f9f053e8a9c2" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8043-9d72-d861f65516fc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">HA = <strong>redundancy + failover</strong> at control plane, node, and application levels.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a1-8799-f9572262421b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes schedules Pods automatically to maintain availability.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c2-bcb5-ddafdb41b373" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>replicas, probes, anti-affinity, and distributed storage</strong> for maximum resilience.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804f-a9ad-e78e7c65ea21"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8094-97bd-e03d0069ebf6" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-96cc-c6582146801d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">HA = <strong>multi-server office üè¢</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806d-aa95-f26b1b94fc28" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">If one server (node) fails, work continues seamlessly on others.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8067-93df-f3d09fbf3507"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-9da3-c4dc3c289a69" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-8dba-ecc4fc875ab1" class=""><em>High availability in Kubernetes is achieved via multiple control plane and worker nodes, replicated Pods, readiness and liveness probes, Pod anti-affinity, HPA, and distributed storage, ensuring continuous operation even if some components fail.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8017-a5f5-ec6f973a48fc" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 95:</strong> What are Kubernetes network policies and how do they enhance security?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8076-ae0b-d1349c9e73f9" class=""><strong>Kubernetes Network Policies</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8098-af10-dd3ac2365af9" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Network Policies are <strong>rules that control traffic flow</strong> at the Pod level.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c1-a5cd-ef1e24781cfb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">They define <strong>which Pods can communicate with each other</strong> and which external endpoints are accessible.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80db-92ec-fb4840213ce3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-92df-ea78c7091b7a" class=""><strong>Key Features</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-a541-f238be00fc3b" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Traffic Control</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-809a-b353-d14534584dab" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can <strong>allow or deny ingress (incoming)</strong> and <strong>egress (outgoing)</strong> traffic.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-803a-b8c5-e8739e150d98" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Label-Based Selection</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8080-b1cd-dba1e7bc9988" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Policies target Pods using <strong>labels</strong>, providing fine-grained control.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-809b-afd3-eb11a6b5274a" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Default Deny</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c8-881b-f2b14b28aaad" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">By default, all traffic is allowed.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-bd02-e18e373c8eae" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Applying a NetworkPolicy with no <code>from</code> or <code>to</code> rules <strong>denies all traffic</strong>, then you selectively allow necessary communication.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-b5f0-f6284d0ff992"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-803b-be91-fb91073785bf" class=""><strong>Example Network Policy</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-877b-ed2a73cc92da" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: NetworkPolicy
metadata:
  name: allow-frontend
  namespace: default
spec:
  podSelector:
    matchLabels:
      app: backend
  ingress:
  - from:
    - podSelector:
        matchLabels:
          app: frontend
    ports:
    - protocol: TCP
      port: 80

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-9392-da1b515f1fe3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Only Pods with label <code>app=frontend</code> can access <code>app=backend</code> on port 80.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805f-ab27-fd5d80e46357"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804d-aa54-d03522577d5b" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a4-a53b-caf814fc30b7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Enhances security by <strong>isolating Pods</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-bcab-fd6ba8525713" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Works with CNI plugins that <strong>support network policies</strong> (Calico, Cilium, Weave Net).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8086-8a29-e4b29b47ee1b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Can define policies for:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-acf5-dc1b2ea3229b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Ingress</strong> ‚Üí controlling incoming traffic</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80db-a1b6-d04c97bba81c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Egress</strong> ‚Üí controlling outgoing traffic</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-809a-b35d-d3b0a5dc22d4"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808c-95d1-fc855ddf675f" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f2-9dbc-ec8d0522c3d3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Network Policy = <strong>security guards üöß</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-96bc-ed6d91dd7f6b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Only allow certain employees (Pods) to enter certain rooms (Pods or services).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8084-b7e7-f7584f55c6a5"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80a9-984c-c59d5e274fcf" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8035-8168-d9caa5ce5ca0" class=""><em>Kubernetes Network Policies control Pod-to-Pod and external traffic using label-based rules, enhancing security by isolating workloads and restricting access only to allowed sources and destinations.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80de-9e5d-fb76fc081cab" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 96:</strong> Explain the difference between <code>Kubernetes ConfigMap</code> and <code>Secret</code>.</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-b93c-cfa667e3b197" class=""><strong>Kubernetes ConfigMap vs Secret</strong></h3><table id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-8cac-eb8024043f9a" class="simple-table"><thead class="simple-table-header"><tr id="272378cb-b17f-805c-8b9a-ec4ea4001803"><th id="QBXd" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header"><strong>Aspect</strong></th><th id="Mcn?" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:258px"><strong>ConfigMap</strong></th><th id="=Wr@" class="simple-table-header-color simple-table-header" style="width:265px"><strong>Secret</strong></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-9f85-f84fe344804e"><td id="QBXd" class=""><strong>Purpose</strong></td><td id="Mcn?" class="" style="width:258px">Store <strong>non-sensitive configuration data</strong></td><td id="=Wr@" class="" style="width:265px">Store <strong>sensitive data</strong> like passwords, tokens, keys</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80de-bc14-e8986ff1d7c5"><td id="QBXd" class=""><strong>Data Storage</strong></td><td id="Mcn?" class="" style="width:258px">Stored in <strong>plain text</strong></td><td id="=Wr@" class="" style="width:265px">Stored in <strong>base64-encoded</strong> form (not encrypted by default)</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-800a-a8f4-f8af8abfe57d"><td id="QBXd" class=""><strong>Use Cases</strong></td><td id="Mcn?" class="" style="width:258px">Environment variables, config files, command-line arguments</td><td id="=Wr@" class="" style="width:265px">Database credentials, API keys, TLS certificates</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-8076-aef7-f3fe455077b0"><td id="QBXd" class=""><strong>Access</strong></td><td id="Mcn?" class="" style="width:258px">Mounted as files, environment variables, or command-line args</td><td id="=Wr@" class="" style="width:265px">Mounted as files, environment variables, or volumes; can be restricted with RBAC</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-80be-9f36-fc0cbf77c5f3"><td id="QBXd" class=""><strong>Security</strong></td><td id="Mcn?" class="" style="width:258px">Not meant for sensitive information</td><td id="=Wr@" class="" style="width:265px">Can be combined with encryption at rest and RBAC for security</td></tr><tr id="272378cb-b17f-806f-9635-dc7b2b50608f"><td id="QBXd" class=""><strong>Creation Example</strong></td><td id="Mcn?" class="" style="width:258px"><code>kubectl create configmap my-config --from-literal=key=value</code></td><td id="=Wr@" class="" style="width:265px"><code>kubectl create secret generic my-secret --from-literal=password=pass123</code></td></tr></tbody></table><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8094-ac38-c54d9bbc1f15"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b052-c89629e1b9df" class=""><strong>Example: Using ConfigMap in a Pod</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-808d-bfa8-e6e6eca9b3cd" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
metadata:
  name: my-pod
spec:
  containers:
  - name: app
    image: nginx
    envFrom:
    - configMapRef:
        name: my-config

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-b84f-f971ce65f3ff" class=""><strong>Example: Using Secret in a Pod</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8031-8812-dca6e64c49b6" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
metadata:
  name: my-pod
spec:
  containers:
  - name: app
    image: nginx
    envFrom:
    - secretRef:
        name: my-secret

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805e-8cee-f28d03016ac9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-b9f9-f3617b804276" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8014-8db4-ce1608e6217c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>ConfigMap</strong> = plain, non-sensitive configuration</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8054-be67-ec443f58746f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Secret</strong> = sensitive data with optional encryption and access control</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-8153-dc269acacafe" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Both can be <strong>mounted as files or injected as environment variables</strong></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8088-94a4-dfd2b969a946"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8091-9d95-efbbc0b30bb7" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-aa47-f14836a51afb" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">ConfigMap = <strong>office manual üìÑ</strong> (anyone can read)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8019-872f-f80d7f1ca6ae" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Secret = <strong>safe with passwords üîê</strong> (restricted access)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8069-84ea-fa36f653989f"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-805b-b84e-c0a648402b70" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8062-87f8-e0e9d0d99dc9" class=""><em>Kubernetes ConfigMap stores non-sensitive configuration data, while Secret stores sensitive information like passwords or keys, often with restricted access and optional encryption.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-807c-a4e5-de9095ba02d0" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 97:</strong> How does Kubernetes handle scaling of stateful applications?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80d1-96cc-c4bf7c1a2360" class=""><strong>Scaling Stateful Applications in Kubernetes</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8030-a272-d028d02dc3ab" class="">Stateful applications (databases, Kafka, Zookeeper) <strong>require stable identities and persistent storage</strong>, so scaling is more controlled.</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8009-b3a9-f7b86a938f78"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8055-9f38-e30c56a873f6" class=""><strong>1. Using StatefulSets</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e2-ad63-e6179c606c4c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">StatefulSets manage <strong>stateful Pods</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fc-bd2b-cc9dc247593f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Each Pod gets a <strong>stable hostname and dedicated PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8010-9408-d3d3f50a999f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Scaling is done <strong>in order</strong>, ensuring stability.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-931c-c2510fef081b" class=""><strong>Scale Command:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8080-bfc9-d7d89ef3d84a" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl scale statefulset my-db --replicas=5

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c4-a2e7-e8837e246916" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Pods are added one at a time (<code>my-db-3</code>, <code>my-db-4</code>, etc.).</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-8b73-c6053597faf6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Deletion also occurs <strong>in reverse order</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8007-84bd-e2820eaaed8d"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8009-9aa1-f33060e0fb82" class=""><strong>2. Considerations for Scaling Stateful Apps</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8034-8f15-c1e7798c715e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Ordered Pod Management</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-aad2-e5c324eac9e0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">StatefulSet ensures Pods start and terminate <strong>one at a time</strong> to avoid conflicts.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cf-bd7e-ccbb72dc0b71" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Persistent Storage</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-88b3-ce73ff316fea" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Each new Pod gets its <strong>own PVC</strong>, ensuring data persistence.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-a47a-d52c8e40f914" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Network Identity</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805d-b6cc-e47bf345c592" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">DNS names remain <strong>stable</strong>: <code>&lt;statefulset-name&gt;-&lt;ordinal&gt;.&lt;service-name&gt;</code>.</li></ul></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e3-ba7b-d248ba65921d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Scaling Down</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b7-aad5-e2879fd6054a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Stateful apps often require <strong>careful data handling</strong> when reducing replicas.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8047-9a41-e4a147048028"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-803d-aeca-c77b4fd8ff7b" class=""><strong>3. Autoscaling Stateful Applications</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-886d-d1be6ca6d5b8" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Kubernetes <strong>Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA)</strong> can be used, but metrics must consider <strong>state consistency</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8041-bcfa-e9bff7ad020f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Often, scaling stateful apps requires <strong>application-level awareness</strong> (like cluster rebalancing for databases).</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-805e-826f-dd7f6f316355"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-803b-8be3-c7b4522fd832" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-ad2d-d18c4be83339" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Stateless apps = <strong>easy horizontal scaling</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8069-aa61-d7bdacf761b1" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Stateful apps = <strong>ordered scaling with stable identity and storage</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-807c-89d2-d6a40238e4cf" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Use <strong>StatefulSets</strong>, PVCs, and DNS services for HA and reliability.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-8bbf-dd0643643094"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8090-8ab8-eca34e545ff2" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-806e-94bb-e991bc2eb00d" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Stateless = <strong>clones of a robot ü§ñ</strong> (anyone can be added/removed freely)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8038-ad02-f23f88ca3f9c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Stateful = <strong>employees with personal desks üßë‚Äçüíª</strong> (each requires their own space and identity)</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ee-872d-cd0db7e019f1"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-8085-be72-c914b7a39a70" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-9186-d40cfe0f4342" class=""><em>Kubernetes scales stateful applications using StatefulSets, which provide stable Pod identities, persistent storage, and ordered scaling to ensure data consistency and application stability.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80d5-b749-f1ab80994c32" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 98:</strong> What is the role of the <code>kube-proxy</code> in Kubernetes networking?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-807b-a930-d96309c28c83" class=""><strong>Role of kube-proxy in Kubernetes</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-b3a3-e0c81fc06b89" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>kube-proxy</strong> is a <strong>network component</strong> that runs on each node.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c3-9c9c-ede9d11da8f2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">It <strong>maintains network rules</strong> that allow Pods to communicate with each other and with Services.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-8038-da12dc89db8a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Implements <strong>service abstraction</strong>, providing <strong>stable IPs and ports</strong> for accessing Pods.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-af22-f31385522135"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8055-9930-c81b80b6783a" class=""><strong>Key Functions</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-800a-92a4-dac7a03e1f97" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><strong>Service Traffic Routing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8079-86d2-dd6c9bb6fa6f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Routes traffic to <strong>the correct Pod endpoints</strong> for a Service.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8040-85a1-c7c8e4d237ed" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Handles both <strong>cluster-internal and external traffic</strong>.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80a2-af11-d9b6cbd9ccf3" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><strong>Load Balancing</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-924d-c6d518bdce84" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Performs simple <strong>round-robin load balancing</strong> among Pod endpoints for a Service.</li></ul></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8069-903e-f546c4ea2dba" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li><strong>Network Rules</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80bd-895d-fd0545f1e396" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Configures <strong>iptables, IPVS, or userspace rules</strong> on each node for routing Service traffic.</li></ul></li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8019-8cd9-ca5a7ea7e1f7"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8036-bfcf-df7838622243" class=""><strong>How It Works</strong></h3><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-807d-9271-cc7c652d51ee" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li>When a Service is created, kube-proxy watches the API server for <strong>Service and Endpoint changes</strong>.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-88de-ebd41fa95af2" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li>It sets up <strong>routing rules</strong> on the node so traffic to <code>ServiceIP:Port</code> is forwarded to one of the Pods.</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8093-ae39-de35d7a7fc40" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Ensures <strong>Pods can be added or removed</strong> without changing client connections.</li></ol><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80de-a8a1-f78c8a57f4a4"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80e0-9fe8-e97523cb4f24" class=""><strong>Modes of kube-proxy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8095-abee-fa0d27fc9025" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>Userspace</strong> ‚Üí Legacy, less efficient</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f5-8c25-c0585c064dd3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>iptables</strong> ‚Üí Uses Linux iptables rules for fast routing</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-805f-a467-f43f18f18ab5" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc"><strong>IPVS</strong> ‚Üí High-performance load balancing</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ae-9740-c507ac37cfd9"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8032-92ad-e5692d49ce4e" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80eb-8664-f213843b8526" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kube-proxy = <strong>enables Kubernetes Service abstraction</strong></li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8029-9172-e057e70bb615" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Provides <strong>stable IPs</strong> for dynamic Pods</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801c-869a-f0072f7a226e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Performs <strong>load balancing</strong> across Pod endpoints</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-89e2-f572e5690ab5"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-806e-af06-d23b0175ee93" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-8e7b-f6a1c971d7dd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">kube-proxy = <strong>reception desk üè¢</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8070-87d3-d3def2ac4a8e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">You call the office number (Service IP), and it <strong>directs your call to the right employee (Pod)</strong>.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80bb-94b3-f3de6dabb028"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-806d-8922-ce4732e65b92" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-804e-a5a1-ff5e086b6857" class=""><em>Kube-proxy runs on each node, manages network rules, and routes Service traffic to the correct Pods, providing load balancing and stable access to dynamic Pod endpoints.</em></p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8013-bcfe-d02a88d6c510"/></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-80d2-beda-c963d2f63197" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 99:</strong> What are the benefits of using <code>Kubernetes Helm</code> for package management?</summary><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805c-82a9-d9592f882791" class=""><strong>Benefits of Using Kubernetes Helm</strong></h3><p id="272378cb-b17f-8018-947f-cc81788440f8" class="">
</p><p id="272378cb-b17f-80c6-8a84-c5fffdd93524" class="">Helm simplifies <strong>deployment and management of applications</strong> on Kubernetes by using <strong>charts</strong> (predefined templates).</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804f-bdf0-ddc37802a393"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8072-9164-d0ba4e59c2a0" class=""><strong>1. Simplified Deployment</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8013-be6a-ef4c243c6218" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm charts <strong>package Kubernetes manifests</strong> into reusable templates.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80a7-8b81-e7ba781c83b3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">You can <strong>install complex applications</strong> with a single command:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80ef-bdd9-f79b2730293e" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">helm install my-app ./my-chart

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8088-819a-d9d5e94ae8a9" class=""><strong>2. Version Control</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8041-a41d-ccff8ed4cb82" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm supports <strong>chart versions</strong>, enabling <strong>rollbacks</strong> to previous releases:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b0-937f-d464e08f6597" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">helm rollback my-app 1

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8068-8905-d169ded6f661" class=""><strong>3. Reusability</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801c-8c66-f897f7feba88" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Charts can be <strong>shared across teams</strong> or downloaded from repositories like <strong>Helm Hub</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-8502-fb3895e6f029" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Promotes <strong>standardization</strong> of deployments.</li></ul><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80c9-ba69-d0e774d8bb80" class=""><strong>4. Parameterization</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803d-a8ca-e230ab978a2c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm allows <strong>dynamic configuration</strong> via <code>values.yaml</code>, enabling deployment <strong>customization per environment</strong>.</li></ul><p id="272378cb-b17f-8069-bd06-de94412c0c87" class=""><strong>Example:</strong></p><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a6-b68d-c6b03de50d3b" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">replicaCount: 3
image:
  repository: my-app
  tag: v2

</code></pre><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-804d-9a00-f9bc1f80e5a0" class=""><strong>5. Dependency Management</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8071-b8fa-debb57069ba6" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm charts can define <strong>dependencies</strong> on other charts.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8020-98f3-d4882d50d6bc" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful for deploying <strong>multi-service applications</strong> in a single command.</li></ul><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-82a7-cc5541be182b" class=""><strong>6. Rollbacks &amp; Upgrades</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8003-a534-c24551a9b14b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm maintains a <strong>release history</strong> for each deployment.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80aa-92eb-e15585185e91" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Easy to <strong>upgrade or revert</strong> applications safely.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f4-9bd0-df2dd458b268"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80fb-98c9-fb64cfbdca4a" class=""><strong>Key Points</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8029-b454-c970755fed28" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Simplifies deployment, configuration, and upgrades.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8093-aeae-d063ed5c4777" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Supports <strong>parameterization, templating, and versioning</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ea-9278-da087b7e5e43" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Promotes <strong>reproducibility and best practices</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8025-aed2-c46c88690d2c"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80bc-a872-f23c8657a38b" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-aafe-d618deaf67ba" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helm = <strong>apt or yum for Kubernetes üì¶</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-808c-89b0-e704fc6e588b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">Install, upgrade, rollback apps like installing packages on Linux.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-804d-9d5b-e4be57fa0c25"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-807d-bf16-db2038c6394a" class="">‚úÖ <strong>One-liner interview answer:</strong></p><p id="272378cb-b17f-8072-8543-fd09c5b76266" class=""><em>Kubernetes Helm simplifies deployment and management by packaging manifests into charts, supports versioning, parameterization, dependencies, rollbacks, and promotes reusable, standardized deployments.</em></p></details></li></ul><ul id="26b378cb-b17f-8004-b3d0-cb73fbcfdd20" class="toggle"><li><details open=""><summary><strong>Question 100:</strong> How do you troubleshoot a Kubernetes pod that is crashing repeatedly (CrashLoopBackOff)?</summary><p id="272378cb-b17f-8031-9f02-d9f5e31a5137" class="">Here‚Äôs a detailed guide for troubleshooting a Kubernetes Pod stuck in <strong>CrashLoopBackOff</strong>:</p><hr id="272378cb-b17f-809e-a3db-d4b6231d966a"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8043-8be2-ca65fcf2512c" class=""><strong>1. Check Pod Status</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8005-9541-c3b7776e3ed0" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl get pods

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80fd-bd27-c40c4f1e1c24" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Look at <strong>STATUS</strong>, e.g., <code>CrashLoopBackOff</code>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80fe-ac5c-ebc672d4025f"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-808e-8c24-d478496a37d1" class=""><strong>2. Describe the Pod</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-bc89-ea1ab03ee99a" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl describe pod &lt;pod-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e1-afa4-f9329ced157f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Check for:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80f3-b0c3-d22fad20e663" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>Events</strong> showing failures or restarts.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800f-98d3-c060398c4963" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle"><strong>ImagePull errors</strong>, OOMKills, or other warnings.</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-a88d-f2d7f4f68e88"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-807f-8bc9-e10c369fda81" class=""><strong>3. Inspect Pod Logs</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-9976-f653352dae89" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl logs &lt;pod-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8088-931a-c589bfe47569" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Shows the <strong>stdout/stderr output</strong> of the container.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d6-a564-d3dd1c2c590f" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">For multiple containers in a Pod:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b4-bdab-fac25fcce1cb" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl logs &lt;pod-name&gt; -c &lt;container-name&gt;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8086-8caf-e5f995d3f97a" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Helps identify <strong>application errors</strong> causing the crash.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-8664-d363ec453b05"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-809a-a358-e1e2ab224185" class=""><strong>4. Check Previous Logs</strong></h3><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-8aec-d60c3163b1aa" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl logs &lt;pod-name&gt; --previous

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80c0-b7af-e81cd089549e" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Useful if the container <strong>crashed before generating logs</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b9-b65c-e4335abea6c2"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a0-a498-c62e3f6baa0b" class=""><strong>5. Examine Resource Limits</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8002-b93c-fba87ba558cd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">If Pod is killed due to <strong>OOMKilled</strong> or CPU throttling:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-809d-bdc7-dcd50730cf5f" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">resources:
  limits:
    memory: &quot;256Mi&quot;
    cpu: &quot;500m&quot;

</code></pre><ul id="272378cb-b17f-801a-86a0-c619645a0cfd" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Consider increasing <strong>limits or requests</strong>.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80e6-a09b-d35d27670632"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8068-9a6b-f18f855d3e3f" class=""><strong>6. Check Image &amp; Command</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cc-9a68-d6db90d598ed" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Verify:<ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-8f56-ea2f5259e94c" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">The container <strong>image exists and is accessible</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80d9-90cd-c529e6912b26" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">The <strong>entrypoint or command</strong> is correct.</li></ul></li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-8032-9dd6-ecf99d33ed16" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-YAML" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">command: [&quot;myapp&quot;]
args: [&quot;--port&quot;, &quot;8080&quot;]

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-801e-9b63-f0038d072273"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-80a5-90b4-f8df7e8cc12b" class=""><strong>7. Test Interactively</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8025-8cb4-e3344e4315ac" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Run the container locally or in another Pod to <strong>debug interactively</strong>:</li></ul><script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/prism.min.js" integrity="sha512-7Z9J3l1+EYfeaPKcGXu3MS/7T+w19WtKQY/n+xzmw4hZhJ9tyYmcUS+4QqAlzhicE5LAfMQSF3iFTK9bQdTxXg==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"></script><link rel="stylesheet" href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/prism/1.29.0/themes/prism.min.css" integrity="sha512-tN7Ec6zAFaVSG3TpNAKtk4DOHNpSwKHxxrsiw4GHKESGPs5njn/0sMCUMl2svV4wo4BK/rCP7juYz+zx+l6oeQ==" crossorigin="anonymous" referrerPolicy="no-referrer"/><pre id="272378cb-b17f-80b6-b9d8-e34ba8bd79d6" class="code code-wrap"><code class="language-Bash" style="white-space:pre-wrap;word-break:break-all">kubectl run -it --rm debug --image=my-image -- /bin/bash

</code></pre><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80fa-af81-dc3872da1e88"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-800d-93b9-d6994226f503" class=""><strong>8. Verify Config and Secrets</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80b3-b6f5-c52af7976673" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Misconfigured <strong>ConfigMaps or Secrets</strong> may cause crashes.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80cb-9dcf-ed857824a592" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Check environment variables or mounted volumes.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8040-a503-ec667ca15b8e"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8004-a0f6-c59fcfac1ba9" class=""><strong>9. Examine Liveness/Readiness Probes</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803f-ae1b-efb9fbbe2f68" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Misconfigured probes can cause <strong>restarts even if app is healthy</strong>.</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8055-8fca-f9ee587fbd9b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Adjust <code>initialDelaySeconds</code>, <code>periodSeconds</code>, or paths.</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80b8-9cb7-dc5ba4e033f3"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-8096-af02-e45acec33513" class=""><strong>10. Common Causes of CrashLoopBackOff</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-803d-91ac-d8c0ccc9e3f7" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Application error or misconfiguration</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80ba-9625-cba0bd163f0b" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Incorrect image or entrypoint</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800e-a72b-f49c5601ac78" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Insufficient resources (CPU/memory)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-80e7-aa72-ccb5924f7e79" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Dependency failure (database, network)</li></ul><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8008-8dea-d36da99fa7d2" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">Probe misconfiguration</li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-80f6-b91b-f96fc1808634"/><h3 id="272378cb-b17f-805f-8293-fcc8ce0e7558" class=""><strong>Analogy</strong></h3><ul id="272378cb-b17f-8072-b535-e09b25326bb3" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:disc">CrashLoopBackOff = <strong>trying to start a car that keeps stalling üîÑ</strong><ul id="272378cb-b17f-800f-9c04-e17ca93b09f0" class="bulleted-list"><li style="list-style-type:circle">You check <strong>fuel, engine, ignition, and tires</strong> (logs, resources, config, probes).</li></ul></li></ul><hr id="272378cb-b17f-8028-8f9a-f637fcdeb9c5"/><p id="272378cb-b17f-80e5-b072-efacf0521af8" class="">‚úÖ <strong>Summary Steps</strong></p><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-8032-a007-f7551a3d178b" class="numbered-list" start="1"><li><code>kubectl describe pod</code> ‚Üí check events</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80ad-aa1f-e969961c09f2" class="numbered-list" start="2"><li><code>kubectl logs</code> ‚Üí check container output</li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80d7-8f45-f3b6600717bc" class="numbered-list" start="3"><li>Check <strong>resources, image, command, config, secrets</strong></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80e8-b7c1-e9149f9c6b86" class="numbered-list" start="4"><li>Check <strong>probes</strong></li></ol><ol type="1" id="272378cb-b17f-80dd-8803-e2794a2aadbd" class="numbered-list" start="5"><li>Debug interactively if needed</li></ol></details></li></ul><p id="26b378cb-b17f-8041-b24c-e25e0c07ccfe" class="">
</p></div></article><span class="sans" style="font-size:14px;padding-top:2em"></span></body></html>
